Intention of Imam When Leading Women
Stating the ruling and proof for imam's intention for women followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition on the imam's intention when leading women, explain the proof based on muhadha, and identify the ruling for Jumu'ah and Eid prayers.

Core Idea
The imam's intention to lead women is a condition to prevent invalidity from alignment; it is not required when leading men.

In this passage, we examine why the Hanafi school requires the imam to specifically intend to lead women in prayer. The key reasoning revolves around the concept of muhadha (alignment) and its potential to invalidate the prayer if the imam is not committed to leading them. We will also see how later scholars extended this ruling to Friday and Eid prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? Identify that it is the imam's intention to lead women, and note that it is a condition (shart) for the validity of the women's prayer.
The ruling is not a hukm taklifi but a shart for sahha.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage states the proof: without intention, corruption from muhadha would be necessitated. Identify this as a rational proof (ta'lil) based on preventing harm.
No explicit textual evidence is cited; it is a legal reasoning from consequence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the risk of muhadha leads to the requirement of intention. The imam's intention commits him to avoid alignment, thereby preserving the women's prayer.
Muhadha is a known invalidator in Hanafi fiqh when a woman stands aligned with the imam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and extension
Observe the contrast with men followers: intention is not required for men. Also note that most mashayikh extended this to Jumu'ah and Eid, indicating some earlier difference.
The extension shows the principle's scope was refined by later authorities.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
Determine the operative ruling: intention is required in all prayers including Jumu'ah and Eid. This is the relied-upon position from al-Khabbaziyya and al-Muhit.
Authority_weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونية الرجل الإمامة شرط لصحة اقتداء النساء به؛ لما يلزم من الفساد بالمحاذاة ولا يلزمه بدون التزامه، بخلاف الرجل فإنه لا يلزمه باقتدائه حكم في حقه، فلا يشترط أن ينوي إمامته فلا تصير المرأة داخلة في صلاة الإمام حتى ينوي إمامتها، وأكثر المشايخ على أن نية إمامتهن شرط في الجمعة والعيدين أيضاً لصحة اقتداء المرأة، كما في «الخبازية» و «المحيط».
And the intention of a man to be imam is a condition for the validity of women following him; because corruption from alignment is necessitated and it is not necessitated without his commitment, contrary to a man because no ruling regarding him is necessitated by his following, so he does not require to intend his imamate. So a woman does not enter into the imam's prayer until he intends her imamate. And most of the mashayikh hold that intending their imamate is also a condition in Friday and the two Eid prayers for the validity of a woman's following, as in al-Khabbaziyya and al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage explains a condition for the validity of women following a male imam: the imam must specifically intend to lead women. The reasoning is that without this intention, the woman's prayer risks invalidity due to al-muhadha (alignment) which would occur without the imam's explicit commitment to lead her. This requirement does not apply when men follow a male imam. The text also notes that most later scholars extend this condition to Friday and Eid prayers, meaning the imam must also intend to lead women in those prayers.

Key Terms
نية الإمامة (niyyat al-imama): The imam's specific intention to lead others in prayer, distinguishing him from one praying alone.
المحاذاة (al-muhadha): Alignment of a woman with the imam or men in the same row, which can invalidate the prayer if not avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the imam's intention to lead women required in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because women's prayers are inherently deficient.
B) To prevent invalidity caused by alignment (muhadha) if the imam does not commit to leading them.
C) Because women cannot form their own congregation.
D) Because the imam must announce the prayer aloud.

Key Takeaway
The imam's intention to lead women is a condition (shart) for the validity of women's prayer in Hanafi fiqh, due to the risk of invalidity from alignment (muhadha).

The Imam's Heel and State Relative to the Ma'mum
Ruling with proof for two specific conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions regarding the imam's heel advancement and his state relative to the ma'mum, and apply them to determine the validity of following.

Core Idea
The imam's heel must be ahead and his legal state cannot be inferior to the follower's.

In congregational prayer, the imam's physical position and legal state directly affect the validity of the follower's prayer. This lesson covers two key conditions: the imam's heel must be ahead of the follower's heel, and the imam must not be in a lower legal state (e.g., praying nafl while the follower prays fard). Understanding these ensures the follower's prayer is valid and the congregation is unified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition: heel advancement
The imam's heel must be ahead of the follower's heel. If the follower is taller so his toes are ahead but heel not, it is still valid.
The measure is the heel, not the toes.
2
Identify the second condition: lower state prohibition
The imam must not be in a lower legal state than the follower, e.g., nafl behind fard, or with an excuse (like tayammum) behind one without.
This ensures the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's.
3
Apply the conditions to scenarios
Given a specific congregation, determine if the follower's prayer is valid based on these two conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقدم الإمام بعقبه عن المأموم شرط لصحة اقتدائه، حتى لو كان عقب المقتدي غير متقدم على عقب الإمام، لكن قدمه أطول فيكون أصابعه قدام أصابع إمامه تجوز، كما لو كان المقتدي أطول من إمامه فيسجد أمامه. و) يشترط لصحة الاقتداء (أن لا يكون الإمام أدنى حالاً من المأموم) كأن يكون متنفلاً والمقتدي مفترضاً، أو معذوراً والمقتدي خالياً عنه. (و) يشترط أن لا يكون الإمام مصلياً فرضاً غير فرضه) أي: المأموم كظهر وعصر، وكظهرين من يومين؛ لأن المقتدي مشارك للإمام فلابد من الاتحاد، وذلك بأن يمكنه الدخول في صلاته بنيته صلاة الإمام، فتكون صلاة الإمام متضمنة لصلاة المقتدي، وهو المراد بقوله: ( الإمام ضامن) أي: تتضمن صلاته صلاة المقتدي، وعلى هذا لا يجوز اقتداء الناذر بالناذر؛ لأن المنذور إنما يجب بالتزامه، فلا يظهر الوجوب في حق عدم غيره؛ لعدم ولايته عليه فيكون بمنزلة اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل، إلا إذا نذر عين ما نذره صاحبه، فيصح اقتداء أحدهما بالآخر للاتحاد، ولا يصح اقتداء الناذر بالحالف لأن المنذورة أقوى من المحلوف على فعلها وقلبه يصح كالحالف بالحالف ومصلي ركعتي الطواف بمثله، كالمتنفل بمثله كذا في قاضي خان وخلافه في الخلاصة جعل ركعتي الطواف كالمنذورة مع المنذورة لا تصح خلف مثلها. (و) يشترط أن لا يكون الإمام مقيماً لمسافر، بعد الوقت، في رباعية) لأن فرض المسافر لا يتغير بعد الوقت لانقضاء السبب، كما لا يتغير بنية الإقامة بعده، فكان اقتداء مفترض بمتنفل. (و) يشترط أن لا يكون الإمام مسبوقاً) فلا يصح الاقتداء بالمسبوق إذا قام لقضاء ما سبق به لشبهة اقتدائه حال تحريمته، ولزوم القراءة عليه لشبهة الانفراد.
And the imam's heel being ahead of the ma'mum's heel is a condition for the validity of following; even if the follower's heel is not ahead of the imam's heel but his foot is longer so his toes are ahead of the imam's toes, it is permissible, just as if the follower is taller than the imam and prostrates in front of him. And it is a condition for the validity of following that the imam not be in a lower state than the ma'mum, such as being a supererogatory worshipper while the follower is an obligatory worshipper, or being excused while the follower is free from that excuse. And it is a condition that the imam not be praying a different obligatory prayer than the ma'mum's, such as Zuhr and Asr, or two Zuhr prayers from different days; because the follower shares in the imam's prayer, so unity is necessary, in that it is possible for him to enter his prayer with the intention of the imam's prayer, so the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer, and this is what is meant by 'the imam is a guarantor', i.e., his prayer includes the follower's prayer. On this basis, it is not valid for one who has made a vow (nadhir) to follow another nadhir, because the vowed prayer is only obligatory by his own commitment, so the obligation does not appear regarding another, and thus it is like an obligatory follower following a supererogatory imam, unless he vowed the exact same prayer as his companion, then one may follow the other due to unity. And it is not valid for a nadhir to follow a swearer (halif), because the vowed prayer is stronger than the oath to perform it. And the one praying two rak'ahs of tawaf is like a supererogatory worshipper. And it is a condition that the imam not be a resident leading a traveller after the time in a four-rak'ah prayer, because the traveller's obligatory prayer does not change after the time due to the expiry of the cause; thus it is like an obligatory follower following a supererogatory imam. And it is a condition that the imam not be a masbuq (one who missed some rak'ahs), so it is not valid to follow a masbuq when he stands to make up what he missed, due to the semblance of following during his own opening takbir, and the necessity of recitation upon him resembling being alone.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage details five conditions related to the imam's personal state required for the validity of following: (1) The imam's heel must be ahead of the follower's heel; if the follower is taller and his toes are ahead, it is still permissible. (2) The imam must not be in a lower state, e.g., praying nafl while the follower prays fard, or having a valid excuse (like tayammum) while the follower has none. (3) The imam and follower must be praying the same fard; exceptions are discussed for vows and oaths. (4) A resident imam may not lead a traveller after the time in a 4-rak'ah prayer, because the traveller's fard does not change after time. (5) The imam must not be a masbuq (someone who missed part of the prayer and stands to make it up), as following him in that state is invalid. Each condition is supported by rational reasoning (talil).

Key Terms
عقب (ʻaqib): The heel of the foot; used to measure the imam's relative position ahead of the follower.
أدنى حالاً (adna halan): A lower legal state; e.g., imam praying nafl while follower prays fard, or imam having an excuse like being a person with chronic illness.
إمام ضامن (imam dhamin): The principle that the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer, ensuring unity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of the imam being in a 'lower state' (adna halan) than the ma'mum?
A) The imam is reciting aloud and the ma'mum cannot hear.
B) The imam is praying a fard prayer while the ma'mum is praying nafl.
C) The imam is a traveller (musafir) and the ma'mum is a resident (muqim) after the prayer time.
D) The imam is praying supererogatory (nafl) while the ma'mum is praying obligatory (fard).

Key Takeaway
The imam's heel must be ahead and his legal state must not be lower than the follower's for the follower's prayer to be valid.

Unity of Fard, Residency, and Masbuq Conditions
Ruling with proof for three conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions regarding the unity of obligatory prayer, the resident/traveler distinction after time, and the prohibition of following a masbuq, and apply them to determine the validity of following.

Core Idea
The imam and follower must share the same fard, the resident cannot lead a traveler after time, and the masbuq cannot lead while making up missed rak'ahs.

The previous lesson covered physical positioning and state; this lesson addresses three additional conditions critical for the validity of congregational prayer. The imam and follower must be praying the same obligatory prayer (unity of fard), with specific rulings for vowed prayers and tawaf. A resident imam cannot lead a traveler after the prayer time has entered for a 4-rak'ah prayer. Finally, a masbuq (one who joined late) cannot lead others while making up missed rak'ahs. Understanding these ensures the congregation's prayer is valid and unified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of unity of fard
The imam and follower must be praying the same obligatory prayer. The principle is 'imam dhamin' – the imam's prayer must encompass the follower's.
Includes exceptions for vowed prayers and tawaf.
2
Understand the resident/traveler condition
A resident imam cannot lead a traveler after the time of a 4-rak'ah prayer because the traveler's obligation changes (qasr) and cannot be encompassed.
This applies when the traveler intends to pray qasr.
3
Understand the masbuq condition
A masbuq (one who missed some rak'ahs) cannot be imam for others when he stands to complete his prayer because his intention is partly separate.
The follower would be following an incomplete intention.
4
Apply the conditions to scenarios
Given a specific congregation, determine if the follower's prayer is valid based on these three conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the imam's heel being ahead of the ma'mum's heel is a condition for the validity of following; even if the follower's heel is not ahead of the imam's heel but his foot is longer so his toes are ahead of the imam's toes, it is permissible, just as if the follower is taller than the imam and prostrates in front of him. Commentary
This passage details five conditions related to the imam's personal state required for the validity of following: (1) The imam's heel must be ahead of the follower's heel; if the follower is taller and his toes are ahead, it is still permissible. (2) The imam must not be in a lower state, e.g., praying nafl while the follower prays fard, or having a valid excuse (like tayammum) while the follower has none. (3) The imam and follower must be praying the same fard; exceptions are discussed for vows and oaths. (4) A resident imam may not lead a traveller after the time in a 4-rak'ah prayer, because the traveller's fard does not change after time. (5) The imam must not be a masbuq (someone who missed part of the prayer and stands to make it up), as following him in that state is invalid. Each condition is supported by rational reasoning (talil).

Key Terms
إمام ضامن (imam dhamin): The principle that the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer, ensuring unity.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joined the congregation late and has missed one or more rak'ahs of the prayer.
ناذر (nadhir): One who has made a vow (nadhr) to perform a specific prayer.
حالف (halif): One who swears an oath (halif) to perform a prayer.
ركعتي الطواف (rak'atay al-tawaf): The two rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer performed after completing tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid scenario for following the imam according to this lesson?
A) A follower prays Asr behind an imam praying Dhuhr.
B) A traveler follows a resident imam for Dhuhr after the time of Dhuhr has begun.
C) A masbuq who missed one rak'ah stands up to complete and another person follows him.
D) Two individuals who have vowed the exact same prayer follow each other.

Key Takeaway
For valid congregational prayer, the imam and follower must share the same fard obligation, the resident-traveler distinction after time must be observed, and the masbuq cannot lead while completing missed rak'ahs.

8 min
Row of Women Between Imam and Ma'mum
Ruling on invalidity caused by a row of women separating imam and ma'mum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the invalidity caused by a row of women separating the imam and ma'mum, apply the rule to different numbers of women, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A row of women between imam and ma'mum invalidates the prayer of those behind, per hadith of Umar (ra).

In congregational prayer, proper formation is essential. The Hanafi school teaches that a row of women between the imam and male followers can break the connection. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its scriptural proof, and the practical consequences based on the number of women rows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the condition: no row of women should separate the imam from male ma'mums. The verdict: if such separation occurs, the prayer of those behind is invalid (la salata lahu).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated from Umar (ra) as both mawquf and marfu', cited in al-Bada'i'. The text equates a row of women with a river or road as a barrier.
Hadith is ahad, so thubut is zanni; dalala is zanni due to ikhtilaf in understanding.
3
Trace wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'la salata lahu' is an explicit negation of validity. The conjunction 'aw' (or) shows that a row of women is a separate invalidating factor, just like a river or road.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is disagreement on how many rows are invalidated. One view: three women rows invalidate three rows behind; another view: all rows behind are invalid.
The text declares 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' for the first view.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
If rows of women are 3, the next 3 male rows are invalid; beyond that, prayer is valid. If 2 rows, only 2 rows behind are invalid. If one woman aligns (muhadhiyah), only those directly opposite and behind are affected.
These details come from the text's expansion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن لا يفصل بين الإمام والمأموم صف من النساء؛ لما روي عن عمر موقوفاً ومرفوعاً إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «من كان بينه وبين الإمام نهر أو طريق أو صف من النساء فلا صلاة له» كما في البدائع. فإن كن ثلاثاً فسدت صلاة ثلاثة خلفهن من كل صف إلى آخر الصفوف وعليه الفتوى، وجاز اقتداء الباقي وقيل: الثلاث صف مانع من صحة الاقتداء لمن خلف صفهن جميعاً، وإن كانتا ثنتين فسدت صلاة اثنين خلفهما فقط، وإن كانت واحدة في الصف محاذية فسدت صلاة من حاذته عن يمينها ويسارها وآخر خلفها.
And that no row of women separate between the imam and the ma'mum; because it is narrated from Umar, both as a stop and as a raise to the Prophet ﷺ, that he said: 'Whoever has between him and the imam a river, or a road, or a row of women, then no prayer is valid for him,' as in al-Bada'i. If they are three, the prayer of three behind them from each row to the end of the rows is invalidated, and upon this is the fatwa, and the following of the rest is valid. It is said: three rows prevent the validity of following for all behind their rows. If they are two, the prayer of two behind them only is invalidated. If one woman is in the row aligned, the prayer of those aligned to her right and left and the one directly behind her is invalidated.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition that no row of women should separate the imam from the male ma'mums. The primary proof is a hadith narrated from Umar (and raised to the Prophet) stating that a row of women, like a river or road, invalidates the prayer of those behind. The text then details the effect based on the number of women: if there are three women rows, the prayer of the next three rows behind them is invalidated (this is the relied-upon view), but others beyond those three rows are valid. Some say that three rows invalidate all rows behind them. For two women rows, only two rows behind them are invalid. For one woman aligned with a man, it invalidates those directly facing her on right, left, and the one exactly behind her.

Key Terms
صف من النساء (saff min al-nisa'): A continuous row of women praying, which if placed between the imam and male ma'mums, invalidates the prayer of those behind.
محاذية (muhadhiyah): A woman aligned directly opposite a man in the same row, causing invalidation for those facing her sides and behind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the row directly behind the women.

C) Three rows behind the women are invalidated.
D) Only the imam's prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A row of women between the imam and male followers invalidates the prayer of those behind; the number of affected rows depends on the women rows: three women rows affect three male rows (mufta bihi).

River and Road as Barriers Between Imam and Ma'mum
Ruling on when a river or road separates imam and ma'mum and related distance rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions regarding physical barriers between imam and ma'mum and apply them to different prayer settings.

Core Idea
A river wide enough for a boat or a road wide enough for a cart is a barrier that invalidates following; but in an open desert, two rows count, while in a mosque or Eid ground, barriers do not invalidate.

In congregational prayer, the follower must be close enough to follow the imam's actions. Physical barriers like wide rivers, roads, or large open spaces can break this connection. The Hanafi school provides specific measures to determine when a barrier is too large. This passage from Nur al-Idah explains those measures for rivers, roads, deserts, and prayer grounds.

Guided Path
1
State the general condition
Recognize that validity of following requires proximity; extreme distance or a barrier invalidates the connection.
This is a shart (condition) for the follower's prayer.
2
Identify barrier criteria for river and road
For a river, the standard is whether a small boat (zawraq) can pass; for a road, whether a cart (ajala) can pass. These indicate significant width.
Alternative view: strong man's leap, but the relied-upon is the boat/cart criterion.
3
Apply the desert rule
In a flat open desert (flaat), the barrier is a space that can fit two rows of worshippers. The mufta bihi is two rows.
Some say any space without continuous rows; but the text settles on two rows.
4
Distinguish Eid and funeral grounds
In the Eid prayer ground, even a large barrier does not invalidate. For a funeral prayer area, it is treated like a mosque, where barriers do not invalidate.
This shows the rule is context-dependent.
5
Note the exceptional case
Very large mosques (e.g., ancient Khwarazm) may have disagreement due to size, but the general rule for mosques is no barrier invalidates.
This exception confirms the rule for normal mosques.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يشترط (أن لا يفصل بينهما (نهر يمر فيه الزَّوْرَق في الصحيح، والزورق نوع من السفن الصغار، (ولا طـريـق تـمـر فيـه العَجَلَةُ ) وليس فيها صفوف متصلة، لأن غاية البعد مانع من صحة الاقتداء، فجعل الحد الفاصل بين البعد والقرب ما ذكر، وقيل : ما يجتازه الرجل القوي بوثبة، والمانع من الاقتداء في الفلاة فاصل يسع فيه صفين على المفتى به كما في «التجنيس والمزيد والفاصل في مصلى العيد لا يمنع وإن کثر، واختلف في المتخذ لصلاة الجنازة. وفي «النوازل: جعله كالمسجد، والمسجد وإن كبر لا يمنع الفاصل، إلا في الجامع القديم بخوارزم فإن ربعـه كـان على أربعة آلاف أسطوانة، وجامع القدس الشريف أعني: ما يشتمل على المساجد الثلاثة الأقصى والصخرا والبيضا، كذا في البزازية».
And it is a condition that there not separate between them a river in which a small boat (zawraq) passes—in the correct view; and a road in which a cart (ajala) passes, and there are no continuous rows in it, because extreme distance prevents the validity of following; so the separating limit between distance and proximity is made as mentioned. And it is said: what a strong man can cross with a leap. And the barrier preventing following in a desert is a space that accommodates two rows, according to the fatwa, as in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid. The barrier in the Eid prayer ground does not prevent even if large. And there is disagreement on a place made for funeral prayer. In al-Nawazil: it is made like a mosque, and the mosque, even if large, does not prevent the barrier, except in the ancient Friday mosque of Khwarazm, where one quarter had four thousand columns; and the Masjid al-Aqsa in Jerusalem, which includes the three mosques: al-Aqsa, the Rock, and the White Mosque, as in al-Bazzaziyya.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage addresses physical barriers between imam and ma'mum. A river wide enough for a small boat or a road wide enough for a cart are barriers that invalidate following, as they represent excessive distance. Alternative opinions define it as the distance a strong man can leap. In a desert (flaat), the barrier is a space that can fit two rows. For the Eid prayer ground, even a large barrier does not prevent validity. For a funeral prayer area, it is treated like a mosque, where barriers do not invalidate, except in very large mosques like the ancient Khwarazm mosque where the size caused disagreement. The ruling is based on maintaining knowledge of the imam's actions.

Key Terms
زورق (zawraq): A small boat; used as a measure for a river that constitutes a barrier.
عجلة (ajala): A cart pulled by an animal; used as a measure for a road that is a barrier.
فلاة (falah): A desert or open land without buildings; specific rules apply for barriers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The distance a strong man can leap.
B) A space that can fit two rows.
C) Any space without continuous rows.
D) The distance of a river with a boat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses objective measures (boat, cart, two rows) to determine when a barrier invalidates following; these criteria ensure practicality and consistency.

Wall as Barrier Between Imam and Ma'mum
Ruling on when a wall separates imam and ma'mum based on knowledge of imam's actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid following through a wall and apply it to scenarios involving sight or hearing.

Core Idea
Following an imam through a wall is valid if you can see or hear him; a wall alone does not invalidate.

This passage addresses a common situation in congregational prayer: when a wall separates the ma'mum from the imam. The key condition is not the presence of the wall itself, but whether the ma'mum has knowledge of the imam's movements. If the ma'mum can see or hear the imam (e.g., the takbir), the following is valid, even if physical access is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The text states that a large wall is problematic only if it obscures knowledge of the imam's movements.
The condition is knowledge, not absence of a wall.
2
Locate the criterion
Knowledge can be through hearing or sight. If either is present, the following is valid.
Even if the ma'mum cannot reach the imam, the prayer is valid.
3
Trace the proof
The hadith of the Prophet praying in 'Aisha's room while people in the mosque followed him shows that a wall did not prevent validity.
The hadith is ahad but accepted.
4
Apply to scenarios
The text applies the ruling to roofs adjacent to mosques and houses next to mosques, as long as the imam's movements are known.
The muballigh (repeater) can also convey the takbir.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi choice
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani selected this as the correct view in the school.
References: al-Tajnis and al-Mazid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يشترط أن لا بفصل بينهما (حَائِط) كبير (يَشْتَبِه) معه العلم بانتقالات الإمام فإنْ لم يَشتَبِه) العلم بانتقالات الإمام ( لسماع، أو رؤيةٍ) ولو لم يمكن الوصول إليه (صح الاقتداء) به ( في الصحيح)، وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة الحلواني، لما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: « كان يصلي في حجرة عائشة والناس في المسجد يصلون بصلاته » (۳) وعلى هذا الاقتداء في الأماكن المتصلة، بالمسجد الحرام وأبوابها من خارجه صحيح إذا لم يشتبه حال الإمام بسماع أو رؤية، ولم يتخلل إلا الجدار، كما ذكر شمس الأئمة: رجل صلى على سطح بيته وسطح بيته متصل بالمسجد، أنه يجوز لأن سطح بيته إذا كان متصلاً بالمسجد، لا يكون أشدّ حالاً من منزل يكون بجنب المسجد، وبينه وبين المسجد حائط، ولو صلى في مثل هذا المنزل مقتدياً بإمام في المسجد، وهو يسمع التكبير من الإمام، أو من المكبر تجوز صلاته، كذا في التجنيس والمزيد.
And it is a condition that there not separate between them a large wall that obscures knowledge of the imam's movements. But if the knowledge of the imam's movements is not obscure due to hearing or sight, even if access is impossible, then following him is valid in the correct view. This is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, based on the narration that the Prophet ﷺ prayed in 'Aisha's room while the people in the mosque prayed following his prayer. And on this basis, following in places connected to the Masjid al-Haram and its doors from outside is valid if the imam's state is not obscure due to hearing or sight, and only the wall intervenes. As Shams al-A'imma mentioned: a man prayed on the roof of his house and his roof was connected to the mosque; it is permissible because his roof, if connected to the mosque, is not more severe than a house adjacent to the mosque with a wall between; and if one prays in such a house following an imam in the mosque while hearing the takbir from the imam or from the muballigh, his prayer is valid, as in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage discusses a large wall as a potential barrier. The key is whether the ma'mum can still know the imam's movements through hearing (e.g., takbir) or sight. If not, the following is invalid. However, if the wall does not obstruct knowledge, the prayer is valid, even if the ma'mum cannot physically reach the imam. This is based on the hadith of the Prophet praying in 'Aisha's room while people in the mosque followed him. The same ruling applies to praying on a roof connected to the mosque or in a house next to the mosque, provided the ma'mum can hear the takbir. This is the correct view in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حائط كبير (ha'it kabir): A large wall that may obscure knowledge of the imam's actions; its size is relevant to whether it prevents following.
مكبر (mukabbir): A person who repeats the imam's takbir for those far away; his transmission can make following valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The imam must raise his voice so the ma'mum can hear every word.

Key Takeaway
A wall separating imam and ma'mum does not invalidate the prayer if the ma'mum can see or hear the imam's actions.

Conditions for Valid Iqtida': Ships and Follower's Knowledge
Lists two conditions for valid iqtida' with detailed sub-rulings and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid iqtida' (connection of place and absence of knowledge of imam's invalidating act) and apply the Hanafi tarjih when madhhab differences arise.

Core Idea
The follower's prayer behind an imam is built on the follower's own ijtihad, not the imam's.

Prayer behind an imam (iqtida') is a core act of worship that requires specific conditions for validity. This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah outlines two critical conditions: physical unity of place and the follower's knowledge of the imam's ritual purity. We will examine each condition in detail, including the qiyas that connects ships to animals and the substantial intra-Hanafi discussion on how to handle situations where the follower knows the imam has done something invalidating in the follower's madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the physical connection condition
Locate the first condition: the follower must not be in a separate, unconnected ship from the imam. Understand that this is a condition (shart) for valid iqtida', not a pillar or obligation.
The text uses the term 'muqtarinah' (connected) – a key technical term.
2
Apply the qiyas: ships as animals, water as a barrier
The text analogizes separate ships to separate animals (like two horses). The intervening water is like a river that breaks the connection. If ships are tied together, the connection is restored virtually.
This is a clear example of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Identify the knowledge condition
Find the second condition: the follower must not know, according to his own madhhab (za'm al-ma'mum), that the imam has done something that invalidates prayer, such as passing blood or vomiting, without having renewed wudu afterward.
Note the phrase 'fi za'm al-ma'mum' – the follower's own conviction, not the imam's.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the knowledge condition
The text presents a scenario: the follower knows something that invalidates prayer in the imam's madhhab (e.g., touching) but the imam is unaware. The majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) permit following; al-Hinduwani rejects it. Understand the reasoning: the follower considers the imam's prayer valid in his own view, so his own prayer is valid.
The tarjih is given: the majority view is the soundest (al-asahh) and is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن لا يكون في سفينة والإمام في أخرى، غير مُقترنة بها. وأن لا يعلم المقتدي من حال إِمامِهِ مُفسِداً في زَعْمِ المأموم، كخروج دَمٍ، أَوْ قَيْءٍ، لم يُعِدْ بَعدَهُ وُضُوءَهُ. وصح اقتداء: متوضئ بمتيمم، وغاسل بماسح . المكان، فلو كانا على دابة واحدة صح الاقتداء لاتحاد المكان، وسيأتي حكم الصلاة على الدابة). (و) يشترط أن لا يكونَ) المقتدي ( في سفينة، والإمام في سفينة (أخرى، غير مقترنة بها) لأنهما كالدابتين، وإذا اقترنتا صح للاتحاد الحكمي، وإذا انفصلتا لم يجز؛ لأن تخلـل مـا بينهما بمنزلة النهر، وذلك يمنع صحة الاقتداء، ومن وقف على أطلال السفينة، واقتدى بالإمام في السفينة صح اقتداؤه، إلا أن يكون أمام الإمام؛ لأن السفينة كالبيت، واقتداء الواقف على السطح بمن هو في البيت صحيح، إذا لم يكن أمام الإمام ولا يخفى عليه حاله كذا هذا. (وَ) الرابع عشر: يشترط أن لا يعلم المقتدي من حال إمامه المخالف لمذهبه ( مُفسِداً في زَعْمِ المأموم: كخروج دم) سائل (أو قي) يملأ الفم، ويتيقن أنه لم يُعِدْ بَعدَهُ وُضُوءَهُ) فلو غاب بعدما شاهد منه ذلك بقدر ما يعيد الوضوء ولم يعلم حاله فالصحيح جواز الاقتداء مع الكراهة، كما لو جهل حاله بالمرة فلم يعلم منه شيئاً، وأما إذا كان يعلم منه أنه لا يحتاط في مواضع الخلاف فلا . يصح الاقتداء، سواء علم حاله في ما يقتدي به فيه أو لا انتهى. وإن علم أنه يحتاط في مواضع الخلاف فإنه بـ يصح على الأصح، ويكره كما في ( المجتبى». وقال في شرح الديري»: لا يكره إذا علم منه الاحتياط في مذهب الحنفي انتهى، وأما إذا علم المقتدي من الإمام ما يفسد الصلاة على زعم الإمـام كـمـس المرأة، أو الذكر، والإمام لا يدري بذلك، فإنه يجوز اقتداؤه به على قول الأكثر. وقال بعضهم: لا يجوز، منهم الهندواني؛ لأن الإمام يرى بطلان هذه الصلاة فتبطل صلاة المقتدي تبعاً له، وجه الأول: وهو الأصح أن المقتدي يرى جواز صلاة إمامه، والمعتبر في حقه رأي نفسه، فوجب القول بجوازها، كما في « التبيين»، و«الفتح»، وإنما قيد بقوله : والإمام لا يدري بذلك ليكون جازماً بالنية؛ لأنه إن علم به وهو على اعتقاد مذهبه صار كالمتلاعب ولا نية له.
And that the follower not be in a ship while the imam is in another ship that is not connected to it. And that the follower not know from the state of his imam something that is invalidating in the follower's view, like blood or vomit, after which he did not repeat his ablution. And valid is the following of a person with wudu behind a person with tayammum, and a person washing (with water) behind a person wiping (over boots). The place: if both are on one animal, following is valid due to unity of place, and the ruling of prayer on an animal will come. And it is a condition that the follower not be in a ship while the imam is in another ship not connected to it; because they are like two animals. When they are connected, it is valid due to virtual unity, and when separated, it is not valid because the space between them is like a river, and that prevents validity of following. Whoever stands on the beach of the ship and follows the imam in the ship, his following is valid, unless he is in front of the imam; because the ship is like a house, and the following of one standing on the roof of one in the house is valid if he is not in front of the imam and his state is not hidden. And the fourteenth condition: that the follower not know from the state of his imam who differs from his madhhab something invalidating in the follower's view: like flowing blood or vomit that fills the mouth, and he is certain that he did not repeat his ablution after it. If he disappeared after witnessing that from him for the time to repeat ablution and he does not know his state, the sound opinion is permissibility of following with dislike, just as if he completely ignored his state. And if he knows that he does not exercise caution in matters of disagreement, following is not valid, whether he knows his state in what he is following him in or not. And if he knows that he exercises caution in matters of disagreement, then it is valid according to the soundest view, with dislike as in al-Mujtaba. And in Sharh al-Dayri: there is no dislike if he knows his caution in the Hanafi madhhab. And if the follower knows of the imam something that invalidates prayer in the imam's view, like touching a woman or the penis, and the imam is unaware of that, then his following him is permissible according to the majority. Some say it is not permissible, among them al-Hinduwani, because the imam considers his prayer invalid, so the follower's prayer becomes invalid in consequence. The first view is the soundest: the follower considers his imam's prayer permissible, and what matters in his case is his own opinion, so it must be said permissible, as in al-Tabyin and al-Fath. He restricted it by saying 'the imam is unaware of that' in order to be certain of intention, because if he knows it while adhering to his madhhab, he becomes like one playing, and he has no intention.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage discusses two conditions for the validity of following the imam in prayer. The first condition concerns the physical proximity between the follower and the imam: they should not be in separate, unconnected ships, as the intervening space like water is akin to a river that breaks the connection, similar to being on two separate animals. However, if the ships are connected (e.g., tied together), it is considered one place. The second condition is more detailed: the follower must not know that the imam has done something that, in the follower's own madhhab, would invalidate his prayer, such as passing wind without renewing wudu. If the follower witnesses such an act and is certain the imam did not rectify it, then following is invalid. But if the follower only suspects or the imam disappeared without known rectification, it is permissible with dislike. A nuance arises when the follower knows the imam is careless in matters of khilaf (differences between madhhabs): then following is invalid because the imam's prayer is likely invalid in the imam's own view. If the imam is known to be cautious, following is valid but disliked, unless the imam is known to follow Hanafi caution then no dislike. Another sub-case: if the follower knows something that invalidates the prayer in the imam's madhhab (e.g., touching one's own private parts) but the imam is unaware, the majority permit following, because the follower considers the imam's prayer valid based on his own madhhab. This is the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtidā’): Following an imam in prayer, with the follower intending to be led.
زعم المأموم (za‘m al-ma’mūm): The follower's belief or ijtihad regarding what invalidates prayer.
مقترنة (muqtarinah): Connected, as ships tied together.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Hanafi follower knows that his Shafi'i imam touched his own skin (which nullifies wudu in Shafi'i) but the imam is unaware, is the follower's prayer valid?
A) Valid, because the follower's own madhhab does not consider touch as nullifying.
B) Invalid, because the imam's prayer is invalid.
C) Valid only if the imam also follows Hanafi.
D) Invalid, because the follower knew.

Key Takeaway
For valid iqtida', physical unity of place is required, and the follower must not know of an invalidating act in his own view from the imam; if the act is invalid only in the imam's madhhab, the majority permits following based on the follower's ijtihad.

Valid Types of Leadership in Prayer: Six Scenarios and Disputes
Lists permissible scenarios of leading and following with proofs and intra-madhhab disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six permissible scenarios of iqtida' and apply the rule that invalidity from the start requires the follower to repeat.

Core Idea
Valid iqtida' requires building the weak on the strong; a missing condition in the imam voids the follower's prayer.

This lesson covers when a follower's prayer remains valid even if the imam's state differs. You will learn six specific scenarios and the critical principle that if the imam's prayer was invalid from the start, the follower must repeat. Pay attention to the intra-Hanafi disputes, especially regarding tayammum and the hunchback.

Guided Path
1
Identify each scenario and its rationale
Read through the six scenarios: wudu behind tayammum, washing behind wiping, standing behind sitting, hunchback, gesturing behind gesturing, supererogatory behind obligatory. For each, note the shared rationale – the follower's state is weaker or equal, so leading is permissible.
The key principle is building the weak on the strong.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi disputes
Focus on two disputes: (1) wudu follower behind tayammum imam – valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, invalid according to Imam Muhammad. (2) Hunchback imam when hunch reaches bowing level – valid according to the two, invalid according to Muhammad. Later scholars differ on the hunchback.
The dispute on tayammum hinges on whether the substitution is between means or purifications.
3
Apply the rule on invalidity
The passage concludes: if the imam's prayer is invalid from the start (due to missing condition or pillar), the follower must repeat. But if a nullifier occurs later (e.g., apostasy), the follower does not repeat.
This distinguishes between initial deficiency and later nullification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح اقتداء: متوضئ بمتيمم) عندهما، وقال محمد: لا يصح، والخلاف مبني على أن الخلفية بين الآلتين وهما التراب والماء أو الطهارتين، بین الآلتين، وظاهر النص (۳) يدل عليه، فاستوى الطهارتان وعند :محمد بين وهما التيمم والوضوء، فيصير بناء القوي على الضعيف، وهو لا يجوز، ولا خلاف في صحة الاقتداء بالمتيمم في صلاة الجنازة. (و) صح اقتداء ( غاسل بماسح ) (۳) على خف أو جبيرة أو خرقة قرحة لا يسيل منها شيء)، (و) صح اقتداء (قائم بقاعد)؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( صلَّى الظَّهر يوم السبتِ أو الأَحَدِ في مرضِ مَوْتِهِ جَالِسًا، والنَّاسِ خَلْفَهُ قِيَامَاً، وهي آخرُ صلاةٍ صَلَاهَا إِمَامَاً وَصَلَّى خَلْفَ أَبِي بَكْرِ الرَّكْعَةَ الثَّانِيَةَ صبحَ يومِ الاثْنَينِ مَأْمُومَاً ثُمَّ أتمَّ لِنَفْسِهِ » ( ذكره البيهقي في ( المعرفة». (وَ) صح الاقتداء (بأحْدَبَ) لم يبلغ حدبه حد الركوع اتفاقاً على الأصح، واختلفوا فيما إذا بلغ، ففي المجتبى » : يجوز عندهما، وبه أخذ عامة العلماء وفي شرح المنية : هو الأصح بمنزلة الاقتداء بالقاعد، لأن القيام استواء النصفين وقد وجد استواء نصفه الأسفل، فيجوز عندهما ولا يجوز عند محمد، قال الزيلعي وفي ( الظهيرية » : هو الأصح انتهى. فقد اختلف التصحيح انتهى. وفي الذخيرة» و«الخلاصة » : يوم الأحدب القائم كما يؤم القاعد القائم انتهى، فقد أطلق الجواز. وقال في « البزازية » : قال الفقيه أبو الليث لا يجوز إمامة الأحدب. أما في حق نفسه إن بلغت حدوبتـه الركوع ينخفض للركوع قليلاً؛ ليحصل الفرق بين القيام والركوع انتهى، فقد أطلق عـدم جــواز الاقتداء به، وعلمت ما فيه من اختلاف التصحيح. (و) صح اقتداء (موم بمثله) بأن كانا قاعدين، أو مضطجعين، أو المأموم مضطجعاً والإمام قاعداً؛ لقوة حاله لا عكسه. (وَ) صح اقتداء (متنفّـل بمُقْتَرِض)؛ لأنه بناء الضعيف على القوي وللقراءة وإن كانت فرضاً في الأخريين من النفل، نفلاً في الفرض، لكن إنما تكون فرضاً إذا كان مصلي النفل منفرداً، أما إذا كان مقتدياً فلا، لأنها محظورة كذا في ( العناية». أو لأنه بالاقتداء صار تبعاً للإمام في القراءة، فكانت نـفــلاً في حقه كإمامه (وإن ظهر بطلان صلاة إمامِهِ ) بفوات شرط أو ركن (أعَادَ) لزوماً يعني: افترض عليه الإتيان بالفرض، وليس المراد الإعادة الجابرة لنقص في المؤدى، لأن الاقتداء بناء، والبناء على المعدوم محال، وتقدم ما إذا أخبر بأنه صلى مرة بغير طهارة، وقيدنا ظهور البطلان بفوات شرط أو ركــن، إشارة إلى أنه لو طرأ المفسد لا يعيد المقتدي صلاته، كما لو ارتد الإمام (۳) أو سعى إلى الجمعة بعـدمــا صـلـي
And valid is the following: of one with wudu behind one with tayammum – according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Muhammad said it is not valid. The disagreement is based on whether the substitution is between the two means (water and soil) or between the two purifications. The apparent text (Quran) indicates the former, so the two purifications are equal. According to Muhammad, it is between the two purifications, so it is building the strong upon the weak, which is not allowed. There is no disagreement about validity of following the one with tayammum in the funeral prayer. And valid is the following of one washing (with water) behind one wiping over a boot or a bandage or a wound cloth from which nothing seeps. And valid is the following of one standing behind one sitting, because the Prophet ﷺ prayed Zuhr on Saturday or Sunday in his illness sitting, and the people behind him were standing, and it was the last prayer he led as imam; and he prayed behind Abu Bakr the second rak‘ah of Fajr on Monday as a follower, then completed for himself. (Narrated by al-Bayhaqi in al-Ma‘rifah). And valid is following a hunchback whose hunch does not reach the limit of bowing, unanimously on the soundest view. They disagreed if it does reach. In al-Mujtaba: it is valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the majority of scholars took this. In Sharh al-Munya: it is the soundest, like following one sitting, because standing means the straightness of the two halves, and the lower half is straight, so it is valid according to the two, but not according to Muhammad. Al-Zayla‘i said: in al-Zahiriyyah, it is the soundest. So the tashih (correction) differs. In al-Dhakhirah and al-Khulasah: the hunchback who stands is like one who leads a sitting person, so permission is absolute. In al-Bazzaziyyah: al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said that the imamate of a hunchback is not allowed; as for himself, if his hunch reaches bowing, he lowers slightly for bowing to distinguish between standing and bowing. So absolute impermissibility is given, and you know the difference in correction. And valid is following of one moving (in gestures) by one like him, whether both are sitting, or lying down, or the follower is lying down and the imam is sitting, because of the strength of his state, not the reverse. And valid is following of one performing supererogatory prayer behind one performing obligatory prayer, because it is building the weak upon the strong; and for recitation, even if it is obligatory in the last two rak‘ahs of supererogatory, it is supererogatory in obligatory, but it is only obligatory if the one praying supererogatory alone; if he is following, it is not because it is prohibited (as in al-‘Inayah). Or because by following he becomes a follower of the imam in recitation, so it is supererogatory in his right like his imam. And if the invalidity of his imam's prayer becomes apparent (due to loss of a condition or pillar), he repeats necessarily, meaning he must perform the obligatory prayer; the intended meaning is not the compensatory repetition for a deficiency in the performed prayer, because following is building, and building on nothing is impossible. And it was previously stated when he informed that he prayed once without purification. We restricted the appearance of invalidity to loss of a condition or pillar to indicate that if a nullifier occurs, the follower does not repeat his prayer, as when the imam apostatizes or goes to Friday prayer after having prayed.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage enumerates several scenarios where following an imam is valid despite differences in ritual state. (1) A person with wudu may follow one with tayammum according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, but the majority view is validity, as both are purifications (the Quran recognizes tayammum as a substitute). For funeral prayer, it's unanimous. (2) One who washes with water may follow one who wipes over boots, bandages, or wound cloths (unless seepage). (3) A standing person may follow a sitting imam, proven by the Prophet's practice in his final illness. (4) Following a hunchback is valid if his hunch does not reach bowing level; there is a dispute among later Hanafis when it does, with some permitting (like the two) and others prohibiting (Muhammad and Abu al-Layth). (5) A person making gestures (e.g., due to illness) may follow another similarly, provided the follower is not in a stronger state. (6) One performing supererogatory prayer may follow one praying obligatory, because the supererogatory is weaker; the recitation in supererogatory becomes supererogatory for the follower. Finally, if the imam's prayer becomes invalid due to a missing condition or pillar (e.g., without wudu), the follower must repeat his own prayer, because the building is on nothing. However, if the invalidity is due to a nullifier that occurs after (e.g., apostasy), the follower does not repeat.

Key Terms
أحدب (ahdab): A person with a hunched back, affecting his ability to stand straight.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One performing supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
بطلان (buṭlān): Invalidation of prayer due to missing a condition or pillar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person with wudu follows an imam who has performed tayammum (and both are valid in their own right), what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Valid according to all Hanafis.
B) Invalid according to Muhammad, valid according to Abu Yusuf and the majority Hanafis.
C) Invalid in all cases.
D) Valid only for funeral prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows wide flexibility in iqtida' as long as the follower's state is weaker than the imam's, but a fundamentally invalid imam ruins the follower's prayer.

Valid Following of a Sitting Imam by a Standing Person
Ruling on validity of standing follower behind sitting imam with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a standing person following a sitting imam and identify the hadith proof used.

Core Idea
A standing follower behind a sitting imam is valid; the Prophet himself did so during his final illness.

This ruling addresses a common question: can a physically able person stand behind an imam who is sitting due to illness? The Hanafi school, relying on the Prophet's own practice, affirms its validity. Here we examine the proof and the conditions of this rule.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the act (stander following a sitter) and the ruling (sahih, i.e., valid).
The passage begins with 'wa saḥḥa iqtidā'u qā'im bi qā'id'.
2
Identify the dalil
Locate the proof cited: the hadith of the Prophet praying while sitting with standing followers during his death illness.
The hadith is recorded by al-Bayhaqi in al-Ma'rifah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates permissibility (ibāḥah) for the ummah unless there is evidence of obligation or prohibition.
Since the Prophet led the prayer while sitting and the companions stood, it establishes the validity of such following.
4
Confirm the authority level
Note that this ruling is from the ẓāhir al-riwāyah and is agreed upon within the madhhab.
The text does not mention any ikhtilāf among the Hanafi imams.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a mosque where the imam falls ill during prayer and sits. The congregation may continue standing, and their prayer remains valid.
This ruling applies regardless of whether the imam's excuse is temporary or permanent.

The hadith also mentions that the Prophet later followed Abu Bakr in prayer, but that part is additional context. The ruling is based on this clear precedent, and it is accepted across the madhhab.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtidā'): Following the imam in prayer by the ma'mum.
قائم بقاعد (qā'im bi qā'id): A standing person following a sitting person as imam.

Valid Following of a Hunchbacked Imam: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on definition of standing for imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions regarding the validity of following a hunchbacked imam and explain the basis of the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
When a hunchbacked imam's hump reaches bowing level, Hanafi scholars differ on whether his standing is valid for imamate.

A hunchback (ahdab) has a curved spine causing his upper body to bend forward. For prayer leadership, the key issue is whether his bent posture constitutes valid qiyam (standing). This passage explores an intra-Hanafi dispute about extreme hunchbacks whose hump reaches the level of ruku'. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi definition of standing and its legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed case
When the hump does NOT reach the level of bowing, all Hanafi scholars agree that following such an imam is valid.
This is the default ruling.
2
Locate the point of dispute
When the hump reaches the level of bowing, the scholars differ. Some say the imam is still considered standing because his lower half is straight; others say he is not standing because his posture resembles ruku'.
The dispute hinges on the definition of qiyam.
3
Analyze the permitting position
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (or Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, depending on reading), it is permissible. Their proof: standing is defined as straightness of the two halves (upper and lower). Since the lower half is straight, he is standing. This is analogous to a sitting person leading a standing person – both are valid.
The key proof is the analogy with a sitting imam.
4
Analyze the prohibiting position
Imam Muhammad prohibits it because the hump reaching bowing level makes the imam's posture effectively bowed, so he is not truly standing. His lower half alone is insufficient for qiyam.
Muhammad focuses on the visual resemblance to ruku'.
5
Determine the thamarah and tarjih
The practical consequence: if the imamate is valid, prayers behind him are accepted; if invalid, they must be repeated. The passage shows no clear tarjih; later scholars like Abu al-Layth lean toward prohibition, while others permit.
No single mufta bihi is established in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) صح الاقتداء (بأحْدَبَ) لم يبلغ حدبه حد الركوع اتفاقاً على الأصح، واختلفوا فيما إذا بلغ، ففي المجتبى » : يجوز عندهما، وبه أخذ عامة العلماء وفي شرح المنية : هو الأصح بمنزلة الاقتداء بالقاعد، لأن القيام استواء النصفين وقد وجد استواء نصفه الأسفل، فيجوز عندهما ولا يجوز عند محمد، قال الزيلعي وفي ( الظهيرية » : هو الأصح انتهى. فقد اختلف التصحيح انتهى. وفي الذخيرة» و«الخلاصة » : يوم الأحدب القائم كما يؤم القاعد القائم انتهى، فقد أطلق الجواز. وقال في « البزازية » : قال الفقيه أبو الليث لا يجوز إمامة الأحدب. أما في حق نفسه إن بلغت حدوبتـه الركوع ينخفض للركوع قليلاً؛ ليحصل الفرق بين القيام والركوع انتهى، فقد أطلق عـدم جــواز الاقتداء به، وعلمت ما فيه من اختلاف التصحيح.
And it is valid the following of a hunchbacked person as long as his hump has not reached the level of bowing, by agreement on the sounder view. They differed when it does reach. In al-Mujtaba: it is permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?), and most scholars adopted it. In Sharh al-Munyah: it is the sounder view, analogous to following a sitting person, because standing is the straightening of the two halves, and his lower half is straight. So it is permissible according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?) and not permissible according to Muhammad. Al-Zayla'i said: in al-Zuhayriyyah it is the sounder view, end. So the correction differed. In al-Dhakhirah and al-Khulasah: a hunchbacked standing person is like a sitting person leading a standing person, end, so permission is absolute. In al-Bazzaziyyah: Abu al-Layth said: the imamate of a hunchback is not permissible. As for himself, if his hump reaches bowing, he should lower slightly for bowing to differentiate between standing and bowing, end, so he absolutely prohibits following him. You know the difference in correction.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of following a hunchbacked (ahdab) imam. It first states that if the hump does not reach the level of bowing (ruku'), all scholars agree it is valid. The dispute arises when the hump is so pronounced that it reaches the bowing position, meaning the imam appears constantly bent. Some scholars say it is permissible to follow him because his lower half is straight, and standing is defined as the straightness of the two halves (upper and lower). Since his lower half is straight, he is considered standing, similar to a sitting person (who is still considered capable of leading a standing person). Others, including Imam Muhammad, say it is not permissible because his posture resembles bowing. The author quotes various sources showing the difference in tashih (correction) of the issue, concluding that there is no single relied-upon view, but the weight of later scholars seems to lean toward permission, though Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi prohibits it absolutely. The practical consequence is whether the prayer behind such an imam is valid or must be repeated.

Key Terms
أحدب (ahdab): A person with a hunchback, curved spine, causing his upper body to be bent forward.
استواء النصفين (istiwa' al-nisfayn): The straightness of the two halves (upper and lower body). This is considered the essence of qiyam (standing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is valid by agreement on the sounder view.
C) It is valid only according to Muhammad.
D) It is invalid according to Abu Yusuf.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following a hunchbacked imam hinges on the definition of standing; when the hump reaches bowing, Hanafi scholars differ based on whether the lower half straightness suffices.

Valid Following of a Person in Similar or Lower Posture
Ruling on validity of following when both imam and follower are in similar or lower postures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which it is valid for a person in a reduced posture to follow an imam in a similar or stronger posture, and identify the invalid scenario.

Core Idea
Following is valid only when the imam's posture is equal to or stronger than the follower's.

In congregational prayer, the imam leads, and the followers build their prayer upon his. When some worshippers cannot stand due to illness, they pray sitting or lying down. This ruling clarifies which combinations of postures are valid for following the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is following (iqitida) in prayer when both imam and follower are in reduced postures (sitting or lying down). The ruling is 'valid' (sahih) under specific conditions.
2
List the three valid scenarios
The passage mentions three valid combinations: both sitting, both lying down, or the follower lying down while the imam sits.
3
Extract the underlying principle
Validity depends on the relative 'strength' of posture. The imam must be in a posture equal to or stronger than the follower's. This is derived from the phrase 'because his state is stronger'.
4
Identify the invalid scenario
The opposite case—imam lying down while follower sits—is invalid because the imam's posture is weaker. The text excludes it by saying 'not the opposite'.
5
Reflect on the rationale
The follower's prayer is built on the imam's prayer. Therefore, the imam must have a firmer foundation (stronger posture) for the follower's prayer to be sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) صح اقتداء (موم بمثله) بأن كانا قاعدين، أو مضطجعين، أو المأموم مضطجعاً والإمام قاعداً؛ لقوة حاله لا عكسه.
And it is valid following of a person in a posture by his like, such that both are sitting, or both are lying down, or the follower is lying down and the imam is sitting; because his state is stronger, not the opposite.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: it is valid for a person to follow an imam who is in the same or a stronger posture. Specifically, it lists three scenarios: both are sitting, both are lying down, or the follower is lying down and the imam is sitting. The key principle is that the imam's state must be equal to or stronger than the follower's (since the follower is building his prayer on the imam's prayer). The opposite case (imam lying down and follower sitting) is invalid because the imam's state is weaker. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that the imam must be in a state no weaker than the follower.

Key Terms
موم (mūm (or mawm)): A person in a posture of prayer, either sitting, lying, or similar. It refers to one who is not standing fully.
مضطجع (muḍṭaji'): A person lying down, usually on his side, for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Sitting follower behind a lying-down imam.
D) Lying-down follower behind a lying-down imam.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following in reduced postures depends on the imam having a posture equal to or stronger than the follower's.

Valid Following: Voluntary Behind Obligatory Prayer
Ruling on a voluntary prayer follower behind an obligatory prayer imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a voluntary prayer (nafl) follower behind an obligatory (fard) imam is valid in the Hanafi school, and explain the two proofs: the principle of binā' al-ḍa'īf 'alā al-qawī and the recitation rule.

Core Idea
A voluntary prayer follower behind an obligatory imam is valid because the stronger (fard) supports the weaker (nafl).

This lesson examines a specific case of prayer following: a person performing a voluntary prayer (mutanafifl) joining an imam who is performing an obligatory prayer (muftariḍ). The Hanafi school rules this as valid based on a key legal principle and a nuanced understanding of recitation obligations. Let us delve into the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqtidā' (following) of a mutanafifl behind a muftariḍ. The ruling is ṣaḥīḥ (valid). This is explicitly stated in the text.
2
Analyze the first proof: the principle of binā' al-ḍa'īf 'alā al-qawī
The 'weak' (nafl prayer) is built upon the 'strong' (obligatory prayer). This means the validity of the follower's prayer is supported by the imam's stronger obligation. This is a rational proof (dalīl 'aqlī) used in Hanafi fiqh.
This principle appears in other areas, e.g., a latecomer building on the imam's prayer.
3
Examine the second proof: recitation rule
In the last two rak'ats of a voluntary prayer, recitation is obligatory (fard) when performed alone. But when following an imam, the follower is prohibited from reciting (the imam's recitation suffices). Thus, for the follower, the recitation becomes voluntary (nafl) just like the imam's, removing a potential inconsistency.
This argument shows that the recitation obligation adjusts to the follower's status.
4
Understand the opposite case: invalid following
The reverse scenario (obligatory performer following a voluntary imam) is invalid because it would be building the strong on the weak, which is not allowed. This distinction highlights the principle's application.
The passage implicitly refers to the well-known rule that such reversed following is invalid.
5
Confirm the Hanafi consensus
This ruling is from the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and is agreed upon within the school (muttafaq alayh). There is no intra-Hanafi dispute, and it is the muftā bihī position.
The source notes no ikhtilaf, so this is a settled ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) صح اقتداء (متنفّـل بمُقْتَرِض)؛ لأنه بناء الضعيف على القوي وللقراءة وإن كانت فرضاً في الأخريين من النفل، نفلاً في الفرض، لكن إنما تكون فرضاً إذا كان مصلي النفل منفرداً، أما إذا كان مقتدياً فلا، لأنها محظورة كذا في ( العناية». أو لأنه بالاقتداء صار تبعاً للإمام في القراءة، فكانت نـفــلاً في حقه كإمامه
And it is valid following of a voluntary performer by an obligatory performer; because it is building the weak on the strong, and for the recitation: even though it is obligatory in the last two rak'ats of voluntary prayer, it is voluntary in obligatory prayer, but it only becomes obligatory if the voluntary performer is alone. As for when he is a follower, it is not, because it is prohibited. That is in al-'Inayah. Or because by following, he becomes a follower of the imam in recitation, so it becomes voluntary in his right like his imam.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling and the reasoning for the validity of a person performing voluntary (nafl) prayer following an imam who is performing obligatory (fard) prayer. The reasoning is based on the principle of building the weak upon the strong: the voluntary prayer is weaker in its obligation, so it can be built upon the strong obligatory prayer. Additionally, the recitation issue is addressed: in the last two rak'ats of a voluntary prayer, recitation is obligatory when performed alone, but when following an imam, the follower is silent (prohibited from reciting), so the recitation becomes voluntary for him as it is for the imam. This further supports the validity. The opposite case (obligatory following voluntary) is invalid because that would be building the strong on the weak.

Key Terms
متنفل (mutanafifl): A person performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer.
مفترض (muftariḍ): A person performing an obligatory (fard) prayer.
بناء الضعيف على القوي (binā' al-ḍa'īf 'alā al-qawī): A legal principle: the weaker act is built upon the stronger act. Here, nafl is built on fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a voluntary prayer follower behind an obligatory imam considered valid according to the passage?
A) Because both have the same intention.
B) Because it is building the weak on the strong.
C) Because the follower can recite behind the imam.
D) Because the imam's prayer becomes voluntary.

Key Takeaway
A voluntary prayer follower behind an obligatory imam is valid in the Hanafi school due to the principle of building weak on strong and the recitation rule.

Follower's Repetition When Imam's Prayer Invalid; Imam's Duty to Inform
Ruling on follower's repetition and imam's duty to inform based on type of defect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when a follower must repeat the prayer due to imam's invalid prayer and explain the imam's obligation to inform the followers.

Core Idea
The follower's prayer is invalid if the imam's lacked a condition or pillar; the imam must inform the followers.

This passage addresses an important scenario in congregational prayer: what happens if it becomes known that the imam's prayer was invalid from the start? The author distinguishes between invalidity due to missing a condition or pillar (which forces the follower to repeat) and invalidity due to a later nullifier (which does not affect the follower). Additionally, the imam has a duty to inform the congregation of the need to repeat, based on prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of defect
Distinguish between a missing condition/pillar (fawt shart or rukn) and a nullifier (mufsid) that occurs after the prayer.
The ruling for the follower differs accordingly.
2
Determine the follower's ruling for each
If the imam's prayer was missing a condition or pillar, follower must repeat (i'ada) as an obligation. If a nullifier occurred, follower does not repeat.
The reasoning: following is like building on a foundation; if the foundation was defective, the building is void.
3
Understand the imam's duty to inform
The imam is obligated to inform the followers to the extent possible (by letter, messenger, or himself) that their prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This is the chosen view (al-Mukhtar).
4
Examine the evidence
The passage cites the hadith: 'When the imam's prayer is corrupted, the prayer of those behind him is corrupted.' Also the practice of Ali and Umar supports the imam's duty.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars (e.g., al-Dirayah) hold that the imam need not inform if the followers are unspecified. The chosen view requires informing regardless.
The story of Umar and Ali strengthens the obligation.

Source Text

(وإن ظهر بطلان صلاة إمامِهِ ) بفوات شرط أو ركن (أعَادَ) لزوماً يعني: افترض عليه الإتيان بالفرض، وليس المراد الإعادة الجابرة لنقص في المؤدى، لأن الاقتداء بناء، والبناء على المعدوم محال، وتقدم ما إذا أخبر بأنه صلى مرة بغير طهارة، وقيدنا ظهور البطلان بفوات شرط أو ركــن، إشارة إلى أنه لو طرأ المفسد لا يعيد المقتدي صلاته، كما لو ارتد الإمام (۳) أو سعى إلى الجمعة بعـدمــا صـلـي الظهر بجماعة، وسعى هو دونهم، فسدت صلاته فقط كما في ( العناية ». وكذا لو عاد إلى سجود التلاوة بعدما تفرقوا)، كما سنذكره ويَلْزَمُ الإِمَامَ إذا علم بفساد صلاته ( إعــلام الـقـوم بإعادة صلاتهم بالقَدْرِ الممكن)، بكتاب أو رسول أو نفسه (في المُخْتَارِ ) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( إِذَا فَسَدَتْ صَلاةُ الإِمَامِ فَسَدَتْ صَلَاةُ مَنْ خَلْفَهُ » (۳). وعن علي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( أنَّه صَلَّى بِهِمْ ثُمَّ جَاءَ وَرَأْسُهُ يَقْطُرُ بهم» (4) كذا قاله الزيلعي، وروى عبد الرزاق في مصنفه » : أن عليه «صلى بالناس وهـو جنب، أو على غير وضوء، فأعاد وأمرهم أن يعيدوا ) وأن عمر ( صلَّى بالنَّاس وهو جنب، فأعاد ولم يعد الناس، فقال له علي قد كان ينبغي لمَن صلَّى معك أن يعيدوا، قال: فرجعوا إلى قـول علي ه ه ه ه ه » (٢). قال القاسم وقال ابن مسعود: مثل قول علي الله كذا في «البرهان» وقال في الدراية » : ولا يلزم الإمام إذا كانوا قوماً غير معينين، وفي خزانة الأكمل لأنه سكت عن . معفو عنه، وعن الوبري ) : يخبرهم وإن كان مختلفاً فيه ونظيره إذا رأى غيره يتوضأ من ماء نجس أو على ثوبه نجاسة.
And if the invalidity of the imam's prayer becomes apparent due to the lapse of a condition or a pillar, he (the follower) must repeat it, meaning: it becomes obligatory upon him to perform the obligatory prayer. It does not mean the repetition that compensates for a deficiency in what was performed, because following is building, and building upon what does not exist is impossible. It has preceded that if he informed that he prayed once without purity, and we restricted the appearance of invalidity to lapse of a condition or pillar, indicating that if a nullifier occurs, the follower does not repeat his prayer, such as if the imam apostatizes, or if he went to the Friday prayer after having prayed noon in congregation, and he went while they did not, then only his prayer is invalidated, as in al-'Inayah. Similarly, if he returned to prostrate for recitation after they had dispersed, as we will mention. And it is necessary for the imam, if he knows the corruption of his prayer, to inform the people to repeat their prayers to the extent possible, by a letter, a messenger, or himself, in the chosen view, because of the Prophet's saying: 'When the imam's prayer is corrupted, the prayer of those behind him is corrupted.' And from Ali from the Prophet: 'He prayed with them then came with his head dripping with water.' So said al-Zayla'i. And Abd al-Razzaq narrated in his Musannaf that he prayed with people while he was junub or without ablution, so he repeated and ordered them to repeat. And that Umar prayed with people while he was junub, so he repeated but did not order the people to repeat. Ali said to him: 'It would have been proper for those who prayed with you to repeat.' He said: So they returned to the saying of Ali. Al-Qasim said, and Ibn Mas'ud said similar to the saying of Ali. That is in al-Burhan. In al-Dirayah: It is not necessary for the imam if they are unspecified people. In Khazanat al-Akmal: because he remained silent about it, it is excused. From al-Wabari: he should inform them even if it is disputed. And the analogy is if he sees someone performing wudu with impure water or with impurity on his garment.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof regarding what happens if the imam's prayer becomes invalid after it has been performed in congregation. The key points are: 1) If the invalidity becomes apparent due to a missing condition (e.g., wudu) or pillar (e.g., ruku'), the follower must repeat the prayer (i'ada) as an obligation, not as a sunnah compensation. This is because following is like building a structure on a foundation; if the foundation is defective, the building does not exist. 2) If the invalidity is due to a nullifier (mufsid) that occurs after the prayer, such as apostasy or breaking wudu intentionally, the follower does not repeat because his prayer was valid at the time. 3) The imam is obligated to inform the followers that their prayer is invalid and needs to be repeated, to the best of his ability (e.g., by sending a message or person). This is based on several hadith and the practice of the Sahaba. The passage mentions the story of Umar praying while junub; he did not inform the people, but Ali told him they should have repeated, so Umar accepted that. There is a difference of opinion: if the followers are unspecified (e.g., general public), the imam may not be required to inform each one. But the relied-upon view is that he must make a reasonable effort. The passage concludes with an analogy to a person seeing someone using impure water for wudu.

Key Terms
إعادة (i'āda): Repeating the prayer from the beginning due to a fundamental defect in the original prayer.
مفسد (mufsid): An act that nullifies the prayer after it was valid, e.g., intentional laughter, apostasy.
إعلام (i'lām): The imam's duty to inform the followers that their prayer must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Imam apostatizes after the prayer.
B) Imam discovers his prayer lacked wudu.
C) Imam laughs during the prayer.
D) Imam returns to recite a sajdah after the congregation dispersed.

Key Takeaway
The follower must repeat if the imam's prayer was missing a condition or pillar; the imam must inform the followers to the best of his ability.

The Imam's Obligation to Inform the Congregation of Invalid Prayer
Ruling with evidence on informing congregation of prayer invalidity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's obligation to inform the congregation when his prayer becomes invalid, identify the evidence (dalil), and distinguish the chosen position from the dissenting view regarding non-specific congregations.

Core Idea
The imam must inform the congregation of his invalid prayer—the proof is the hadith and the practice of the Companions.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a critical issue in congregational prayer: what happens when the imam's prayer becomes invalid? Does he have a duty to inform the followers? The Hanafi school, relying on prophetic hadith and companion practice, holds that he must inform to the extent possible. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the chosen position, and the nuance regarding unspecified congregations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and what legal classification it receives. The act is the imam knowing his prayer is invalid. The ruling is that he must inform the congregation to repeat their prayers. This is wajib (obligatory) according to the chosen position.
Wajib here indicates obligation, not fard; the evidence is zanni.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the textual evidence cited. The primary dalil is the hadith: 'When the imam's prayer becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' Additional evidence from the actions of Ali and Umar.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Hurairah, recorded by Ibn al-Jawzi and al-Muttaqi al-Hindi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the evidence proves the ruling. The hadith establishes a causal link: the imam's invalidity causes the followers' invalidity. Therefore, the imam must inform them so they can repeat correctly.
The conditional clause 'idha...fasadat' indicates a direct consequence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify any scholarly disagreement. Some later Hanafi scholars (as in al-Dirayah) hold that the imam is not obligated if the congregation is not specifically designated (ghayr mu'ayyanin).
This view is based on the idea that harm is general and the imam's responsibility is limited.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine which position is preferred. The author states that the chosen (mukhtar) position is that the imam must inform in all cases, citing al-Wabari and the general implication of the hadith. The dissenting view is excused but not relied upon.
The chosen position is the mufta bihi for fatwa, as it aligns with the primary evidence.

It is necessary for the imam to inform the people to repeat their prayer to the extent possible, according to the chosen position. If he led the noon prayer in congregation and then went to the Friday prayer, his own prayer becomes invalid, as in al-'Inayah. Similarly, if he returned to prostrate for recitation after they had dispersed, as we will mention. Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a sharh on the ruling that if an imam's prayer becomes invalid (e.g., due to being in a state of janabah or having had an incorrect intention), he must inform the congregation to repeat their prayers. The proof includes hadith: 'When the imam's prayer becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' The text provides examples from the actions of Ali and Umar, showing that the imam should order the repetition. There is a dispute: some say it is obligatory (the chosen position), while others exempt it for non-specific congregations. The author includes an exception for cases where the imam had a valid excuse or the people were not designated. The footnote gives two example scenarios: one about Friday prayer and one about returning for prostration of recitation after the congregation had dispersed.

Key Terms
إعلام (i'lam): Informing the congregation about the invalidity of the imam's prayer so they can repeat.
فساد الصلاة (fasad al-salah): Invalidity of prayer due to missing a condition or pillar, requiring repetition.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or relied-upon position in the madhhab.
غير معينين (ghayr mu'ayyanin): Non-specific congregation: people not individually known or designated.
