والروافض()، الغالية. ومن يقول بخلق القرآن (۳)، والخطابية (۳)، والمشبهة )، ونحوهم، ممن تكفره بدعته. والحاصل أن من كان من أهل قبلتنا، ولم يغل حتى لم يحكم بكفــره تـصــح الـصـلاة خلفه وتكره، فلا تجوز خلف منكر الشفاعة، والرؤية، وعذاب القبر، والكرام الكاتبين، لأنـه كـافر لتواتر هذه الأمور عن الشارع، ومن قال: لا يرى لعظمته وجلاله فهو مبتدع، ولا خلف منكر المسح على الخفين، والمشبه إذا قال: له تَعَالى يَد ورجل كما للعباد، فهو كافر ملعون، وإن قال: جسم لا كالأجسام فهو مبتدع، لأنه ليس فيه إلا إطلاق لفظ الجسم عليه، وهو موهم للنقص، فرفعه بقوله لا كالأجسام، فلم يبق إلا مجرد الإطلاق، وذلك معصية تنتهض سبباً للعقاب، لمـا فـيـه مـن الإيهام، بخلاف ما لو قاله على التشبيه، فإنه كافر، وقيل: يكفر بمجردا د الإطلاق أيضاً، ولا خلف منكر خلافة أبي بكر، أو عمر، أو عثمان الله لأنه كافر، ويصح خلف من يفضل عليـا عـلـيـهـم لأنه مبتدع. وروی محمد عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أن الصلاة خلف أهل الأهواء لا تجوز، والصحيح أنـهـا تجوز على الحكم الذي ذكرنا مع الكراهة خلف من لا تكفره بدعته؛ لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «صلوا خلـف كـلّ بر وفاجر، وصلوا على كل بر وفاجر، وجَاهِدُوا مـع كـل بـر وفاجر " رواه الدارقطني كما في (٥) البرهان»، وإذا صلى خلف فاسق أو مبتدع يكون محرزاً ثواب الجماعة، لكن لا ينال ثـواب مــن يصلي خلف تقي، قال : ( مَنْ  َصلَّى خَلْفَ عَالِم تَقي فَكَأَنَّما صَلَّى خَلْفَ نَبي » كذا في مجمع
And the child of fornication, the ignorant, the sinful, and the innovator. They know the legal rulings. And they said: it is recommended to prefer the one who resides in the cities among the Arabs due to knowledge. And in al-Mustasfa, it is narrated that a Bedouin followed an imam who recited: 'The Bedouins are more severe in disbelief and hypocrisy' (Surah at-Tawbah: 97), so he struck him with a stick. Then he followed him again and he recited: 'And among the Bedouins are those who believe in Allah and the Last Day' (Surah at-Tawbah: 99), so he said: 'The stick benefited you.' (And) the imamah of a child of fornication is disliked because he has no father to teach him, so ignorance prevails over him. Hence, he restricted it along with what preceded by saying: (and the ignorant). For if he were knowledgeable and pious, his imamah would not be disliked, because the dislike in their case is due to the defects we mentioned, and if they are absent, then a Bedouin is better than a city dweller, a slave than a free man, a child of fornication than a legitimate child, and a blind person than a sighted one. So the ruling is contrary. This is from al-Ikhtiyar. (And) the imamah of a sinful person (who is knowledgeable) is disliked because he does not care about his religion, and because appointing him as imam is honoring him, while it is obligatory to dishonor him according to the Sharia. And if it is impossible to prevent him, Friday prayer may be performed behind him if Friday prayer is not established except in his locality; otherwise, one should go to another mosque. Ibn Umar and Anas ibn Malik used to pray behind al-Hajjaj on Friday. The sinful (fasiq) is the one who deviates from obedience. The noun is fasiq, and it is pluralized as fassaq and fisq. Its origin is the exit of a thing from a thing in a corrupt manner. It is said: the date has become rotten when it comes out of its peel. (And) the imamah of an innovator (mubtadi') is disliked with karahah tanzih. The word is derived from ibtida' al-amr, i.e., to initiate and innovate something. Bid'ah is like raf'ah (elevation), then it came to be used for one who follows whims, adding to or subtracting from the religion. Bid'ah is defined as something introduced contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from knowledge, action, or state, by way of some doubt or approval, and made into a correct religion and a straight path. What is meant is the innovator whose innovation does not render him a disbeliever. For if it renders him a disbeliever, his imamah is not valid, as we have stated. Indeed, following ahl al-ahwa (people of whims) is valid except the Jahmiyyah, the Qadiriyyah... and the Rawafid, the Ghaliyah, and those who say the Qur'an is created, and the Khattabiyyah, and the Mushabbihah, and similar ones whose innovation renders them disbelievers. The conclusion is that whoever is from the people of our qiblah and does not go to extremes so that he is not ruled a disbeliever, prayer behind him is valid and disliked. So prayer is not allowed behind one who denies intercession, the vision (of Allah), the punishment of the grave, and the noble scribes (angels), because he is a disbeliever due to these matters being mutawatir from the Lawgiver. One who says: He is not seen due to His greatness and majesty is an innovator. And one who denies wiping over the socks (khuffs) – prayer is not allowed behind him. And the Mushabbih (anthropomorphist) if he says: Allah has a hand and a foot like the servants, then he is a disbeliever, accursed. And if he says: He is a body not like bodies, then he is an innovator, because there is nothing in it except the application of the word 'body' to Him, which suggests deficiency, so he removed it by saying 'not like bodies', so nothing remains except mere application, and that is a sin that becomes a cause for punishment, due to the suggestion (of deficiency). Contrary to if he said it as actual comparison, then he is a disbeliever. And it is said: he becomes a disbeliever by mere application as well. And prayer is not allowed behind one who denies the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, or Uthman (may Allah be pleased with them) because he is a disbeliever. And prayer is valid behind one who prefers Ali over them (may Allah be pleased with them) because he is an innovator. Muhammad reported from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind ahl al-ahwa is not permissible. The correct view is that it is permissible as per the ruling we mentioned, with dislike behind one whose innovation does not render him a disbeliever, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, and pray over every righteous and sinful person, and strive (in jihad) with every righteous and sinful person' – narrated by al-Daraqutni as in al-Burhan. And if one prays behind a fasiq or mubtadi', he attains the reward of the congregation, but he does not attain the reward of one who prays behind a pious person. He said: 'Whoever prays behind a knowledgeable pious person is as if he prayed behind a prophet' – as in Majma' al-Anhur.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding leading prayer (imamah) for certain types of individuals. It begins by discussing the imamah of a child of fornication (walad zina), the ignorant, the sinful (fasiq), and the innovator (mubtadi'). The text clarifies that the dislike (karahah) for these individuals is based on specific defects: a child of fornication is likely ignorant due to lack of paternal teaching, an ignorant person lacks knowledge, a sinful person does not care about religion (even if knowledgeable), and an innovator introduces beliefs contrary to the Sunnah. However, if these defects are absent (e.g., the individual is knowledgeable and pious despite being a child of fornication), then there is no dislike. The text uses a historical anecdote from al-Mustasfa about a Bedouin who struck an imam for reciting a verse that seemed to insult Bedouins, but later approved when the imam recited a positive verse—this illustrates that ignorance can lead to inappropriate actions, but knowledge and piety are important. The discussion then turns to the definition of fasiq and the ruling of praying behind him: it is disliked (makruh) but permissible, and in cases where Friday prayer cannot be established elsewhere, it may be necessary. The example of Ibn Umar and Anas praying behind Hajjaj (a notoriously oppressive governor) is cited. For innovators (mubtadi'), the dislike is classified as tanzih (religiously undesirable but not sinful). The key distinction is whether the innovation takes one out of Islam. If the innovation is kufr (disbelief), such as the beliefs of the Jahmiyyah, Qadiriyyah, Rawafid, Khawarij, etc., then prayer behind them is invalid. If the innovation does not constitute kufr (e.g., preferring Ali over the first three caliphs), the prayer is valid but disliked. The text then presents an intra-madhhab dispute: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan reports from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind ahl al-ahwa is not permissible, but the relied-upon (sahih) view is that it is permissible with dislike, supported by the hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' The reward for such prayer is the general congregational reward, but not the full reward of praying behind a truly pious imam. The passage concludes with the statement that praying behind a knowledgeable pious imam is like praying behind a prophet, though this hadith is noted as weak by some scholars. Overall, the commentary provides a nuanced ruling that balances the need for community prayer with the avoidance of honoring sinners and innovators.

Key Terms
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): A child born from fornication; in this context, one whose imamah is disliked because he likely has no father to teach him, leading to ignorance.
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists in minor sins; the one who deviates from obedience to Allah.
مبتدع (mubtadi'): An innovator in religion, introducing beliefs or practices contrary to the Sunnah. If the innovation is kufr, imamah is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling on praying behind an imam who is a fasiq (sinful)?
A) Invalid
B) Valid but disliked (makruh tanzih)
C) Valid and recommended
D) Valid only if no other imam is available

Key Takeaway
Praying behind a fasiq or non-kufr innovator is valid but disliked; the hadith and Companion practice override the general principle of dishonoring sinners.

Prayer Behind Innovators: When It Is Valid and When It Is Not
Ruling on prayer behind deviant sects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between innovators whose beliefs constitute kufr and those who remain Muslims, and state the Hanafi ruling on praying behind each category.

Core Idea
Prayer behind an innovator is valid unless his innovation reaches disbelief.

Not all innovators are the same in Hanafi fiqh. Some beliefs take a person out of Islam entirely, while others are sinful innovations that still leave him a Muslim. This ruling has practical consequences for congregational prayer. Let's examine the criteria and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage states: anyone who is from the people of our qiblah and does not go to extremes such that he is judged a disbeliever—prayer behind him is valid but disliked. This is the default rule.
The default is validity with karahah tanzihiyyah.
2
Distinguish between kufr and bid'ah
The text lists specific beliefs that constitute kufr: denial of intercession, vision of Allah, punishment of the grave, recording angels, and denial of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman. Other beliefs (e.g., preferring Ali, saying 'body unlike bodies') are bid'ah but not kufr.
The key is whether the belief rejects a matter proven by tawatur or ijma.
3
Apply the test to sects
Rafidis, Ghaliyah, those who say Quran is created, Khattabiyyah, Mushabbihah (if they liken Allah to creation) are kafir. Deniers of wiping over socks are innovators. Anthropomorphists who say 'body unlike bodies' are innovators.
Mushabbih who says 'hand like a human' is kafir; different wording changes the ruling.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Muhammad reports from Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind ahl al-ahwa is not permissible. But the relied-upon position (sahih) is permissibility with dislike, based on the hadith 'Pray behind every pious and wicked person.'
The disagreement is within the school; the mufta bihi is permissibility.
5
Note the practical consequence
If one prays behind an innovator (not a kafir), the prayer is valid and he gets the reward of congregation, but he loses the extra virtue of praying behind a truly pious imam.
Weak hadith is used for fada'il al-a'mal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والروافض الغالية ومن يقول بخلق القرآن والخطابية والمشبهة ونحوهم ممن تكفره بدعته والحاصل أن من كان من أهل قبلتنا ولم يغل حتى لم يحكم بكفره تصح الصلاة خلفه وتكره فلا تجوز خلف منكر الشفاعة والرؤية وعذاب القبر والكرام الكاتبين لأنه كافر لتواتر هذه الأمور عن الشارع ومن قال لا يرى لعظمته وجلاله فهو مبتدع ولا خلف منكر المسح على الخفين والمشبه إذا قال له تعالى يد ورجل كما للعباد فهو كافر ملعون وإن قال جسم لا كالأجسام فهو مبتدع لأنه ليس فيه إلا إطلاق لفظ الجسم عليه وهو موهم للنقص فرفعه بقوله لا كالأجسام فلم يبق إلا مجرد الإطلاق وذلك معصية تنتهض سببا للعقاب لما فيه من الإيهام بخلاف ما لو قاله على التشبيه فإنه كافر وقيل يكفر بمجرد الإطلاق أيضا ولا خلف منكر خلافة أبي بكر أو عمر أو عثمان لأنه كافر ويصح خلف من يفضل عليا عليهم لأنه مبتدع وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أن الصلاة خلف أهل الأهواء لا تجوز والصحيح أنها تجوز على الحكم الذي ذكرنا مع الكراهة خلف من لا تكفره بدعته لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر وصلوا على كل بر وفاجر وجاهدوا مع كل بر وفاجر رواه الدارقطني كما في البرهان وإذا صلى خلف فاسق أو مبتدع يكون محرزا ثواب الجماعة لكن لا ينال ثواب من يصلي خلف تقي قال من صلى خلف عالم تقي فكأنما صلى خلف نبي كذا في مجمع الروايات والحديث الضعيف يعمل به في فضائل الأعمال
And the Rafidis, the extremists (Ghaliyah), and those who say the Quran is created, and the Khattabiyyah, and the Mushabbihah, and similar groups, those whose innovation renders them disbelievers. The conclusion: whoever is from the people of our qiblah and does not go to extremes such that he is not judged a disbeliever, prayer behind him is valid but disliked. So it is not permissible to pray behind one who denies intercession, the vision (of Allah), the punishment of the grave, and the noble recording angels, because he is a disbeliever due to the tawatur of these matters from the Lawgiver. And whoever says: He is not seen due to His greatness and majesty, he is an innovator. And it is not permissible to pray behind one who denies wiping over the leather socks. And the anthropomorphist (Mushabbih) if he says: For Allah, the Exalted, has a hand and foot like that of servants, he is a disbeliever and accursed. And if he says: a body not like bodies, he is an innovator, because it is nothing but applying the term 'body' to Him, and it suggests imperfection; so he removes it by saying 'not like bodies,' and nothing remains except mere application, and that is a sin leading to punishment due to the suggestion it contains, unlike if he said it as an anthropomorphism, then he is a disbeliever. And it is said: he becomes a disbeliever by mere application as well. And it is not permissible to pray behind one who denies the caliphate of Abu Bakr, or Umar, or Uthman, because he is a disbeliever. And it is valid to pray behind one who prefers Ali over them, because he is an innovator. Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind the people of desires (ahl al-ahwa) is not permissible. But the correct view is that it is permissible according to the ruling we mentioned, with dislike, behind one whose innovation does not cause him to be a disbeliever, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Pray behind every pious and wicked person, and pray over every pious and wicked person, and strive with every pious and wicked person,' narrated by al-Daraqutni as in al-Burhan. And if one prays behind a sinner or innovator, he attains the reward of congregation, but he does not attain the reward of one who prays behind a pious person. He said: 'Whoever prays behind a pious scholar is as if he prayed behind a prophet.' So in Majma' al-Riwayat, and weak hadith is acted upon in virtuous deeds.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of praying behind various deviant sects. It first lists groups that are considered disbelievers due to their innovation: the Rafidis (extreme Shia who reject Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman and the like), the Ghaliyah (extremists who deify Ali), those who say the Quran is created (a Mu'tazilite view), the Khattabiyyah (extreme Shia sect), the Mushabbihah (anthropomorphists), and similar groups. The key principle is: anyone who is from the people of our qiblah (i.e., faces Makkah in prayer) and does not go to such extremes that his innovation makes him a disbeliever—prayer behind him is valid but disliked (makruh). Conversely, if his innovation makes him a disbeliever (kafir), prayer behind him is not valid. The passage details specific beliefs that constitute kufr: denial of intercession (shafa'ah), the beatific vision (ru'yah), punishment of the grave, and the noble recording angels—because these matters have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission) from the Prophet. Also, denial of wiping over leather socks does not make one a disbeliever but an innovator; anthropomorphism with explicit comparison (like saying Allah has a hand like a human) is kufr, but saying 'body unlike bodies' is innovation (bid'ah). Denial of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman is kufr (since it rejects the consensus of the Sahabah). Preferring Ali over them is innovation but not kufr. Then an intra-Hanafi dispute is narrated: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani reports from Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind ahl al-ahwa (people of heretical desires) is not permissible. However, the correct position (sahih) according to the author is that it is permissible, but with dislike, as long as the imam's innovation does not reach kufr. The proof is the hadith: 'Pray behind every pious and wicked person...' The author adds that praying behind a sinner or innovator still earns the reward of congregation, but not the full reward of praying behind a truly pious person. The phrase 'weak hadith is acted upon in virtuous deeds' indicates that although the chain of the hadith may be weak, it is used for encouragement in non-obligatory matters. The 'Majma' al-Riwayat' may refer to a collection where similar narrations are gathered.

Key Terms
الروافض (al-Rawafid): Extreme Shia who reject the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman.
أهل الأهواء (Ahl al-Ahwa): People of heretical desires or innovations.
مبتدع (Mubtadi'): An innovator in religious matters whose innovation does not reach kufr.
كرامة (Karahah): Dislike (makruh) - in this context, tanzihi (not prohibitive).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying behind someone who denies the punishment of the grave?
A) Valid and not disliked
B) Valid but disliked
C) Invalid because he is a kafir
D) Invalid only if he denies it explicitly

Key Takeaway
The validity of prayer behind an innovator hinges on whether his innovation constitutes kufr; if it does not, the prayer is valid but disliked.

Disliked Acts in Congregational Prayer
Details three disliked scenarios in congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three disliked acts in congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for each ruling.

Core Idea
Prolonging prayer, naked congregation, and women's congregation with a female imam are disliked but not invalid.

This passage from Nur al-Idah identifies three scenarios in congregational prayer that are makruh: the imam prolonging the prayer, a group of naked people praying together, and women forming a congregation with a female imam. We will examine the evidence for each ruling and the conditions that affect their application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three disliked acts
Read the passage and name each act that is described as makruh. Note the specific wording for each.
2
Examine the proof for each disliked act
For prolonging prayer, locate the hadith of Abu Mas'ud and the hadith of Anas. For naked congregation, identify the reasoning given (exposure of awrah). For women's congregation, find the hadith 'Their houses are better for them' and the practice of A'ishah and Umm Salamah.
The proofs range from direct prophetic statements to juristic analogy.
3
Note the exceptions and conditions
Observe that prolonging is only disliked if it burdens the congregation; the imam may adapt. For women, funeral prayer is excluded from the dislike. Recognize that the dislike is contextual.
The imam should consider the needs of those praying behind him.
4
Determine the practical implications
Understand how these rulings apply in everyday prayer settings. Consider the balance between recommended acts and avoiding hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتطويل الصلاة وجماعة العراة والنساء فإن فعلن يقف الإمام وسطهنه و كره للإمام تطويل الصلاة لقول أبي مسعود الأنصاري جاء رجل إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا رسول الله إني لا أكاد أدرك الصلاة مما يطول بنا فلان فما رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في موعظة أشد غضبا من يومئذ فقال يا أيها الناس إن منكم منفرين من صلى بالناس فليخفف فإن منهم الكبير والضعيف وذا الحاجة رواه الشيخان وفي لفظ للبخاري والمريض وفي رواية وإذا صلى وحده فليصل كيف شاء ولحديث أنس أنه قال ما صليت خلف إمام قط أخف صلاة ولا أتم صلاة من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وفي المضمرات لا يزيد القراءة المستحبة ولا يثقل على القوم ولكن يخفف بعد أن يكون على التمام والاستحباب انتهى ولكن يراعي حال من معه كما روي أنه قرأ بالمعوذتين في الفجر فلما فرغ قيل أوجزت قال سمعت بكاء صبي فخشيت أن تفتن أمه انتهى فمع مراعاة حال المؤتم لا يخرج بذلك عن المسنون و كره جماعة العراة إذا اقتدوا بواحد منهم لما فيها من إطلاع بعضهم على عورة بعض و كره جماعة النساء بإمام منهن لأن اجتماعهن قل ما يخلوا عن فتنة وفي قيامهن مخالفة حال الإمام وهذا في غير صلاة الجنازة فإنها لا تكره لهن جماعة لفوات الصلاة بانفراد واحدة بها لغيرها والتنفل بها ممتنع وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام بيوتهن خير لهن لو كن يعلمن فإن فعلن أردن الصلاة جماعة بواحدة منهن يجب أن يقف الإمام وسطهنه لما صح أن عائشة وأم سلمة كانتا تؤمان النساء حين كانت جماعتهن مشروعة فتقومان وسطهما
And the prolonging of prayer, and the congregation of naked people, and the congregation of women. If they do so, the imam stands in their middle. And it is disliked for the imam to prolong the prayer, because of the statement of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: A man came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I can hardly catch the prayer because so-and-so prolongs it for us.' I never saw the Messenger of Allah more angry in an admonition than that day. He said, 'O people, some of you are repellers. Whoever leads the people in prayer, let him lighten it, for among them are the elderly, the weak, and those with needs.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. In a wording of al-Bukhari: 'and the sick.' And in a narration: 'And if he prays alone, let him pray as he wishes.' And for the hadith of Anas: he said, 'I never prayed behind any imam whose prayer was lighter and more complete than the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' In al-Mudmarat: 'He should not increase the recommended recitation, nor burden the people, but should lighten while being complete and in accordance with the recommended—end.' But he should consider the conditions of those with him, as it is narrated that he recited al-Mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr, and when he finished it was said, 'You shortened.' He said, 'I heard the cry of a child, and feared that his mother would be tempted.' End. So by considering the condition of the followers, he does not deviate from the sunnah. And it is disliked: the congregation of naked people if they follow one of them, because it involves exposing each other's private parts. And it is disliked: the congregation of women with an imam from among them, because their gatherings are seldom free from temptation, and in their standing there is going against the state of the imam. This is other than the funeral prayer, for which congregation for women is not disliked, because the prayer would be lost if one woman prayed alone for another, and supererogatory prayer with it is forbidden. And he (peace be upon him) said, 'Their houses are better for them, if they only knew.' If they do it—i.e., intend to pray in congregation with one of them as imam—the imam must stand in their middle, because it is authentically reported that A'ishah and Umm Salamah used to lead women in prayer when their congregation was legislated, and they would stand in their middle.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage covers three disliked matters in congregational prayer. First, it is makruh for the imam to prolong the prayer unnecessarily. The proof is the hadith of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari where the Prophet became angry and instructed imams to lighten the prayer, considering the elderly, weak, sick, and those with needs. The Prophet himself was the lightest yet most complete in prayer. However, the imam should not skip recommended acts but consider the congregation's condition. The hadith of the child crying shows that even reciting short surahs is acceptable if there is a reason. Second, it is makruh for a group of naked people to pray in congregation behind one of them, because it leads to exposing private parts (awrah). Third, it is makruh for women to hold a congregation with a female imam, due to potential temptation and because their standing differs (women stand behind, not beside, the imam). However, this does not apply to funeral prayer, where women's congregation is not disliked because the prayer is lost if done individually, and supererogatory funeral prayer is not allowed. The hadith 'Their houses are better for them' indicates that women praying at home is superior. If women do pray in congregation, the female imam must stand in the middle of the row, not in front, as narrated from A'ishah and Umm Salamah (may Allah be pleased with them).

Key Terms
تطويل الصلاة (Tatwil al-Salah): Prolonging the prayer by the imam beyond what is customary, causing hardship.
جماعة العراة (Jama'at al-'Urat): A congregation of naked people (who have no clothes to cover their awrah).
وسطحهن (Wasatahunna): The female imam stands in the middle of the row, not in front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The imam prolonging the prayer.
B) A congregation of naked people.
C) Women praying in congregation with a female imam.
D) A person praying alone in the masjid.

Key Takeaway
Prolonging prayer, naked congregation, and women's congregation with a female imam are makruh tanzih in the Hanafi school, unless specific exceptions apply.

Dislike of Prolonging Prayer by the Imam
Explains the ruling and hadith evidence for imam not prolonging prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prolonging prayer by the imam and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Prolonging prayer unnecessarily is disliked for the imam because it burdens the congregation — lightening is sunnah.

This lesson examines a key adab (etiquette) for the imam in congregational prayer: avoiding excessive length. The Hanafi school rules that it is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked) for the imam to prolong the prayer beyond what is customary, especially when it causes hardship to the followers. We will explore the primary hadith evidence and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'tatwil al-salah' (prolonging prayer) by the imam. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked).
It is not haram because the command to lighten is a recommendation, not an obligation.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari recorded by al-Bukhari and Muslim is the main evidence.
The Prophet (peace be upon him) expressed strong anger at those who prolong prayer.
3
Analyze the imperative
The Prophet said 'falyukhaffif' (let him lighten). In Hanafi usul, an imperative indicates wujub, but here the context (anger, reasons) qualifies it as a strong recommendation to avoid dislike.
The imperative is not absolute due to the reasons given (old, weak, sick, needy).
4
Note additional evidence
Hadith of Anas that the Prophet's prayer was both light and complete, and the incident of shortening Fajr upon hearing a child cry.
These show that lightening does not compromise completeness.
5
State the allowance
The imam may shorten while maintaining the integral elements (arkan and wajibat). Consideration of the followers keeps him within the sunnah.
As long as he does not omit essential parts, shortening is acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الروايات والحديث الضعيف يعمل به في فضائل الأعمال. (وَ) كره للإمام (تطويلُ الصَّلاةِ) لقـــول أبي مسعود الأنصاري : جاء رجل إلى النبي فقال : يا رسول الله إنِّي لا أَكَادُ أدْرِكُ الصَّلاةَ مِمَّا يُطَوِّلُ بِنَا فُلانٌ فَمَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ لا فِي مَوْعِظَةٍ أَشَدَّ غَضَباً مِنْ يَوْمِئِذٍ فَقَالَ: يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ إِنَّ مِنْكُمْ مُتفرِينَ مَنْ صَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ فَلْيُخَفِّف، فَإِنَّ مِنْهُمُ الكَبِيرَ وَالضَّعِيفَ وَذَا الْحَاجَةِ ) رواه الشيخان وفي لفظ للبخاري: « والمريض». وفي رواية: « وإِذَا صَلَّى وَحْدَهُ فَلْيُصَلِّ كَيْفَ شَاءَ » (۳) ولحديث أنس أنــه قال: « مَا صَلَّيْتُ خَلْفَ إِمَامٍ قَط أَخَفَّ صَلاةٌ ولا أَتَمَّ صَلاةٌ مِنْ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وفي ( المضمرات ) : لا يزيد القراءة المستحبة، ولا يثقل على القوم، ولكن يخفف بعد أن يكون على التمام والاستحباب انتهى. ولكن يراعي حال من معه. كما روي أنه : ( قرأ بالمعوذتين فِي الفَجْرِ فَلَمَّا فرغ قيلَ: أَوْجَزْتَ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ بُكَاءَ صَبِي فَخَشِيتُ أَنْ تُفْتَنَ أُمُّهُ ). انتهى. فمع مراعاة حال المؤتم لا يخرج بذلك عن المسنون،
Narrations and weak hadith are acted upon in virtues of deeds. (And) it is disliked for the imam (to prolong the prayer) due to the statement of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: A man came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I can hardly catch the prayer because so-and-so prolongs it for us. I never saw the Messenger of Allah more angry in a sermon than that day. He said: O people, among you are those who cause aversion. Whoever leads the people in prayer, let him lighten it, for among them are the old, the weak, and those with needs. Reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim. In a wording of al-Bukhari: 'and the sick.' In a narration: 'And when he prays alone, let him pray as he wishes.' (3) And due to the hadith of Anas that he said: I never prayed behind an imam who was lighter in prayer nor more complete in prayer than the Messenger of Allah. And in al-Mudmarat: He should not increase the recommended recitation, nor burden the people, but should lighten while being complete and recommended. End. But he should consider the state of those with him. As it is narrated that he (the Prophet) recited al-Mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr, and when he finished, it was said: You have made it brief. He said: I heard the crying of a child and feared that his mother would be distracted. End. So by considering the state of the follower, he does not thereby deviate from the sunnah.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah. It addresses the ruling that it is makruh (disliked) for the imam to prolong the prayer for the congregation. The proof is the hadith of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari recorded by al-Bukhari and Muslim, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) expressed strong anger at those who prolong prayer and commanded lightening it, considering the elderly, weak, sick, and those with needs. Another hadith from Anas confirms that the Prophet's prayer was both light and complete. The text also cites al-Mudmarat stating that the imam should not add extra recommended recitation or burden the people, but should maintain completeness. A further incident where the Prophet shortened the prayer upon hearing a child cry shows that consideration of the congregation is paramount. The overall conclusion: as long as the imam considers the followers' conditions, he remains within the sunnah even if he shortens the prayer.

Key Terms
تطويل الصلاة (tatwil al-salah): The act of lengthening the prayer excessively, beyond what is customary or necessary, especially by the imam.
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The follower praying behind the imam, also called al-ma'mum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari, why did the Prophet (peace be upon him) become angry?
A) Because the man missed the prayer entirely.
B) Because a person prolonged the prayer excessively, causing hardship.
C) Because the imam prayed alone.
D) Because the congregation complained without reason.

Key Takeaway
It is disliked (makruh tanzih) for the imam to prolong the prayer unnecessarily; the sunnah is to lighten while maintaining completeness, considering the congregation's needs.

Disliked Congregations: Naked People and Women in Prayer
Explains the ruling on congregational prayer of naked people and women, with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on congregational prayer for naked people and women, identify the conditions for a valid female-led congregation, and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Women's congregation is disliked but valid; the female imam must stand in the middle of the row.

This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah addresses two disliked congregational prayers: one involving naked people and one involving women with a female imam. While the rulings may seem surprising, they are rooted in concerns for modesty and avoidance of fitna. The text also provides an exception for funeral prayer and specifies the proper positioning of a female imam if women do pray together.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disliked congregations
Read the text and note the two scenarios: congregation of naked people and congregation of women with a female imam. Identify the ruling (makruh tanzih) and the reasons given.
The naked congregation is disliked because of exposing awrah; women's congregation is disliked due to fitna and violation of the imam's position.
2
Examine the exception for funeral prayer
Locate the exception: funeral prayer (salat al-janaza) is not disliked for women because the prayer would be missed if only one woman prays alone.
The text says 'fawāt al-salāh bi-infirad wāḥidah bihā li-ghayrihā' meaning the prayer would be lost if one prays alone for the deceased.
3
Analyze the position of the female imam
If women form a congregation, the imam must stand in the middle of the row (wasat). The text compares this to the way Aisha and Umm Salama led women. Understand the three scenarios: advancing (sinful but valid), middle (less disliked), behind (invalid).
The condition for validity is that the follower's heel must be behind the imam's heel; if the female imam stands behind, the following is invalid.
4
Study the hadith proof
The passage cites the hadith 'Their houses are better for them' to discourage women from congregational prayer. Recognize that this is a zanni dalil (ahad hadith) and it implies preference, not prohibition.
The hadith is used as evidence for the ruling of dislike (karaha).
5
Note additional rulings
The text also mentions that a man should not lead women without a mahram, and that old women are also discouraged from attending congregational prayers.
These reinforce the general principle of seclusion (hijab) for women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) كره (جماعةُ العُرَاةِ) إذا اقتدوا بواحد منهم، ، لما فيها من إطلاع بعضهم على عورة بعض، (وَ) كره : جماعة ( النّساءِ) بإمام منهن، لأن اجتماعهن قل ما يخلوا عن فتنة، وفي قيامهن مخالفة حال الإمام، وهذا في غير صلاة الجنازة فإنها لا تكره لهن جماعة لفوات الصلاة بانفراد واحدة بها لغيرها. والتنفل بها ممتنع وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: « بيوتهنَّ خير لهنَّ لَو كُنَّ يَعْلَمُنَ) () (فإن فعلنَ) أي: أردن الصلاة جماعة بواحدة منهن يجب أن يقف الإمامُ وسَطَهُنَّ)، لما صح أن عائشة وأم سلمة لو كانتا توم النساء حين كانت جماعتهن مشروعة فتقومان كالعراة. ويقف الواحد عن يمين الإمام، والأكثر خلفَهُ.. الصف وسطهنَّ )، ولأنه أبلغ في الستر فلو تقدمت أثمت وصحت الصلاة، وإذا توسطت كــان أقل كراهة من التقدم، ولو تأخرت لم يصح الاقتداء عندنا لعدم شرطه، وهو تأخر المأموم بعقبــه عن عقب الإمام، كما قدمناه (۳) والإمام من يؤتم به أي يُقتدى به ذكراً كان أو أنثى، والوسط بالتحريك ما بين طرفي الشيء، وبالسكون لما بين بعضه عن بعض كجلست وسط الدار بالسكون. وقوله: ( كالعُرَاةِ) التشبيه من حيثية القيام في وسط الصف وأفضلية الانفراد لكل من النساء والعراة، وأما العراة فيصلون بالإيماء قعوداً، وهو أفضل والنساء قائمات، وكذلك يكـره للرجل أن يؤم النساء في بيت ليس معهن له محرم من نحو أم وأخت أو زوجة أو جارية ولا يحضرن الجماعات مطلقاً في كل الأوقات، والعجوز كالشابة في المنـع مـن حضور الجمــع والأعياد وغيرها، لأنها ممنوعة عن البروز، ولذلك كانت صلاتها في جوف بيتها أفضل من صلاتها في صحن دارها،
(And) it is disliked (congregation of naked people) if they follow one of them, because of exposing each other's private parts. (And) it is disliked: congregation of women with an imam from among them, because their gatherings are rarely free from fitna, and in their standing there is a violation of the imam's situation. This is other than the funeral prayer, for which their congregation is not disliked because of the loss of the prayer if one prays alone for others, and supererogatory prayer is prohibited. And the Prophet said: 'Their houses are better for them, if they knew.' (So if they do it) meaning: they intend to pray in congregation with one of them, it is necessary for the imam to stand in the middle of them, because it is authentic that Aisha and Umm Salama, when they led women in prayer when their congregation was prescribed, they stood like the naked. And the one (male) stands on the right of the imam, and the majority behind him. The row (for women) is in the middle of them, because it is more concealing. If she advances, she sins and the prayer is valid; if she stands in the middle, it is less disliked than advancing; if she stands behind, the following is not valid according to us because of the condition, which is that the follower's heel is behind the imam's heel, as we have presented. And the imam is the one who is followed, male or female. 'Al-wasat' (middle) with a fatha is what is between the ends of a thing, and with sukun is what is between some parts of it, like 'jalastu wasata al-dar' with sukun. And his saying: 'like the naked' is a comparison in terms of standing in the middle of the row and the superiority of praying alone for both women and the naked. As for the naked, they pray sitting with gestures, which is better, and women standing. Likewise, it is disliked for a man to lead women in prayer in a house where he has no mahram among them, such as mother, sister, wife, or slave girl, and they should not attend congregations at all at all times. The old woman is like the young woman in being prevented from attending congregations, Eid prayers, and others, because she is prohibited from appearing, and therefore her prayer in the inner part of her house is better than her prayer in the courtyard of her house.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh. It discusses two disliked congregations: (1) Naked people praying in congregation because they see each other's awrah. (2) Women praying in congregation with a female imam because of potential fitna and the violation of the imam's position (i.e., women should not be imams except in limited cases). However, for funeral prayer, it is not disliked because the benefit outweighs. If women do form a congregation, the imam must stand in the middle of them, based on the practice of Aisha and Umm Salama. The text also clarifies that if the woman imam stands ahead of the row, she sins but the prayer is valid; standing in the middle is less disliked; standing behind invalidates the following per Hanafi conditions (follower's heel behind imam's heel). The definition of 'wasat' is given. The comparison to naked people is only about standing in the middle, not about the mode of prayer (naked pray sitting, women standing). Additionally, it is disliked for a man to lead women without a mahram, and old women are also discouraged from attending congregations, as their prayer at home is better.

Key Terms
جماعة العراة (jama'at al-urāh): Group prayer of people who are naked, which is disliked because it exposes awrah.
وسط (wasat): The middle position; with fatha it means between two ends, with sukun it means among the parts. Here it refers to the imam standing in the middle of the row of women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where must a woman imam stand when leading other women in congregational prayer?
A) At the front of the row.
B) Behind the row.
C) In the middle of the row.
D) Next to a male mahram.

Key Takeaway
Women's congregation is makruh tanzih in Hanafi fiqh; if performed, the female imam must stand in the middle of the row, and funeral prayer is an exception.

Positioning of Followers in Congregational Prayer
Ruling with proof on follower positioning in congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah positions for followers in congregational prayer and identify which position is disliked according to the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
One follower stands on the imam's right; many stand behind; women stand behind everyone.

The placement of followers around the imam is not arbitrary; it follows prophetic practice with specific rulings. This lesson clarifies the sunnah positions for men, women, and boys, and settles an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether standing directly behind the imam alone is disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled (positioning of followers) and the hukm level (sunnah, disliked, permissible).
The text explicitly states 'hādhihi al-sunnah' for standing on the right.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: hadith of Ibn Abbas (standing on right) and the practice with Anas and the orphan (standing behind for multiple).
The text provides two proofs: one for the individual case, one for the collective.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each hadith yields the ruling: Ibn Abbas shows the sunnah is to stand on the right; the Prophet's action with Anas and the orphan shows the sunnah for multiple is behind.
The text says 'dalīl al-afḍaliyya' for the multiple case, indicating preference.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute: is it disliked for one follower to stand behind the imam? One narration says no, another says yes, and the latter is correct.
The text resolves with 'wa huwa al-ṣaḥīḥ'.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the 'disliked' view is relied upon (mufta bihi). The text gives weight to the hadith evidence and declares it correct.
No further tarjih authority is cited; the text itself chooses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقف الواحد) إذا لم يكن ثَمَّ غيره ( عن يمين الإمام) مساوياً له متأخراً بعقبه عقبه، هكذا السنة لحديث ابن عباس : « إِنَّه قَامَ عَنْ يَسَارِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَقَامَهُ عن يمينه » (۳). ويكره: عن أن يقف عن يساره، لما روينا، ولا يكره أن يقف خلفه، في رواية ويكره في أخرى وهو الصحيح، والصبي في القيام كالبالغ، ولا تكون المرأة إلا خلفه، بحيث لا تحاذي شيئاً منـــه، فـلـو كــان مـعـه رجل أيضاً يقيمه عن يمينه والمرأة خلفهما، (وَ) يقف (الأكثرُ) مــن واحـد (خلفه)، لأنـه عليـه الصلاة والسلام « تَقَدَّم عَنْ أَنَسِ واليتيم حينَ صَلَّى بِهما ) وهو دليل الأفضلية، وما ورد مـن قـول ابن مسعود الله من القيام بينهما (ه) فهو دليل الإباحة،...
And the one (follower) – if there is no other – stands (on the right of the imam), equal to him, with his heel behind the imam's heel. This is the sunnah, due to the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'He stood on the left of the Prophet, and the Prophet moved him to his right.' (3) And it is disliked for him to stand on his left, according to what we narrated. And it is not disliked for him to stand behind him, in one narration, and it is disliked in another, and that is the correct one. The boy in standing is like the adult. And the woman is only behind him, such that she does not align with anything of him. So if there is also a man, he places him on his right and the woman behind them. (And) the majority (more than one) stand (behind him), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) advanced (himself) above Anas and the orphan when he prayed with them, and that is evidence of preference. And what is reported from Ibn Mas'ud about standing between the two is evidence of permissibility...
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the positioning of followers in congregational prayer. For a single male follower, the sunnah is to stand on the imam's right, level with him, with his heel slightly behind. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas. It is disliked to stand on the left, but there is a difference of opinion on standing behind: one narration says it is not disliked, another says it is disliked, and the latter is correct. Boys are treated like adults. Women must stand entirely behind the imam, not even aligning with him. If there is both a man and a woman, the man stands on the right and the woman behind. For multiple followers (two or more), they stand behind the imam, as the Prophet did with Anas and the orphan. Ibn Mas'ud's practice of standing between two people shows permissibility but is not preferred.

Key Terms
يمين الإمام (yamin al-imam): The right side of the imam; the preferred position for a single male follower.
الأكثر (al-akthar): More than one follower (two or more), who should stand behind the imam.
الصحيح (al-ṣaḥīḥ): The correct opinion, used to settle the dispute on standing behind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct ruling (mufta bihi) regarding a single male follower standing behind the imam when there is space on the right?
A) It is obligatory to stand behind.
B) It is not disliked, according to all narrations.
C) It is disliked (makruh).
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
For a single male follower, the sunnah is to stand on the imam's right; standing behind is disliked in the mufta bihi view; multiple followers and women have distinct positions.

Positioning of Followers in Congregational Prayer
Rulings on follower positions in jama'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on where a single male, multiple males, and women stand relative to the imam in congregational prayer, and apply the condition that the follower's heel must be behind the imam's heel.

Core Idea
A single male stands to the imam's right; multiple men stand behind; women stand behind all men.

The placement of followers in jama'ah is governed by specific sunnah practices derived from the Prophet's ﷺ actions. This lesson unpacks the rulings for different congregational compositions: one man, several men, and women. Understanding these positions ensures the prayer follows the established sunnah and avoids disliked or invalid arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the composition of the congregation: single male, multiple males, women, or mixed.
The ruling differs based on who is present.
2
Recall the sunnah position for a single male
For a single male, the sunnah is to stand to the right of the imam, level with him, with his heel behind the imam's heel.
Proof: Hadith of Ibn 'Abbas (Bukhari, Muslim).
3
Apply the ruling for multiple males
When there are two or more male followers, they should stand behind the imam in rows. This is preferred (afdal), not obligatory.
Based on the hadith of Anas and the orphan.
4
Determine the position for women
Women must stand behind all men, not aligning with the imam. If a woman advances, her prayer is valid but she sins. Standing in the middle of the women's row is less disliked than advancing. If she stands behind, the prayer is invalid because the condition of being behind the imam is lost.
The condition for valid following: the follower's heel must be behind the imam's heel.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For a single male, there is a difference: is it disliked to stand behind the imam? The correct (sahih) position is that it is disliked. The boy is treated like an adult.
The text says 'wa huwa al-sahih'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالعراة. ويقف الواحد عن يمين الإمام، والأكثر خلفَهُ.. الصف وسط هنَّ ) ()، ولأنه أبلغ في الستر فلو تقدمت أثمت وصحت الصلاة، وإذا توسطت كــان أقل كراهة من التقدم، ولو تأخرت لم يصح الاقتداء عندنا لعدم شرطه، وهو تأخر المأموم بعقبــه عن عقب الإمام، كما قدمناه (۳) والإمام من يؤتم به أي يُقتدى به ذكراً كان أو أنثى، والوسط بالتحريك ما بين طرفي الشيء، وبالسكون لما بين بعضه عن بعض كجلست وسط الدار بالسكون. وقوله: ( كالعُرَاةِ) التشبيه من حيثية القيام في وسط الصف وأفضلية الانفراد لكل من النساء والعراة، وأما العراة فيصلون بالإيماء قعوداً، وهو أفضل والنساء قائمات، وكذلك يكـره للرجل أن يؤم النساء في بيت ليس معهن له محرم من نحو أم وأخت أو زوجة أو جارية ولا يحضرن الجماعات مطلقاً في كل الأوقات، والعجوز كالشابة في المنـع مـن حضر الجمــع والأعياد وغيرها، لأنها ممنوعة عن البروز، ولذلك كانت صلاتها في جوف بيتها أفضل من صلاتها في صحن دارها، (ويقف الواحد) إذا لم يكن ثَمَّ غيره ( عن يمين الإمام) مساوياً له متأخراً بعقبه عقبه، هكذا السنة لحديث ابن عباس : « إِنَّه قَامَ عَنْ يَسَارِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَقَامَهُ عن يمينه » (۳). ويكره: عن أن يقف عن يساره، لما روينا، ولا يكره أن يقف خلفه، في رواية ويكره في أخرى وهو الصحيح، والصبي في القيام كالبالغ، ولا تكون المرأة إلا خلفه، بحيث لا تحاذي شيئاً منـــه، فـلـو كــان مـعـه رجل أيضاً يقيمه عن يمينه والمرأة خلفهما، (وَ) يقف (الأكثرُ) مــن واحـد (خلفه)، لأنـه عليـه الصلاة والسلام « تَقَدَّم عَنْ أَنَسِ واليتيم حينَ صَلَّى بِهما ) وهو دليل الأفضلية، وما ورد مـن قـول ابن مسعود الله من القيام بينهما (ه) فهو دليل الإباحة،
Like the naked. And the single [male] stands to the right of the imam, and the majority behind him... The row [of women] is in the middle of them, because it is more covering. So if she [a woman] advances, she sins but her prayer is valid; if she stands in the middle, it is less disliked than advancing; if she delays, the following is not valid according to us due to lack of its condition, which is that the follower's heel is behind the imam's heel, as we presented. And the imam is the one who is followed, male or female. 'Al-wasat' with fath is between the two ends; with sukun is between parts of a thing, like 'I sat in the middle (wasat) of the house'. And His statement: 'like the naked' is a comparison in terms of standing in the middle of the row and the preference of individual prayer for both women and the naked. As for the naked, they pray sitting with gestures, which is better, while women pray standing. Similarly, it is disliked for a man to lead women in a house where there is no mahram for him among them, such as mother, sister, wife, or slave-girl. And they [women] should not attend congregations at all in all times. The old woman is like the young woman in prohibition from attending gatherings, Eid prayers, and others, because she is prevented from appearing. Therefore, her prayer in the inner part of her house is better than her prayer in the courtyard of her house. (And the single [male] stands) if there is no other (to the right of the imam) equal to him, his heel behind the imam's heel. This is the sunnah according to the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'He stood to the left of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he moved him to his right.' And it is disliked for him to stand to his left, based on what we narrated. And it is not disliked for him to stand behind him, in one narration, and disliked in another, which is the correct one. The boy in standing is like the adult. And the woman is only behind him, such that she does not align with any part of him. So if there is also a man with him, he stands him to his right and the woman behind both. (And) the majority (more than one) stand (behind him), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'went forward ahead of Anas and the orphan when he prayed with them,' and this is evidence of preference. And what is narrated from the saying of Ibn Mas'ud about standing between them is evidence of permissibility.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings regarding the positioning of followers in congregational prayer (salah al-jama'ah). It covers several distinct scenarios: when the congregation consists only of women, when there is a single male follower, multiple male followers, and when both men and women are present. The commentary begins by comparing the placement of women in their rows to that of naked men (al-urāh) in theirs—both should stand in the middle of their row, as it provides the best cover. For women, standing in the middle of the row is more concealing than advancing; if they advance, they sin but their prayer remains valid. The preferred position is the middle; standing behind is invalid because the condition of the follower being behind the imam is not met. The imam can be male or female, but a woman leading men is disliked unless she is a mahram. Women are prohibited from attending congregational prayers entirely, regardless of age; the old woman is like the young in this prohibition. A woman's prayer in the innermost part of her house is superior to prayer in her courtyard. For a single male follower, the sunnah is to stand to the right of the imam, level with him, with his heel behind the imam's heel, as proven by the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas. It is disliked to stand on the left, and there is a difference of opinion on standing behind—the correct view is that it is disliked. A boy is treated like an adult in this ruling. A woman must stand behind the imam, not aligning with him. If there is both a man and a woman, the man stands to the right and the woman behind both. When there are multiple followers (more than one), they stand behind the imam. This is based on the hadith of Anas and the orphan, where the Prophet advanced ahead of them, indicating preference. Ibn Mas'ud's practice of having followers stand on both sides indicates permissibility. The commentary explains that the ruling for multiple followers is one of preference (afdaliyyah), not obligation.

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): With fatha (wasat) means the middle of something; with sukun (wasṭ) means between parts.
العراة (al-ʿurāh): Naked people who pray in congregation due to lack of covering.
المأموم (al-ma'mūm): The follower in prayer, one who prays behind an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should a single male follower stand if there is no other male present?
A) To the imam's right
B) To the imam's left
C) Behind the imam
D) Anywhere in the first row

Key Takeaway
The sunnah for a single male follower is to stand to the right of the imam; multiple males stand behind; women must stand behind all men.

Ordering Rows in Congregational Prayer
Ruling with proofs for row arrangement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of rows in congregational prayer and identify the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
Men of understanding come first, then others; rows must be straight and compact.

In congregational prayer, the arrangement of rows reflects the importance of order and discipline. This passage from Nur al-Idah explains the sunnah of placing men of understanding (ahlām wa al-nuhā) near the imam, followed by others, and emphasizes straightening rows to prevent gaps that allow shaytan to enter. We will analyze the key proofs and rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
State the ruling on row order: men of understanding (adult males with sound intellect) should be placed in the first rows behind the imam.
This is based on the hadith command 'liyalnī minkum ulū al-ahlām wa al-nuhā'.
2
Examine the proof for straightening rows
Review the hadith from al-Barā' ibn 'Āzib that commands straightening rows, aligning necks, and filling gaps.
Multiple narrations support this; the command is taken as sunnah muakkadah.
3
Understand the wisdom behind row arrangement
Reflect on the reasons: those of understanding are more attentive and can follow the imam; straight rows prevent discord and block shaytan.
The hadith warns that differing in rows causes differences in hearts.
4
Identify the secondary rulings
Note the additional sunan: the imam should instruct the congregation, they should be compact, fill gaps, align shoulders, and make room for newcomers.
These are derived from the same hadith corpus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُصَفُ الرّجالُ. (1) اليتيم" هو أخو أنس من أمه اسمه عمير بن سليم بفتح السين وباللام. تنبيه: فضل تعمير ميسرة المسجد لما رواه الجلال السيوطي في ( الجامع الصغير » قال : من عمر ميسرة المسجدِ كتب الله له كفلين من الأجر » (" ). (و) إذا اجتمع الرجال وغيرهم، (يُصَفُ الرّجالُ) خلف الإمام؛ لقوله : ( لِيَلِنِي مِنْكُمْ أُولُو الأحْلامِ، وَالنَّهَى ) (۳) قوله « ليلني ) أمر للغائب من الولي، وهو القريب بكسر اللام وحذف الياء بـيـن اللام والنون والأحلام: جمع حلم بضم الحاء واللام، وهو ما يراه النائم أريد به البالغون مجازاً؛ لأن الحلم سبب البلوغ، والنهى: جمع نهية وهي: العقل باعتبار أن العقل يمنع وينهى عن الأشياء الضارة في الدين، وينبغي للإمام أن يأمرهم بذلك، ويتراصوا ويسدوا الخلل، ويســـوا بـيـن مناكبهم، ويلينوها للداخل بينهم في الصف، لقول البراء بن عازب كان رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَأْتِينَا إِذَا أَقيمتِ الصَّلاةُ فيمسح عواتقنـا ويقول: « أقيموا صفوفكم، ولا تختلفُوا فتختلف قلوبكم، ولِيَلِنِي مِنْكُمْ أُولُو الأحلام، وَالنَّهَى ) وقوله : ( سَرُّوا صفوفكم، وقارِبُوا بَيْنَها ، وحاذوا بالأعناق فوالذي نفسي بِيَدِهِ، إِنِّي لأرَى الشَّيْطَانَ يدخُلُ مِنْ خَلَلِ الصَّفِّ كَأَنَّهَا الحذفُ » (٥) أي: كـأن الشياطين: الحذف بالتحريك: غنم سود صغار من غنم الحجاز الواحدة: حذفة. كذا في ( الصحاح»، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( أتموا الصَّفَّ المقدَّم، ثم الذي يليه، فمَا كَانَ مِن نقص فليكن في الصف المؤخر » ) رواه أبو داود، ولقول البراء كان النبي لا يأتي ناحية الصف فيساوي بين صدور القوم ومناكبهم ويقول: لا تَخْتَلِفُوا فَتَخْتَلِفَ قلوبكم إِنَّ الله وملائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى الصَّفِّ الأوَّلِ » ) رواه ابن خزيمة في صحيحه وقوله : ( استووا تستوي قلوبكم، وتماسوا تَرَاحَمُوا » رواه الطبراني.
The men are arranged. (1) The orphan is the maternal brother of Anas, his name is 'Umayr ibn Sulaym, with fatḥ on the sīn and lām. Note: The virtue of populating the left side of the mosque, as narrated by al-Suyuti in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Whoever populates the left side of the mosque, Allah will write for him two rewards.' And when men and others gather, (the men are arranged) behind the imam, due to his saying: 'Let those of you who are men of understanding and wisdom be near me.' His saying 'liyalnī' is a command to the absent from al-waī, meaning close, with kasr of the lām and deletion of the yā between the lām and nūn. 'Al-ahlām' is plural of 'hulm' (dream), meaning here adults metaphorically because dreaming is a cause of puberty. 'Al-nuhā' is plural of 'nuhya' meaning intellect, because intellect prevents one from harmful things in religion. The imam should command them to do that, to be compact, fill gaps, align shoulders, and make room for those entering the row, according to the saying of al-Barā' ibn 'Āzib: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to come to us when the prayer was established, wipe our shoulders, and say: Straighten your rows, do not differ lest your hearts differ, and let those of you who are men of understanding and wisdom be near me.' And his saying: 'Straighten your rows, bring them close together, and align necks. By Him in whose hand my soul is, I see the devil entering through the gaps of the row like small black sheep.' That is, the devils are like al-ḥudhuf (small black sheep of Hijaz). And his saying (peace be upon him): 'Complete the front row, then the one after it; whatever deficiency remains should be in the last row' – narrated by Abu Dawud. And the saying of al-Barā': 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to come to the side of the row and make the chests and shoulders equal and say: Do not differ lest your hearts differ; indeed Allah and His angels send blessings upon the first row' – narrated by Ibn Khuzaymah. And his saying: 'Be straight so that your hearts become straight, and be in contact so that you have mercy' – narrated by al-Tabarani.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer when men, children, and women are present. It begins by stating that men are arranged first, behind the imam. The text then provides a brief note on the identity of the orphan mentioned in the earlier hadith (Umayr ibn Sulaym, maternal brother of Anas). A note follows on the virtue of populating the left side of the mosque, citing al-Suyuti. The main ruling is that when men and others (i.e., children and women) are present, men are arranged behind the imam, based on the Prophet's command: 'Let those of you who are men of understanding and wisdom be near me.' The commentary explains the key words: 'liyalnī' (come near me) is a command; 'al-ahlām' (dreams) refers to adults metaphorically because majority (bulugh) generally occurs through dreams (ihtilam); 'al-nuhā' (intellect) refers to those with sound mind. The imam should instruct the congregation to be compact, fill gaps, align their shoulders, and make space for newcomers. Multiple hadith are cited to support the straightening of rows: from al-Barā' ibn 'Āzib, the Prophet would straighten rows and emphasize not differing; from the Prophet comparing gaps in rows to holes through which the devil enters, like small black sheep (al-ḥudhuf); the command to complete the front rows first; the blessing of Allah and angels upon the first row; and the command to be straight and close together for mutual mercy. These hadith collectively establish the sunnah of row straightening and the order of rows: men of understanding first, then others.

Key Terms
الأحلام (al-aḥlām): Plural of hulm (dream); metaphorically means adults who have reached puberty through dreams.
النهى (al-nuhā): Plural of nuhya meaning intellect; those who have wisdom and refrain from harm.
الحذف (al-ḥudhuf): Small black sheep of Hijaz; used in hadith to describe the devil or his resemblance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'Let those of you who are men of understanding and wisdom be near me' indicate about row arrangement?
A) It is obligatory (fard) to place only scholars in the first row
B) It is sunnah to place mature, intelligent men in the first rows
C) It is permissible for anyone to stand anywhere
D) It is only for the Prophet's time

Key Takeaway
In congregational prayer, it is sunnah muakkadah to place men of understanding near the imam and to straighten rows, based on multiple authentic hadith.

Arranging Rows in Congregational Prayer: Rulings and Etiquettes
Commentary on ruling that men occupy front rows with hadith proofs and etiquettes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on row arrangement, identify the key hadith proofs, and apply the etiquettes of straightening rows and filling gaps.

Core Idea
Arranging men in front rows and straightening rows is a commanded sunnah; gaps invite Shaytan.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on the ruling that men are arranged in rows behind the imam. It provides multiple hadith proofs emphasizing the importance of straight rows, closing gaps, and making room for others. The commentary also refutes a misconception that moving to accommodate someone invalidates the prayer, clarifying that such action is obedience to Allah and His Messenger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Evidence
Find the opening statement 'يُصَفُ الرّجالُ' and the hadith 'لِيَلِنِي مِنْكُمْ أُولُو الأَحْلامِ وَالنَّهَى'. Note that the ruling is that men occupy the front rows, and the command indicates strong recommendation (sunnah muakkadah).
The hadith is from Muslim and others.
2
Understand the Linguistic Explanation
The commentator explains key words: 'لِيَلِنِي' (command to be near), 'أُولُو الأَحْلامِ' (mature men), 'النَّهَى' (intellect). This shows the preference for mature, sensible men in front.
The imperative form implies emphasis.
3
List the Prophetic Etiquettes
From the hadith cited, extract the commands: straighten rows, align shoulders, fill gaps, make room for those entering, and close the front row first.
These are considered sunnah muakkadah.
4
Analyze the Refutation of Misconception
The passage addresses a view from 'Majma' al-Riwāyāt' that moving for someone invalidates prayer. The commentator refutes using hadith: slight movement does not break prayer, and one is obeying Allah's command to close gaps.
The refutation is based on text (hadith) overriding weak reasoning.
5
Apply the Rulings on Pulling and Order
If there is a gap in the first row but not the second, one may step back. If fearing loss of rak'ah, a knowledgeable person may be pulled forward after takbir.
In desert prayer, sequence matters: takbir first, then pull.

(و) إذا اجتمع الرجال وغيرهم، (يُصَفُ الرّجالُ) خلف الإمام؛ لقوله : ( لِيَلِنِي مِنْكُمْ أُولُو

(۱) تنبيه: قال الإمام العيني في شرحه على الصحيح: اليتيم هو ضميرة بن أبي ضميرة وأبو ضميرة مولى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ومن هنا تبين السهو في نسبة اليتيم إلى أخي أنس بن مالك من أمه. ا.هـ العمدة (٣٣٩/٣).
(۲) أخرجه ابن ماجه في إقامة الصلاة، باب فضل ميمنة الصف (۱۰۰۷) ، والسيوطي في الجامع الصغير (۸۸۹۱).
(۳) أخرجه مسلم في الصلاة، باب تسوية الصفوف وإقامتها (٤۳۲)، والترمذي في الصلاة، باب ما جاء ليلني منكم أولوا الأحلام والنهى (۲۲۸).
(٤) أخرجه مسلم في الصلاة، باب: تسوية الصفوف (٤٣٢)، وأبو داود في الصلاة، باب: تسوية الصفوف (٦٦٤).
(٥) أخرجه أحمد في مسنده (٢٦٠/٣)، وابن خزيمة في صحيحه (۲۲/۳).
(٦) أخرجه أبو داود في الصلاة، باب تسوية الصفوف (٦٧١) ، وأحمد في مسنده (۲۳۳/۳).
(۷) أخرجه ابن خزيمة في صحيحه (٢٤/٣)، وأبو داود في الصلاة، باب: تسوية الصفوف (٦٦٤).
(۸) أخرجه الطبراني في الأوسط (٢١٤/٥)، وذكره الهيثمي في مجمع الزوائد (٩٠/٢).
وقوله : ( أقِيمُوا الصَّفُوفَ وَحَاذُوا بَيْنَ الْمَنَاكِبِ وَسُدُّوا الْخَلَلَ وَلِينُوا بِأَيْدِي إِخْوَانِكُمْ وَلَا تَذَرُوا فُرُجَاتِ لِلشَّيْطَان مَنْ وَصَلَ صَفًّا وَصَلَهُ اللَّهُ وَمَنْ قَطَعَ صَفًّا قَطَعَهُ اللَّهُ » (۱) وقوله : (خيارُكُم ألينُكُمْ مناكِبَ في الصَّلاةِ » ("). رواه أبو داود كذا في « البرهان». تنبيه: أشرنا بما رويناه إلى ما قاله « صاحب البحر » ، وبهذا يعلم جهل من يستمسك عنـد دخــول داخل بجنبه في الصف، ويظن أن فسحه له رياء، بسبب أنه يتحرك لأجله، بل ذلك إعانة لـه علـى إدراك الفضيلة وإقامة لسد الفرجات المأمور بها في الصف، والأحاديث في هذا كثيرة شهيرة انتهى. وهـو يـشـيـر إلى رد ما قال في مجمع الروايات » ، وفي كتاب ( المتجانس » : لو قيل لمصل: تقدم، فتقدم أو دخل فرجة الصف أحد فتجانب المصلي توسعة له فسدت صلاته، لأنه امتثل أمر غير ) الله تعالى في الصلاة، وينبغي أن يمكث ساعة، ثم يتقدم برأيه انتهى لأنه تعليل في مقابلة النص، وليس فيه عمل كثير ومجرد الحركة الواحدة كالمرتين لا تفسد به الصلاة، والامتثال إنما هو امتثال لأمر الله تعالى ورسوله. تنبيه: روينا « أَنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى الصَّفِّ الأَوَّلِ ) (۳)، وقال في « القنية : القيام في الصف الأول أفضل من الثاني، وفي الثاني أفضل من الثالث، وهكذا لأنه روي في الأخبار « أن الله تعالى إذا أنزل الرحمة على الجماعة ينزلها أولاً على الإمام، ثم تتجاوز عنه إلى من يحاذيه في الصف الأول، ثم إلى الميامن، ثم إلى المياسر ، ثم إلى الصف الثاني ) (4) ، وروي عنـه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام أنه قال: ( يكتب للذي خَلْفَ الإمام بحذَائِهِ مَانَةُ صَلاة، وللذي في الجانب الأيمن خمسة وسبعون صلاة، وللذي في الأيسر خمسون صلاة، وللذي في سائر الصفوف خمسة وعشرون صلاة» (ه)، وإذا وجد فرجة في الصف الأول دون الثاني، فـلـه فـرق الثاني؛ لأنه لا حرمــــة لهـم لتقصيرهم، حيث لم يسدوا الصف الأول، ولو كان الصف منتظماً انتظر مجئ آخر، فإن خاف فــوت الركعة جذب واحداً من الصف إليه، إن علم أنه لا يتأذى، وهو من أهل العلم، فلو كان في الصحراء ينبغي أن يكبر أولاً ثم يجذبه، فلو جذبه أولاً فتأخر ثم كبر هو، قيل: تفسد صلاة الذي تأخر،
(1) أخرجه أبو داود في الصلاة، باب تسوية الصفوف (٦٦٦) ، وأحمد في مسنده (۹۷/۲).
(۲) أخرجه أبو داود في الصلاة، باب: تسوية الصفوف (٦٧٢)، والبيهقي في السنن الكبرى (١٠١/٣).
(۳) ص (۳۲۳).
(٤) لم أهتد إليه فيما بين يدي من كتب الحديث وإنما ورد في الكتب الفقهية منها ( البحر الرائق) (٣٧٥/١).
(٥) لم أهتدِ إليه فيما بين يدي من كتب الحديث وإنما ورد في الكتب الفقهية منها ( البحر الرائق) (٣٧٥/١).
Men are arranged (in rows). (1) The orphan: He is the brother of Anas from his mother, named Umair bin Sulaim... (And) When men and others gather, men are arranged behind the Imam; because of his saying: 'Let those of you who are mature and sensible stand nearest to me...'
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that men should be arranged in the front rows of congregational prayer, behind the Imam. The author begins by stating the ruling: 'Men are arranged.' Then a footnote identifies an orphan mentioned in a previous context. The main discussion then proceeds: when men and others (women, children) gather, men are placed in rows behind the Imam. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let those of you who are mature and sensible stand nearest to me.' The commentator explains the words: 'līlīnī' is a command, 'ulū al-ahlām' means adults (because dreams are associated with puberty), and 'al-nuhā' means intellect. The Imam should command the congregation to straighten rows, fill gaps, align shoulders, and make room for those entering the row. Several hadith are cited to emphasize straightening rows and closing gaps. The passage then addresses a misconception: some people think that making room for someone entering the row is riyā' (showing off), but it is actually an act of obedience to Allah and His Messenger. It refutes a view from 'Majma' al-Riwāyāt' that moving for someone invalidates the prayer; rather, slight movement does not break the prayer, and one is acting upon the command to close gaps. The passage continues with virtues of the first row and the right side, then discusses the ruling if there is a gap in the first row: it is permissible to skip to the second row if the first row is incomplete. If one fears losing the rak'ah, he may pull someone from the row towards him, provided the person is a knowledgeable person who will not be offended. In the desert, the one pulling should first say takbīr and then pull. If he pulls first and then says takbīr, some say the prayer of the one being pulled is invalidated.

Key Terms
صَف (saff): A row in congregational prayer, specifically referring to the line of worshippers behind the imam.
لِيَلِنِي (līlīnī): Command meaning 'let him be near to me' or 'stand closest to me'.
فُرْجَة (furjah): A gap or opening in the row of worshippers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a person do if he finds a gap in the first row but the second row is already full?
A) He should remain standing and wait for someone to pull him forward.
B) He should step back to the second row if the first row has a gap.
C) He should immediately pull someone from the second row into the first row.
D) He should pray alone behind the rows.

Key Takeaway
Arranging men in front rows and straightening rows is a sunnah muakkadah; making room for others to fill gaps is obedience to the Prophet, not a violation.

Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer: Men, Boys, Hermaphrodites, Women
Ruling on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer with proof and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of rows in congregational prayer and explain the reasoning behind the placement of boys and hermaphrodites, including the precautionary rules for alignment.

Core Idea
The row order is men, boys, hermaphrodites, women — a sunnah based on prophetic practice.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the recommended arrangement of worshippers in congregational prayer. While the order is a confirmed sunnah, the commentator also addresses nuanced issues such as the treatment of hermaphrodites and the conditions under which alignment invalidates prayer. Understanding this hierarchy helps maintain proper etiquette (adab) and validity in congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence
List the four categories in the prescribed order: men, boys, hermaphrodites, women. The text states: 'Then the boys, then the hermaphrodites, then the women.'
The front row is always for men; the following rows are for boys, then hermaphrodites, then women.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites the hadith of Abu Malik al-Ash'ari and the Musnad of al-Harith. These narrations describe the Prophet (peace be upon him) arranging the rows in this order.
The proof is a hadith ahad, so it establishes a sunnah, not an obligation.
3
Understand the khuntha rules
The 'khuntha' (hermaphrodite) refers to a person with ambiguous gender. The commentator advises caution: the khuntha is placed behind boys. To avoid invalidating alignment (muḥādhāh), khunthas must stand in a single row with gaps or barriers between them.
Alignment between two khunthas is considered potentially invalid because it is unclear if they are of the same gender.
4
Distinguish sunnah from fard
The order is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), not fard. However, alignment between a man and a woman in the same row invalidates the prayer. The commentator stresses that following the order avoids this risk.
Missing the sunnah order does not invalidate prayer, but deliberate misalignment may.
5
Note the contemporary consideration
The commentator recommends that a person stand alone in prayer in our time due to widespread ignorance. This prevents misunderstandings when others pull or push, which could lead to actions that break the prayer.
This is a practical concession, not a change in the sunnah order.

Source Text
