ثم الصبيانُ، ثمَّ الخَنَائي، ثمَّ النِّسَاءُ. والأصح أنها لا تفسد، والقيام وحده في زماننا أولى؛ لغلبة الجهل فربما إذا جذبه يظن أمراً غـيـر مـا أراده الجاذب فيفعل ما يبطل صلاته.
تنبيه: هذه المسألة تناقض القول بفساد صلاة من تقدم أو فسح بأمر الداخل لجنبه، وتؤيد مـا ذكرنا من عدم صحة القول بفساد الصلاة بامتثال أمره؛ لأن تأخير المجذوب بقدر ما يقـف مـع الجاذب أقوى وأكثر فعلاً من مجرد تليين منكبه، وفسحه للداخل بجانبه أو تقدمه خطوة أو خطوتين، (ثُمَّ) يصف (الصبيانُ) لقول أبي مالك الأشعري أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ( صَلَّى وَقَامَ الرِّجَالُ يَلونَهُ، وأقام الصبيانَ خَلْفَ ذَلِكَ، وأقامَ النِّساء خَلْفَ ذَلِكَ، وإنْ لَمْ يَكُن جمع مِنَ الصَّبيانِ يقومُ الصبي بَينَ الرِّجَالِ » (۱) (ثمَّ الخَنَاثَى): جمع خنثى، والمراد به المشكل احتياطاً في الأمر؛ لأن الخنثى المشكل إن كان رجلاً فقيامه خلف الصبيان لا يضره، وإن كان امرأة فهو متأخر. تنبيه: أطلق المشايخ في صلاة الخنثى خلف الإمام، ولم أر من شرط لصحة اقتدائه نـيــة الإمامة وكذلك أطلقوا في اصطفاف الخناثى، ولم يشترطوا عدم المحاذاة ، ولا كونه خلف مثله في كثير من المعتبرات، ولعلهم اتكلوا في ذلك على ما هو المشتهر من معاملة الخنثـى بـالأضر في أحواله، وهو مستلزم فساد صلاته بمحاذاة مثله وبتأخره خلف مثله؛ لاحتمال أنوثة المتقدم والمحاذي، وعدم صحة صلاته إذا لم ينو الإمام إمامته كالنساء، والصفوف الممكنة عقلاً في الخناثى ممتنعة شرعاً؛ لعدم صحة القيام خلف مثله، فيشترط أن يكون الخناثي صفاً واحداً بـيـن كل اثنين فرجة أو حائل ليمنع المحاذاة، وهذا مما من الله بالتنبه له، (ثُمَّ ) يصف (النساء) لما رويـنـا", وفي مسند الحارث كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ( يصفهم في الصلاة فيجعــل الرجـال قـدام الـغـلـمـان، والـغـلمــان خـلـفـهـم، والنساء خلف الغلمان» (۳) وسنذكر مسألة المحاذاة في المفسدات (4).
Then the boys, then the hermaphrodites, then the women. And the correct view is that it does not invalidate, and standing alone in our time is better due to the prevalence of ignorance, for perhaps if he pulls him, he may think something other than what the puller intended and thus do something that invalidates his prayer. Note: This issue contradicts the saying that the prayer of one who steps forward or makes room for the entrant by his side is invalidated, and supports what we mentioned that the saying that the prayer is invalidated by obeying his command is not correct; because the delay of the one being pulled to the extent that he stands with the puller is stronger and involves more action than merely softening his shoulder, or making room for the entrant by his side, or stepping forward one or two steps. Then he arranges the boys due to the statement of Abu Malik al-Ash'ari that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed and the men stood next to him, and he placed the boys behind that, and he placed the women behind that, and if there is no group of boys, a boy stands among the men. Then the hermaphrodites: plural of khuntha, and what is meant here is the ambiguous case as a precaution in the matter; because if the ambiguous khuntha is a man, then his standing behind the boys does not harm him, and if he is a woman, he is behind. Note: The mashayikh have spoken generally about the prayer of the khuntha behind the imam, and I have not seen anyone condition for the validity of his following that the imam intend imamate, and similarly they spoke generally about the lining up of khunathas, and they did not condition the absence of alignment, nor that he be behind someone like him in many of the considered matters. Perhaps they relied on what is well-known of treating the khuntha with the more harmful in his situations, which necessitates the invalidity of his prayer if he aligns with someone like him, and if he stays behind someone like him, due to the possibility that the one ahead or aligned is female, and the invalidity of his prayer if the imam does not intend his imamate, as for women. And the rows that are rationally possible for khunathas are legally prevented, due to the invalidity of standing behind someone like him. So it is required that the khunathas be in one row with a gap or barrier between every two to prevent alignment. This is something for which I thank Allah for drawing attention to. Then he arranges the women due to what we narrated, and in the Musnad of al-Harith: The Prophet (peace be upon him) would arrange them in prayer, placing the men in front of the boys, the boys behind them, and the women behind the boys. And we will mention the issue of alignment in the invalidators.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer. It states the order: men, then boys (sibyan), then hermaphrodites (khunatha), then women. The commentator notes that the correct view is that prayer is not invalidated by certain actions like pulling. He then discusses a hadith from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari regarding the row order. A significant portion is dedicated to the khuntha (hermaphrodite). The commentator explains that 'khunatha' here refers to the ambiguous case (mushkil). He points out that the early scholars did not condition that the imam must intend imamate for the khuntha's prayer to be valid, nor did they condition absence of alignment. However, the commentator argues that treating the khuntha with the more harmful (al-ḍarar) necessitates invalidation if he aligns with another khuntha, so they must stand in a single row with gaps. Finally, he cites a hadith from Musnad al-Harith for the order of women. The passage ends by noting that the issue of alignment will be discussed later in the section on invalidators.

Key Terms
الصبيان (al-sibyān): Boys who have reached the age of discretion but not yet puberty, or young boys in general.
الخنثى (al-khunthā): A person with ambiguous gender characteristics; here specifically the 'mushkil' (difficult) case where gender is unclear.
المحاذاة (al-muḥādhāh): Standing in alignment (shoulder to shoulder) with another person; in this context, it invalidates the prayer when one of the same gender aligns with another behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct order of rows in congregational prayer?
A) Men, then women, then children
B) Men, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women
C) Men, then hermaphrodites, then boys, then women
D) Women, then men, then boys

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of rows is a sunnah based on prophetic practice, with specific precautions for hermaphrodites to avoid alignment invalidation.

Completing Tashahhud and Following the Imam: Rulings for the Follower
Rulings on follower's actions after imam completes an obligatory act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for a follower when the imam completes an obligatory act before the follower finishes tashahhud or tasbihat, and distinguish between cases where following the imam takes precedence.

Core Idea
Following the imam (muta'aba) is fard; tashahhud is wajib (must be completed); tasbihat are sunnah (can be left for fard).

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its sharh lays out several scenarios a follower may face after the imam completes an obligatory part of the prayer. Two key principles govern these rulings: the obligation to follow the imam (muta'aba) and the requirement to complete wajib acts like tashahhud. The text explains how to resolve conflicts between these principles, such as when the imam says salam before the follower finishes tashahhud, or when the imam raises his head before the follower completes the tasbihat. We will work through each scenario step by step, understanding the proofs and the preferred Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what act the follower is engaged in (e.g., tashahhud, tasbihat) and the ruling of completing it (wajib, sunnah). Also identify the imam's action (salam, raising head, adding sajdah).
Key: tashahhud is wajib, tasbihat are sunnah, following imam (muta'aba) is fard.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
For each scenario, find the reasoning (talil) given in the text. For example, for the tashahhud case: 'because the tashahhud is wajib and the prayer's sanctity remains after the imam's salam.' For tasbihat: 'because tasbihat are sunnah and following the imam is fard.'
The text uses qiyas and preference (istihsan) in some cases.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Proof Applies)
Explain how the proof leads to the ruling. For instance, if wajib conflicts with fard, the fard (following imam) takes precedence, but if two wajib acts conflict (tashahhud vs. following imam), the follower completes tashahhud because it remains wajib and can be followed by salam.
The text also notes that if only sunnah remains, it is better to leave it for fard.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Disagreement)
Identify any intra-Hanafi or cross-madhhab disagreement. For example, Imam Muhammad holds that the follower exits with the imam's salam, so completing tashahhud is not required. Some scholars held tasbihat are obligatory (three minimum).
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the one given in the text.
5
Evaluate the Mufta Bihi and Tarjih
State which position is relied upon for fatwa and why. The commentator prefers completing tashahhud and following imam immediately for tasbihat, as supported by Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir.
The tarjih mechanism uses the principle that sunnah is left for fard, and wajib is completed when possible.

Source Text

فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي بعد فراغ إمامه من واجب وغيره
لوْ سَلَّمَ الإمام قبل فراغ المقتدي من التشهد يُتِمُهُ، ولو رفع الإمام رأسه، قبل تسبيح المقتدي ثلاثاً، في الركوع أو السجودِ يتابعه، ولو زاد الإمام ،سجدة، أو قام بعد القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، لا يَتْبَعُهُ المُؤْتَم، وإنْ قَيْدَها سَلَّمَ وَحْدَهُ،

فصل: فيما يفعله المقتدي بعد فراغ إمامه من واجب وغيره لوْ سَلَّمَ الإمامُ) أو تكلم لأنه في معنى السلام (قبل فراغ المقتدي من) قراءة (التشهد يُتِمُّهُ)؛ لأن التشهد من الواجبات ويُسلّم بعده، وحرمة الصلاة باقية بعد سلام الإمام، وهو ذكر منظوم، فترك ما بقي يوجب بطلان ما مضى، وإن بقي عليه شيء من الدعوات أو الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لأنه لم يبق عليه واجب، ولأنه عند محمد رحمه الله يخرج بسلام الإمام فخروجه بسلام نفسه أولى، وأما إذا أحدث الإمام عمداً، ولو بقهقهته عند السلام لا يقرأ المقتدي التشهد، ولم يكن عليه أن يسلم؛ لخروجه عن الصلاة ببطلان الجزء الذي لاقاه حدث الإمام، فلا يبني على ما فسد، ولا يضر ذلك في صحة الصلاة، لكنها ناقصة بترك السلام، فيجب إعادتها لجبر الخلل، وإذا لم يكن قعد قدر التشهد بطلت بالحدث العمد، ولو قام الإمام إلى الثالثة ولم يتم المقتدي التشهد أتمه، وإن لم يتمه جاز، وفي فتاوى الفضلي»، و « التجنيس » ، يتمه ولا يتبع الإمام وإن خاف فوت الركوع؛ لأن قراءة بعض التشهد لم تعرف قربة والركوع لا يفوته في الحقيقة لأنه يدرك، فكان خلف الإمام ومعارضته واجب آخر لا يمنع الإتيان بما كان فيه من واجب غيره لإتيانه به بعده فكان تأخير أحد الواجبـيـن مـع الإتيان بهما أولى من ترك أحدهما بالكلية، بخلاف ما إذا عارضه سنة؛ لأن ترك السنة أولى من تأخير الواجب، أشار إليه بقوله: (ولو رفع الإمام رأسه قبل تسبيح المقتدي ثلاثاً، في الركوع، أو السجود، يتابعه في الصحيح، لأن التسبيحات سنة، ومتابعة الإمام فريضة، فكان الاشتغال بـهـا أولى وهو مذكور في شرح الجامع الكبير في باب صلاة العيدين. ومنهم من قال: يتمها ثلاثاً لأن من أهل العلم من قال: لا تجوز الصلاة بأقل من ثلاث تسبيحات ولو زاد الإمام سجدة، أو قام بعد القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، لا يَتْبَعُهُ المُؤْتَمُّ؛ لأنه ليس من أصل صلاته، فينتظر سلامه ليسلم إن تذكر وجلس قبل تقييده الزائدة بسجدة، (وإنْ قَيَّدَها ) أي: الإمام الزائدة بسجدة (سَلَّمَ) المقتدي ( وَحْدَهُ)، ولا ينتظر لخروجه من تلك الصلاة واشتغاله بالنفل
Chapter on what the follower does after his imam completes an obligatory act or other. If the imam says the salam before the follower finishes the tashahhud, he completes it. If the imam raises his head before the follower completes the three tasbihat in bowing or prostration, he follows him. If the imam adds a sajdah, or stands after the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow him, and if he binds it (the additional sajdah) with a prostration, the follower says the salam alone. Chapter: What the follower does after his imam completes an obligatory act or other. If the imam says the salam (or speaks, because it is like the salam) before the follower finishes reading the tashahhud, he completes it because the tashahhud is obligatory and he says the salam after it, and the sanctity of the prayer remains after the imam's salam, and it is a structured remembrance, so abandoning what remains necessitates the invalidity of what has passed. And if there remains on him any of the supplications or salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), because no obligatory act remains upon him, and because according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) he leaves by the imam's salam, so his leaving by his own salam is more appropriate. And if the imam deliberately does an invalidating act, even by laughing loudly at the time of salam, the follower does not recite the tashahhud, and he does not have to say salam, because he leaves the prayer by the invalidity of the portion that was concurrent with the imam's invalidating act, so he does not build upon what is corrupted, and that does not harm the validity of the prayer, but it is deficient by leaving the salam, so he must repeat it to remedy the defect. And if he did not sit for the duration of the tashahhud, the prayer is invalidated by the deliberate invalidating act. And if the imam stands for the third rak'ah and the follower has not completed the tashahhud, he completes it, and if he does not complete it, it is permissible. In Fatawa al-Fadli and al-Tajnis, he completes it and does not follow the imam even if he fears missing the bowing, because reciting part of the tashahhud is not known to be an act of worship, and the bowing is not actually missed because he will catch it. So being behind the imam and his opposing another obligatory act does not prevent performing the obligatory act he was engaged in because he will perform it afterwards. Thus, delaying one of the two obligatory acts while performing both is better than completely abandoning one of them, unlike if it is opposed by a sunnah, because abandoning the sunnah is better than delaying the obligatory. He indicated that by his saying: (If the imam raises his head before the follower completes three tasbihat in bowing or prostration, he follows him according to the correct view, because the tasbihat are sunnah and following the imam is fard, so engaging in it is more appropriate. This is mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir in the chapter on the two Eid prayers. And some say he completes them as three because some scholars said prayer is not valid with less than three tasbihat.) And if the imam adds a sajdah, or stands after the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow him, because it is not part of his original prayer, so he waits for his salam to say salam. If he remembers and sits before binding it (the addition) with a sajdah, he says the salam alone, and does not wait because he leaves that prayer and engages in supererogatory.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on what a follower (muqtadi) should do after the imam completes an obligatory action or other. It opens with several scenarios: (1) If the imam says the salam before the follower finishes tashahhud, the follower completes it because tashahhud is wajib and the prayer's sanctity continues. (2) If the imam raises his head before the follower completes three tasbihat in ruku' or sujud, the follower follows the imam because following the imam is fard while tasbihat are sunnah. (3) If the imam adds an extra sajdah or stands after the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow him; if the imam performs the sajdah, the follower says the salam alone. The commentary elaborates on each: for the tashahhud case, it notes a difference with Imam Muhammad (who holds the follower exits with imam's salam), but the ruling is that the follower completes it. For the tasbihat, there is a difference with some scholars who require three tasbihat. The passage also covers cases where the imam invalidates his prayer deliberately, in which case the follower does not recite tashahhud but must repeat the prayer due to deficiency.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of 'At-tahiyyat' etc. in the sitting position; an obligatory part of prayer.
التسبيحات (al-tasbīḥāt): The glorifications said in ruku' and sujud (e.g., Subhana rabbiya al-adheem).
المتابعة (al-mutābaʿah): The act of following the imam in actions of prayer; it is considered fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam raises his head from ruku' before the follower has completed three tasbihat, what should the follower do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Complete three tasbihat first, then follow the imam
B) Follow the imam immediately and leave the tasbihat incomplete
C) Repeat the entire rak'ah
D) Say the salam alone

Key Takeaway
When a wajib act (tashahhud) conflicts with the imam's completion, complete the wajib; when a sunnah act (tasbihat) conflicts with the fard of muta'aba, follow the imam immediately.

Completing Tashahhud When Imam Says Salam Early
Ruling on follower finishing tashahhud after imam's salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for a follower who has not completed tashahhud when the imam says salam, and identify the exceptional case when the imam intentionally invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
A wajib act like tashahhud must be completed even if the imam has left the prayer.

In congregational prayer, the imam leads and the follower must follow, but sometimes the imam finishes an action before the follower is ready. This lesson addresses the most common scenario: when the imam says salam before the follower completes the tashahhud. You will learn that the follower must finish the wajib tashahhud before leaving the prayer, and how the ruling changes if the imam's action is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The imam says salam before the follower finishes tashahhud. The follower must complete the tashahhud because it is wajib and the prayer's inviolability remains.
Tashahhud is wajib, not fard, so it must be fulfilled.
2
Understand the exception
If the imam intentionally commits a nullifier (e.g., deliberate speech), the follower does not complete tashahhud because the prayer is invalidated.
The follower exits the prayer due to the imam's action.
3
Apply the ruling to similar cases
The same principle applies if the imam stands before the final sitting: the follower waits and reminds the imam.
Only explicit in the matn.

الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لأنه لم يبق عليه واجب، ولأنه عند محمد رحمه الله يخرج بسلام الإمام فخروجه بسلام نفسه أولى، وأما إذا أحدث الإمام عمداً، ولو بقهقهته عند السلام لا يقرأ المقتدي التشهد، ولم يكن عليه أن يسلم؛ لخروجه عن الصلاة ببطلان الجزء الذي لاقاه حدث الإمام، فلا يبني على ما فسد، ولا يضر ذلك في صحة الصلاة، لكنها ناقصة بترك السلام، فيجب إعادتها لجبر الخلل، وإذا لم يكن قعد قدر التشهد بطلت بالحدث العمد، ولو قام الإمام إلى الثالثة ولم يتم المقتدي التشهد أتمه، وإن لم يتمه جاز، وفي فتاوى الفضلي» ، و « التجنيس » ، يتمه ولا يتبع الإمام وإن خاف فوت الركوع؛ لأن قراءة بعض التشهد لم تعرف قربة والركوع لا يفوته في الحقيقة لأنه يدرك، فكان خلف الإمام ومعارضته واجب آخر لا يمنع الإتيان بما كان فيه من واجب غيره لإتيانه به بعده فكان تأخير أحد الواجبـيـن مـع الإتيان بهما أولى من ترك أحدهما بالكلية، بخلاف ما إذا عارضه سنة؛ لأن ترك السنة أولى من تأخير الواجب، أشار إليه بقوله: (ولو رفع الإمام رأسه قبل تسبيح المقتدي ثلاثاً، في الركوع، أو السجود، يتابعه في الصحيح، لأن التسبيحات سنة، ومتابعة الإمام فريضة، فكان الاشتغال بـهـا أولى وهو مذكور في شرح الجامع الكبير في باب صلاة العيدين. ومنهم من قال: يتمها ثلاثاً لأن من أهل العلم من قال: لا تجوز الصلاة بأقل من ثلاث تسبيحات ولو زاد الإمام سجدة، أو قام بعد القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، لا يَتْبَعُهُ المُؤْتَمُّ؛ لأنه ليس من أصل صلاته، فينتظر سلامه ليسلم إن تذكر وجلس قبل تقييده الزائدة بسجدة، (وإنْ قَيَّدَها ) أي: الإمام الزائدة بسجدة (سَلَّمَ) المقتدي ( وَحْدَهُ)، ولا ينتظر لخروجه من تلك الصلاة واشتغاله بالنفل معه وإن قام الإمام قبل القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، انتظره المأموم فإنْ سَلَّمَ المقتدي قبل أن يُقيِّدَ إمامه الزائدة بسجدةٍ، فَسَدَ فَرْضُهُ. وكُرِهَ سلامُ المقتدي بعدَ تَشَهُدِ الإمام قبل سلامِهِ. (وإنْ قامَ الإمام، قبل القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، انتظره المأموم وسبح ليتنبه إمامه، فإنْ سَلَّمَ المُقتدي قبل أنْ يُقيِّدَ إمامهُ الزَّائِدَةَ بسجدة فسَدَ فَرْضُهُ، لانفراده بركن القعود حال الاقتداء، كمـا تفسـد بتقييد الإمام الزائدة بسجدة لتركه القعود الأخير في محله، وهاتان مسألتان مما لا يتبع المؤتم إمامه فيه، والثالث: لو زاد على أقاويل الصحابة في تكبيرات العيد وسمعه من الإمام لا إن سمعه من المقتدي لجواز الخطأ عليه، والرابع: لو كبر في الجنازة خامسة. وخمسة أشياء إذا تركها الإمام يتركها المؤتم ويتابع الإمام القنوت إذا خاف فـوت الركوع وتكبير الزوائد في العيدين كذلك، و والقعدة الأولى، وسجدة التلاوة، والسهو. وتسعة أشياء إذا تركها الإمام يأتي بها المقتدي رفع اليدين للتحريمة، والثناء إن كان الإمام في الفاتحة وإن في السورة لا عند محمد خلافاً للثاني)، وتكبير الركوع أو السجود، والتسبيح فيهما، والتسميع، وقراءة التشهد، والسلام، وتكبير التشريق من ( البزازية» وغيرها. (وكُـرة سـلام المقتدي بعدَ تَشَهدِ الإمام المستلزم لقعوده قدر التشهد، إذ هـو الشـرط (قبـل سـلامه) لـتـرك المتابعة، وصحت صلاته (۳)؛ لعدم بقاء شيء من فروضها، حتى لو اعترض المفسد بـعـده كطلوع الشمس في الفجر ووجدان الماء للمتيمم بطلت صلاة الإمام فقط على القول بأن الخروج بالصنع فرض عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح أو لا تبطل على القول بوجوبه كما سنذكره إن شاء الله تعالى).
Chapter on what the follower does after the completion of his imam from obligatory and other acts. If the imam says salam before the follower finishes the tashahhud, he completes it. And if the imam raises his head before the follower's three tasbihs in ruku or sujud, he follows him. And if the imam adds a sajdah or stands after the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow him, and if he ties it with a sajdah, he says salam alone. (Commentary:) ...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn from Nur al-Idah, explaining the duties of the follower (muqtadi) when the imam progresses ahead in prayer. The author systematically addresses various scenarios. First, if the imam says salam before the follower finishes tashahhud, the follower must complete the tashahhud because it is obligatory (wajib) and the prayer's inviolability remains. He then says his own salam. However, if the imam intentionally causes a nullifier (like deliberate speech), the follower does not complete tashahhud and does not need to say salam, as the prayer becomes invalid. Next, regarding tasbih in ruku and sujud: if the imam lifts his head before the follower completes three tasbihs, the follower should follow the imam immediately because tasbih is sunnah while following the imam is wajib. Some scholars held that the follower should complete three tasbihs, but the relied-upon (sahih) position is to follow. Then, if the imam adds an extra prostration or stands up after the final tashahhud forgetfully, the follower must not follow; he waits for the imam's salam. If the imam ties the extra act with a sajdah, the follower says salam alone. Later, the text discusses when the imam stands before the final sitting: the follower should wait and alert the imam by saying tasbih. If the follower says salam before the imam ties the extra with sajdah, his obligatory prayer is invalidated. The passage also lists four things the follower does not follow the imam in, five things the follower abandons if the imam abandons them, and nine things the follower does even if the imam omits them. Finally, it states the disliked nature (karahah) of the follower saying salam after the imam's tashahhud but before his salam, though the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in prayer, comprising at least 'al-tahiyyat lillah...'
متابعة (mutaba'ah): The follower's duty to follow the imam in actions without delay

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam says salam before the follower finishes his tashahhud, what should the follower do?
A) Immediately say salam and follow the imam
B) Complete the tashahhud and then say salam
C) Stop the tashahhud and wait for the imam
D) Leave the prayer invalid because the imam rushed

Key Takeaway
A follower must complete a wajib act like tashahhud even if the imam has left the prayer, unless the imam's action nullifies the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Following the Imam in Ruku/Sujud vs. Completing Tasbih
Dispute within Hanafi school on tasbih completion vs. following imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that prioritises following the imam over completing sunnah tasbih, and evaluate the opposing view within the school.

Core Idea
Following the imam (fard) takes precedence over reciting sunnah tasbih.

When the imam raises his head from ruku or sujud before the follower has completed three tasbihs, the follower faces a conflict between a sunnah (tasbih) and a fard (mutaba'ah). This lesson examines the Hanafi position that the follower must immediately follow the imam, and the dissenting view of some scholars who insisted on completing three tasbihs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The follower should follow the imam immediately even if he has not completed three tasbihs, because following the imam (mutaba'ah) is fard and tasbih is sunnah.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
2
Understand the opposing view
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., Abu Mutii al-Balkhi) held that the follower should complete three tasbihs because less than that invalidates the prayer (according to some opinions).
This view is considered weak.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the prayer is valid with fewer tasbihs, and the obligation of mutaba'ah is stronger, so the sunnah is left for the fard.
The text says 'في الصحيح' to indicate the correct view.

In Hanafi prayer, if the imam raises his head from ruku before the follower has completed three tasbihs, what should the follower do?

Key Takeaway

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Follower's Response to Imam's Extra Actions and Summary Lists
Rulings on non-following of extra actions and lists of obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify four situations where the follower does NOT follow the imam, list things the follower abandons if the imam abandons them, and list things the follower does even if the imam omits them.

Core Idea
The follower does not follow the imam in extra actions that are not part of the original prayer.

The imam may occasionally add an extra prostration or stand up after the final sitting forgetfully. The follower must not follow in these actions because they are not part of the established prayer. This lesson also provides three important lists: four things the follower never follows the imam in, five things the follower abandons if the imam abandons them, and nine things the follower performs even if the imam omits them.

Guided Path
1
Identify extra actions not to follow
If the imam adds an extra sajdah or stands after the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow; he waits for the imam to return.
If the extra sajdah is tied with a real sajdah, the follower says salam alone.
2
Learn the four things not followed
The text lists four things: extra sajdah, standing after final sitting, extra takbir in Eid if heard from follower (not imam), and a fifth takbir in janazah.
These are from the expanded commentary.
3
Learn the five things abandoned if imam abandons them
If the imam omits: qunut, extra takbir in Eid, the first sitting, sajdah tilawah, and sajdah sahw, the follower also omits them.
These are sunnah or non-obligatory.
4
Learn the nine things the follower does even if imam omits them
These include: raising hands for takbir, thana (commendation), takbir for ruku/sujud, tasbih in ruku/sujud, tasmee', tashahhud, salam, and takbir of tashriq.
These are wajib or sunnah acts that the follower must perform individually.

Source Text

الإمام فريضة، فكان الاشتغال بـهـا أولى وهو مذكور في شرح الجامع الكبير في باب صلاة العيدين. ومنهم من قال: يتمها ثلاثاً لأن من أهل العلم من قال: لا تجوز الصلاة بأقل من ثلاث تسبيحات ولو زاد الإمام سجدة، أو قام بعد القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، لا يَتْبَعُهُ المُؤْتَمُّ؛ لأنه ليس من أصل صلاته، فينتظر سلامه ليسلم إن تذكر وجلس قبل تقييده الزائدة بسجدة، (وإنْ قَيَّدَها ) أي: الإمام الزائدة بسجدة (سَلَّمَ) المقتدي ( وَحْدَهُ)، ولا ينتظر لخروجه من تلك الصلاة واشتغاله بالنفل معه وإن قام الإمام قبل القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، انتظره المأموم فإنْ سَلَّمَ المقتدي قبل أن يُقيِّدَ إمامه الزائدة بسجدةٍ، فَسَدَ فَرْضُهُ. وكُرِهَ سلامُ المقتدي بعدَ تَشَهُدِ الإمام قبل سلامِهِ. (وإنْ قامَ الإمام، قبل القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، انتظره المأموم وسبح ليتنبه إمامه، فإنْ سَلَّمَ المُقتدي قبل أنْ يُقيِّدَ إمامهُ الزَّائِدَةَ بسجدة فسَدَ فَرْضُهُ، لانفراده بركن القعود حال الاقتداء، كمـا تفسـد بتقييد الإمام الزائدة بسجدة لتركه القعود الأخير في محله، وهاتان مسألتان مما لا يتبع المؤتم إمامه فيه، والثالث: لو زاد على أقاويل الصحابة في تكبيرات العيد وسمعه من الإمام لا إن سمعه من المقتدي لجواز الخطأ عليه، والرابع: لو كبر في الجنازة خامسة. وخمسة أشياء إذا تركها الإمام يتركها المؤتم ويتابع الإمام القنوت إذا خاف فـوت الركوع وتكبير الزوائد في العيدين كذلك، و والقعدة الأولى، وسجدة التلاوة، والسهو. وتسعة أشياء إذا تركها الإمام يأتي بها المقتدي رفع اليدين للتحريمة، والثناء إن كان الإمام في الفاتحة وإن في السورة لا عند محمد خلافاً للثاني)، وتكبير الركوع أو السجود، والتسبيح فيهما، والتسميع، وقراءة التشهد، والسلام، وتكبير التشريق من ( البزازية» وغيرها. (وكُـرة سـلام المقتدي بعدَ تَشَهدِ الإمام المستلزم لقعوده قدر التشهد، إذ هـو الشـرط (قبـل سـلامه) لـتـرك المتابعة، وصحت صلاته (۳)؛ لعدم بقاء شيء من فروضها، حتى لو اعترض المفسد بـعـده كطلوع الشمس في الفجر ووجدان الماء للمتيمم بطلت صلاة الإمام فقط على القول بأن الخروج بالصنع فرض عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح أو لا تبطل على القول بوجوبه كما سنذكره إن شاء الله تعالى).
Chapter on what the follower does after the completion of his imam from obligatory and other acts. If the imam says salam before the follower finishes the tashahhud, he completes it. And if the imam raises his head before the follower's three tasbihs in ruku or sujud, he follows him. And if the imam adds a sajdah or stands after the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow him, and if he ties it with a sajdah, he says salam alone. (Commentary:) ...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn from Nur al-Idah, explaining the duties of the follower (muqtadi) when the imam progresses ahead in prayer. The author systematically addresses various scenarios. First, if the imam says salam before the follower finishes tashahhud, the follower must complete the tashahhud because it is obligatory (wajib) and the prayer's inviolability remains. He then says his own salam. However, if the imam intentionally causes a nullifier (like deliberate speech), the follower does not complete tashahhud and does not need to say salam, as the prayer becomes invalid. Next, regarding tasbih in ruku and sujud: if the imam lifts his head before the follower completes three tasbihs, the follower should follow the imam immediately because tasbih is sunnah while following the imam is wajib. Some scholars held that the follower should complete three tasbihs, but the relied-upon (sahih) position is to follow. Then, if the imam adds an extra prostration or stands up after the final tashahhud forgetfully, the follower must not follow; he waits for the imam's salam. If the imam ties the extra act with a sajdah, the follower says salam alone. Later, the text discusses when the imam stands before the final sitting: the follower should wait and alert the imam by saying tasbih. If the follower says salam before the imam ties the extra with sajdah, his obligatory prayer is invalidated. The passage also lists four things the follower does not follow the imam in, five things the follower abandons if the imam abandons them, and nine things the follower does even if the imam omits them. Finally, it states the disliked nature (karahah) of the follower saying salam after the imam's tashahhud but before his salam, though the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
سجدة زائدة (sajdah za'idah): An extra prostration added by the imam inadvertently
قنوت (qunut): Supplication recited in the last rakat of Fajr, Witr, or during calamities
تشريق (tashriq): Takbirs recited after prayers on the days of Tashriq (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam forgetfully stands after the final tashahhud, what should the follower do?
A) Stand up and follow
B) Remain seated and wait
C) Say salam immediately
D) Say tasbih to alert and then stand

Key Takeaway
The follower follows the imam in original prayer actions but not in extra actions, and there are distinct lists of actions the follower must perform or abandon.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

When the Imam Stands Before the Final Sitting: The Follower's Obligation and the Analogy
Explains follower's obligations when imam errs by standing early

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a follower who gives salam before the imam ties the extra rak'ah with a sajdah, explain the clear analogy (qiyas jaliy) used, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding subsequent nullifiers.

Core Idea
A follower's prayer becomes invalid if he salam before the imam completes the extra rak'ah — based on a clear analogy to the imam leaving the final sitting.

In congregational prayer, the follower must follow the imam. When the imam forgetfully stands for an extra rak'ah, what is the follower to do? This passage addresses precisely that: the follower must wait and alert the imam. If he prematurely gives the salam, his prayer is invalid. The author uses a clear qiyas (analogy) to explain the ruling, and then discusses a related intra-madhhab difference regarding the effect of nullifiers after the follower's salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the first part of the passage: the imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully. The follower must wait. If the follower gives salam before the imam ties the extra rak'ah with a sajdah, what is the ruling? The text says 'his prayer becomes invalid' (fasada farduhu).
The ruling is clear: the follower's prayer is invalid (batil) in this case.
2
Locate the dalil – the clear analogy
The passage provides the proof: 'because he isolated himself in the pillar of sitting while being in a state of following, just as it becomes invalid by the imam's tying the extra with a sajdah due to leaving the final sitting in its place.' This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy). Identify the asl (original case) and far' (new case).
Asl: imam tying extra sajdah (prayer invalid). Far': follower giving salam before that (prayer invalid).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah – how the analogy proves the ruling
The shared effective cause (illa) is the abandonment of the required following (mutaba'ah) or the missing of the final sitting pillar. In both cases, the prayer is invalid because a fundamental obligation of following or a pillar is breached.
The analogy is straightforward and directly cited in the text.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on subsequent nullifiers
After discussing the main ruling, the passage adds: if a nullifier occurs after the follower's salam but before the imam's salam (e.g., sunrise in Fajr), does the imam's prayer become invalid? Abu Hanifa says yes; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no. Identify the basis of the difference.
The disagreement hinges on whether the action of exiting is considered fard or wajib.
5
Evaluate the tarjih – which view is relied upon
The author states that the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is rajih (preferred) – the imam's prayer does not become invalid. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
Thus, the relied-upon ruling: the imam's prayer remains valid despite subsequent nullifiers after the follower's salam.

Source Text

(وإنْ قامَ الإمام، قبل القُعود الأخير، ساهياً، انتظره المأموم وسبح ليتنبه إمامه، فإنْ سَلَّمَ المُقتدي قبل أنْ يُقيِّدَ إمامهُ الزَّائِدَةَ بسجدة فسَدَ فَرْضُهُ، لانفراده بركن القعود حال الاقتداء، كمـا تفسـد بتقييد الإمام الزائدة بسجدة لتركه القعود الأخير في محله، وهاتان مسألتان مما لا يتبع المؤتم إمامه فيه، والثالث: لو زاد على أقاويل الصحابة في تكبيرات العيد وسمعه من الإمام لا إن سمعه من المقتدي لجواز الخطأ عليه، والرابع: لو كبر في الجنازة خامسة. وخمسة أشياء إذا تركها الإمام يتركها المؤتم ويتابع الإمام القنوت إذا خاف فـوت الركوع وتكبير الزوائد في العيدين كذلك، و والقعدة الأولى، وسجدة التلاوة، والسهو.
وتسعة أشياء إذا تركها الإمام يأتي بها المقتدي رفع اليدين للتحريمة، والثناء إن كان الإمام في الفاتحة وإن في السورة لا عند محمد خلافاً للثاني)، وتكبير الركوع أو السجود، والتسبيح فيهما، والتسميع، وقراءة التشهد، والسلام، وتكبير التشريق من ( البزازية» وغيرها. (وكُـرة سـلام المقتدي بعدَ تَشَهدِ الإمام المستلزم لقعوده قدر التشهد، إذ هـو الشـرط (قبـل سـلامه) لـتـرك المتابعة، وصحت صلاته (۳)؛ لعدم بقاء شيء من فروضها، حتى لو اعترض المفسد بـعـده كطلوع الشمس في الفجر ووجدان الماء للمتيمم بطلت صلاة الإمام فقط على القول بأن الخروج بالصنع فرض عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح أو لا تبطل على القول بوجوبه كما سنذكره إن شاء الله تعالى).
(۱) أي: خلافاً لأبي يوسف فإنه يثني وإن كان في السورة. فتح القدير (٤٨٤/١). (۲) أي: تحريماً للنهي عن الاختلاف على الإمام، إلا أن يكون القيام لضرورة صون صلاته عن الفساد كخـوف حدث لو انتظر السلام، وخروج وقت فجر وجمعة وعيد ومعذور وتمام مدة مسح ومرور مـار بين يديه، فلا يكره حينئذ أن يقوم بعد القعود قدر التشهد قبل السلام. ط .

(٤) ص (٣٤٤).
If the Imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully, the follower waits for him. If the follower gives salam before the Imam ties the extra (rak'ah) with a sajdah, his prayer becomes invalid. And it is disliked for the follower to give salam after the Imam's tashahhud before his salam. (If the Imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully, the follower waits for him and says Subhan Allah to alert his Imam. If the follower gives salam before the Imam ties the extra with a sajdah, his prayer becomes invalid, because he isolated himself in the pillar of sitting while being in a state of following, just as it becomes invalid by the Imam's tying the extra with a sajdah due to leaving the final sitting in its place. These are two matters in which the follower does not follow his Imam. Third: If he adds to the statements of the Companions regarding the takbeers of Eid and the follower heard it from the Imam, he does not follow, but if he heard it from the follower, he does follow because error is possible for him. Fourth: If he says a fifth takbeer in the funeral prayer. And five things: If the Imam leaves them, the follower leaves them: following the Imam in Qunut if he fears missing the bowing, the extra takbeers in the two Eids likewise, the first sitting, the prostration of recitation, and the prostration of forgetfulness. And nine things: If the Imam leaves them, the follower performs them: raising the hands for the opening takbeer, the Thana' if the Imam is in the Fatihah or in the Surah, but not according to Muhammad contrary to the second, the takbeer for bowing or prostration, the glorifications in them, the listening (sami'a), reciting the tashahhud, the salam, and the takbeer of Tashreeq from al-Bazzaziyyah and others. (And it is disliked for the follower to give salam after the Imam's tashahhud which necessitates his sitting for the measure of tashahhud, for that is the condition, before his salam, due to leaving the following, yet his prayer is valid because none of its obligatory acts remain. So much so that if a nullifier occurs after it, such as sunrise in Fajr or finding water by one performing tayammum, only the Imam's prayer becomes invalid according to the view that exiting by [specific] action is obligatory according to the Imam, and that is the correct view, or it does not become invalid according to the view that it is obligatory, as we will mention if Allah wills.)
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings regarding the follower when the imam makes a mistake in prayer, specifically standing before the final sitting. The main text states that if the imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully, the follower must wait for him. If the follower gives the salam before the imam performs the sajdah for the extra rak'ah, the follower's prayer becomes invalid because he has separated himself from the imam while the imam is still in prayer. The commentator explains the reasoning: the prayer invalidates because the follower performed the sitting alone while being required to follow, just as it would invalidate if the imam himself performed the extra sajdah after the extra rak'ah. This is one of four cases where the follower does not follow the imam: (1) imam stands before final sitting, (2) imam adds an extra sajdah, (3) imam adds extra takbeers in Eid prayer beyond the reported Companions' practice, and (4) imam adds a fifth takbeer in funeral prayer. Then the text lists five things if the imam leaves them, the follower also leaves them: following the imam in Qunut when fearing to miss the bowing, the extra takbeers in Eid, the first sitting, the prostration of recitation, and the prostration of forgetfulness. Then nine things if the imam leaves them, the follower must perform them: raising hands for the opening takbeer, the Thana' (if the imam is reciting Fatihah or Surah—though Muhammad differs if the imam is in the Surah), the takbeer for bowing and prostration, the glorifications in them, the listening (Sami'a), reciting the tashahhud, the salam, and the takbeer of Tashreeq. The footnote clarifies that according to Abu Yusuf, the follower should recite Thana' even if the imam is in the Surah. Finally, the text discusses the case where the follower gives salam after the imam's tashahhud but before the imam's salam: this is disliked (makruh) because it breaks the obligatory following, but the prayer is still valid since all fard acts have been fulfilled. However, if a nullifier occurs after that, like sunrise for Fajr prayer or finding water for a mutayammim, only the imam's prayer is invalidated according to the view that exiting prayer by a specific action is fard (obligatory) according to Abu Hanifa. The commentator notes that the correct view is that the imam's prayer is not invalidated, which is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qu‘ud al-akhir): The final sitting in prayer, after the last rak‘ah, during which tashahhud and salawat are recited before salam.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer (ma'mum).
المتابعة (al-mutaba‘ah): Following the imam in actions of prayer without preceding or delaying excessively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully, what must the follower do?
A) Give salam immediately to end the prayer.
B) Wait and say Subhan Allah to alert the imam.
C) Leave the congregation and pray alone.
D) Sit down and recite tashahhud again.

Key Takeaway
The follower must wait for the imam to correct his mistake; premature salam invalidates the prayer if it occurs before the imam completes the extra sajdah.

Recommended Dhikr After Fard Before Sunnah
Describes recommended practice after fard before sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended practice after the fard prayer regarding the sunnah prayer and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the incident with Umar.

Core Idea
Pause briefly after fard to say 'Allahumma antas-salam' then stand for sunnah; lengthy awrad are not recommended.

After completing an obligatory prayer, a Hanafi should not immediately stand for the sunnah without a short pause. The Prophet's guidance shows a specific brief dhikr before rising. This lesson clarifies the recommended practice, the proofs, and a permissible but less preferred view about longer litanies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The matn states that standing for sunnah immediately after fard is mas'oon (disapproved). However, a brief pause for a specific dhikr is recommended.
Mas'oon is equivalent to makruh tanzihi; not sinful but better avoided.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The hadith from Aisha shows the Prophet would pause after fard to recite 'Allahumma antas-salam...' before standing for sunnah. This establishes the recommended separation.
The hadith is found in Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi.
3
Understand the secondary evidence
The incident of Umar commanding a man to sit because 'the People of the Book were destroyed for lack of separation' further supports a brief pause rather than no pause.
Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi difference
Al-Halwani said 'no harm' in reciting longer awrad (litanies) between fard and sunnah, but the phrase implies the opposite is better. The majority view prefers only the brief dhikr.
Al-Halwani's view is recorded in al-Kamal's commentary.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is to pause for the short dhikr only; longer awrad are not recommended before the sunnah. The sunnah after such awrad is still valid but not in the optimal manner.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by al-Kamal and the author of Imdad al-Fattah.

( القيام إلى ) صلاة ( السِّنَّةِ) التي تعقب الفرض (متصلاً بالفرض مَسْئُونٌ)، غير أنه يستحب الفصل بينهما بقدر ما يقول: اللهم أنت السلام... إلخ، لما قال الكمال عن « شرح الشهيد». وفي الشافي» : كان عليه الصلاة والسلام إذا سلم يمكث قدر ما يقول: «اللَّهُمَّ أَنْتَ السَّلامُ وَمِنْكَ السَّلامُ وَإِلَيْكَ يَعُوْدُ السَّلامُ تَبَارَكْتَ يَا ذَا الْجَلالِ وَالإِكْرَامِ ) وكذلك عن ( البقالي»، (و) قال الكمال (عن شمس الأئمةِ الحَلْوَانِي): أنه قال: لا بأس بقراءة الأورادِ بين الفريضة والسنّة) وإنما قال: لا بأس لأن المشهور من هذه العبارة استعمالها فيما يكون خلافه أولى منه، فكان معناها: أنَّ الأولى أن لا يقرأ الأوراد قبل السنة، ولو فعل لا بأس به، فلا تسقط السنة بقراءته ذلك، حتّى إذا صلاها بعد الأوراد تقع سنة مؤداة لا على وجه السنة. انتهى ما قاله الكمال. وقال في « الاختيار » : كل صلاة بعدها سنة يكره القعود بعدها والدعاء، بل يشتغل بالسنة كيلا يفصل بين ا السنة والمكتوبة. وعن عائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يَقْعُدُ مِقْدَارَ مَا يَقُولُ: اللَّهُمَّ  َأنْتَ السَّلامُ وَمِنْكَ السَّلامُ وَإِلَيْكَ يَعُودُ السَّلامُ تَبَارَكْتَ يَا ذَا الْجَلالِ وَالإِكْرَامِ ثُمَّ يَقومُ إلى السُّنَّة ) (۲) انتهى. أي: فيندب الفصـل بـهذا، لهذا انتهى. ولأنه « قامَ رجلٌ قد أدرك مع النبي و التكبيرة الأولى ليشفع، فوثــب عـمـر بـن الخـطـابه فأخذ بمنكبِهِ فَهَزَّهُ ثمَّ قال: إجلس فإنَّه لم يهلك أهلُ الكتابِ إلا أنَّهُ لم يكُن لَهُمْ بينَ صَلاتِهِمْ فَصْلٌ، فرفع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بَصَرَهُ، فقال: أصَابَ اللهُ بِكَ يا ابْنَ الخَطَّابِ ) (۳) ثم قال الكمال: فمن ادعى فصلاً أكثر منه فلينقله، ولا يقتضي الأكثر ما ورد من أنَّه لو كان يقول: « دَبْرَ كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَحْدَهُ لا شريكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ، وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرُ، اللَّهُمُ لا مَانِعَ لِمَا أَعْطَيْتَ وَلَا مُعْطِيَ لِمَا مَنَعَتَ وَلَا يَنْفَعُ ذَا الْجَدَّ مِنْكَ الْجَدُّ » . وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الفقراء المهاجرين: « تُسَبِّحُونَ وَتُكَبِّرُونَ وَتَحْمَدُونَ
(1) أخرجه مسلم في المساجد ومواضع الصلاة، باب استحباب الذكر بعد الصلاة وبيان صفته (٥٩٢)، وأبو داود في الصلاة، باب ما يقول الرجل إذا سلم (١٥١٢)، والترمذي في كتاب الصلاة، باب ما يقول إذا سلم من الصلاة (۲۹۸). (۲) تقدم تخريجه بالحديث السابق. (۳) أخرجه أبو داود في الصلاة، باب : في الرجل يتطوع مكانه الذي صلى فيه المكتوبة (١٠٠٧)، والحاكم في المستدرك (٤٠٣/١).
(٤) أخرجه مسلم في المساجد ومواضع الصلاة، باب استحباب الذكر بعد الصلاة، وبيان صفته (٥٩٣)، والترمذي في الصلاة، باب: ما يقول إذا سلم من الصلاة (۲۹۸)، وأبو داود في الصلاة، باب ما يقول الرجل إذا سلم (١٥٠٥).
Chapter on the description of the remembrances reported after the obligatory prayer.
(Standing for the Sunnah prayer that follows the obligatory prayer immediately is disapproved (mas'oon)). However, it is recommended to separate between them by the amount of saying: 'Allahumma antas-salam...' etc., as stated by al-Kamal from 'Sharh al-Shahid'. And in 'al-Shafi': The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to pause after salutation for as much as it takes to say: 'Allahumma anta al-salam wa minka al-salam wa ilayka ya'oodu al-salam, tabarakta ya dhal-jalali wa al-ikram' – similarly from al-Baqqali. And al-Kamal said from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani that he said: There is no harm in reciting the regular litanies (al-awrad) between the obligatory prayer and the sunnah. He said 'no harm' because the common usage of this phrase is for something whose opposite is better. So its meaning is that it is better not to recite the litanies before the sunnah, but if one does so, there is no harm. The sunnah is not invalidated by that recitation, so much so that if one performs the sunnah after the litanies, it counts as an offered sunnah but not in the complete manner of the sunnah. This ends the statement of al-Kamal. And in 'al-Ikhtiyar': For every prayer that has a sunnah after it, it is disliked to sit after it and make du'a; rather one should occupy with the sunnah so as not to separate between the sunnah and the obligatory prayer. And from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to pause as much as it takes to say: 'Allahumma anta al-salam...' then stand for the sunnah. That is, it is recommended to separate with this. And because a man who had caught the first takbeer with the Prophet stood up to pray an additional two rak'ahs, and Umar ibn al-Khattab grabbed him and said: Sit, for the People of the Book were only destroyed because they had no separation between their prayers. The Prophet raised his gaze and said: Allah has guided you, O Ibn al-Khattab. Then al-Kamal said: Whoever claims a longer separation should bring evidence. The longer separation is not implied by what is reported that he used to say after every prayer: 'La ilaha illa Allah...' and his saying to the poor immigrants: 'Glorify, magnify, and praise...'
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a chapter (fasl) on the recommended adhkar after the obligatory prayer. The main text (from Nur al-Idah) states that standing for the sunnah prayer immediately connected to the fard is 'mas'oon' (disapproved). However, it is recommended to separate between them by the duration of reciting a specific dhikr: 'Allahumma antas-salam...' This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Aisha. The commentator (Imdad al-Fattah) discusses a difference of opinion: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said there is no harm in reciting longer litanies (awrad) between the fard and sunnah, but this is not the preferred view. The word 'no harm' (la ba's) implies that the opposite (not reciting) is better. So it is better to proceed to the sunnah immediately after the short dhikr, not reciting lengthy awrad. Al-Kamal cites from al-Ikhtiyar that for every prayer that has a sunnah after it, it is disliked to sit for a while and make du'a; one should engage in the sunnah to avoid separating the sunnah from the fard. The hadith of Umar supports the idea of a small separation but not lengthy interruption. The passage also notes that longer dhikr (like 'La ilaha illa Allah...') are reported to be said after prayer, but these do not require a longer pause; they can be recited while standing for the sunnah or in a brief moment. The overall ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) to pause briefly after the fard salutation to recite 'Allahumma antas-salam' and then proceed to the sunnah. Reciting extensive awrad before the sunnah is permissible but not preferred.

Key Terms
السنة الراتبة (al-sunnah al-ratibah): The regularly performed sunnah prayers that accompany the obligatory prayers, such as the two rak'ahs after Zuhr.
الأوراد (al-awrad): Regular litanies or recitations of dhikr, prescribed or voluntary, recited at specific times.
مَسْئُون (mas'oon): Disapproved (makruh tanzihan) – an action that is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the recommended practice after the obligatory prayer regarding the sunnah prayer?
A) Stand immediately for the sunnah without any separation.
B) Recite lengthy litanies before standing for the sunnah.
C) Pause briefly to recite 'Allahumma antas-salam' then stand for the sunnah.
D) Make sujud al-sahw before standing for the sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The recommended separation between fard and sunnah is a brief dhikr ('Allahumma antas-salam'); lengthy awrad are not recommended before the sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Reciting Adhkar Between Fard and Sunnah Prayers
Ruling with proof on timing of adhkar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating fard and sunnah prayers with adhkar and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to separate fard and sunnah with a short supplication; longer adhkar should be delayed after the sunnah.

After completing the fard prayer, many Muslims are accustomed to reciting lengthy litanies before the sunnah prayer. However, the Hanafi school teaches a nuanced ruling: it is recommended to pause only briefly—just long enough for a short supplication—before standing for the sunnah. This lesson, drawn from Imdad al-Fattah, explains the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the scholarly consensus on the optimal timing of adhkar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being discussed (standing for the sunnah immediately after fard) and its legal classification: it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to stand immediately; it is mustahabb (recommended) to separate with a short pause.
The text uses 'mas'ūn' which is a corruption of 'makruh'.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary proof cited: the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet sat only long enough to say 'Allahumma anta al-salam...' and the incident with Umar affirming separation.
The hadith is from Muslim and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The phrase 'lam yaq'ud illa miqdar ma yaqul' indicates a very brief pause, implying that longer adhkar should not be inserted between fard and sunnah.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, but sufficient for this ruling.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Halwani said 'la ba's' (no harm) in reciting longer adhkar between fard and sunnah, but this implies it is permissible only, not preferred.
Al-Kamal and the author of Imdad al-Fattah prefer delaying them.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is to recite only the short supplication between fard and sunnah, and delay lengthy adhkar until after the sunnah.
Tarjih authority: Al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam) and the author.

ليس من توابع الصلاة، فصح كونها دبرها. ثم قال الكمال: والحاصل أنه لم يثبت عنه هو الفصل بالأذكار التي يواظب عليها في المساجد في عصرنا، من قراءة آية الكرسي والتسبيحات وأخواتها ثلاثاً وثلاثين وغيرها، بل ندب هو إليها، والقدر المتحقق أن كلا من السنن والأوراد له نسبة إلى الفرائض بالتبعية، والذي ثبت عنه الا الله من الأذكار التي تؤخر عنه السنة، ويفصل به بينها وبين الفرض هو ما روى مسلم والترمذي عن عائشة كما قدمناه. كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا سَلَّمَ لَمْ يَقْعُدَ إِلا مِقْدَارَ مَا يَقولُ: «اللَّهُمَّ أَنْتَ السَّلامُ وَمِنْكَ السَّلامُ تَبَارَكْتَ يَا ذَا الْجَلالِ وَالإِكْرَامِ ) فهذا نص صريح في المراد، وما يتخايل منه أنه يخالفه لم يقو قوته، [ أو لم تلزم دلالته على ما يخالفه ] فوجب اتباع هذا النص. واعلم أن المذكور في حديث عائشة هذا [ هو قولها لم يقعد إلا مقدار ما يقول، وذلك ] لا يستلزم سنية ذلك اللفظ بعينه، في دبر كل صلاة، إذا لم تقل إلا حتى يقول، أو [ إلى ] أن يقول، فيجوز كونه صلى الله عليه وسلم كان مرة يقوله، ومرة يقول غيره مما ذكرنا من قوله : « لا إِلَهَ إلا الله وحدَهُ لا شَريكَ لَهُ ». إلخ. ومقتضى العبارة حينئذ أن السنة: أنه يفصل بين الفرض والسنة بذكــر قدر ذلك، وذلك يكون تقريباً، فقد يزيد قليلاً وقد ينقص قليلاً، وقد يدرج وقد [ يرتل ]، فأما ما يزيــد مثل آية الكرسي، والعدد في التسبيحات ثلاثاً وثلاثين فينبغي استنان تأخيره عن السنة البتة، على أن ثبوت مواظبته لا لا لا لا لا أعلمه، بل الثابت عنه ندبه إلى ذلك، ولا يلزم من ندبه إلى شيء مواظبته عليه، وإلا لم يفرق حينئذ بين السنة والمندوب، وعندي قول الحلواني حكم آخر لا يعارض القولين، يفيد عدم سقوط السنة بقراءة الأوراد بين الفرض والسنة فقط انتهى.
تنبيه: قال في «البحر » : إذا تكلم بكلام كثير ، أو أكل أو شرب بين الفرض والسنة، نقص ثواب السنة، ولا تبطل هو الأصح، ولذا لو أخَّر السنة بعد الفرض، ثم أداها في آخر الوقت لا
Chapter on the description of remembrances after the obligatory prayer. Standing for the sunnah prayer immediately after the fard is disliked, but it is recommended to separate between them by the amount of saying: 'O Allah, You are Peace...' etc. Al-Kamal said from 'Sharh al-Shahid' and in 'al-Shafi': The Prophet, peace be upon him, when he said the salam, would pause the amount of saying: 'O Allah, You are Peace, and from You is Peace, and to You returns Peace; Blessed are You, O Possessor of Majesty and Honor.' Similarly from al-Baqqali. Al-Kamal said from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani that he said: There is no harm in reciting the litanies between the fard and the sunnah. He only said 'no harm' because the common usage of this phrase is for something whose opposite is better. So its meaning is that it is better not to recite litanies before the sunnah, but if one does, there is no harm. The sunnah is not invalidated by his recitation; rather if he prays it after the litanies, it occurs as a performed sunnah but not in the perfect manner. End of al-Kamal's words. And in 'al-Ikhtiyar': For every prayer that has a sunnah after it, it is disliked to sit after it and supplicate; rather one should occupy himself with the sunnah so that there is no separation between the sunnah and the obligatory prayer. From Aisha that the Prophet, peace be upon him, would sit for the amount of saying: 'O Allah, You are Peace...' then stand for the sunnah. End. That is, the separation with this is recommended. Also because a man who had caught the first takbir with the Prophet stood to pray an additional prayer, so Umar ibn al-Khattab took him by the shoulder and shook him and said: Sit, for the People of the Book were only destroyed because they had no separation between their prayers. The Prophet raised his eyes and said: 'Allah has guided through you, O son of al-Khattab.' Then al-Kamal said: Whoever claims a longer separation should bring evidence. And the many (hadiths) do not entail (that the litanies are to be recited immediately after fard). For he said: 'After every prayer, there is no god but Allah, alone, no partner...' and his saying to the poor Muhajirun: 'Glorify Allah, magnify Allah, praise Allah after every prayer thirty-three times' etc. This does not necessitate connecting these litanies to the fard; rather they are after the sunnah without occupying oneself with what is not from the appendages of prayer. So they are correctly after it. Then al-Kamal said: In summary, it has not been established from him (the Prophet) the separation with the litanies that are regularly recited in our time in the mosques, like reciting Ayat al-Kursi, tasbihat, and their sisters thirty-three times, etc. Rather, he recommended (nadaba) them. The established fact is that each of the sunan and the litanies has a relation of subordination to the fard. What is established from him of the litanies that are delayed after the sunnah and separate between it and the fard is what Muslim and al-Tirmidhi narrated from Aisha as we presented: When the Prophet said the salam, he would not sit except for the amount of saying: 'O Allah, You are Peace...' This is an explicit text regarding the intent. And what is imagined to contradict it does not have its strength [or its indication does not necessitate contradiction], so following this text is obligatory. Know that what is mentioned in this hadith of Aisha [is her saying: he did not sit except the amount of saying] does not necessitate that that exact wording is sunnah after every prayer, since she did not say 'until he says' or 'so that he says'. It is possible that the Prophet said it sometimes and said other times what we mentioned: 'There is no god but Allah, alone...' etc. The implication of the phrase then is that the sunnah is to separate between the fard and the sunnah with a dhikr of that amount. That is approximative: one may increase a little or decrease a little, or be brief or slow. As for what exceeds, like Ayat al-Kursi and the number of tasbihat thirty-three times, it is proper to delay them absolutely after the sunnah, for I do not know that he regularly practiced them, but what is established is his recommendation (nadb) of them. His recommendation of something does not entail his regular practice of it; otherwise there would be no distinction between sunnah and mandub. I have from al-Halwani another ruling that does not contradict the two sayings: it indicates that the sunnah is not invalidated by reciting litanies between fard and sunnah only. End.
Note: In 'al-Bahr': If one talks excessively, eats, or drinks between fard and sunnah, the reward of the sunnah is diminished, but it is not invalidated; this is the correct view. Therefore if one delays the sunnah after fard and then performs it later in the time, it is not...
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, discusses the proper sequence and timing of reciting adhkar (litanies) after the obligatory (fard) prayer and before the sunnah prayer. The passage is a detailed exposition of a ruling with proofs from hadith and scholarly opinions.

The ruling states: Standing immediately after the fard prayer to begin the sunnah prayer is disliked (makruh). It is recommended (mustahabb) to separate the two with a brief pause, approximately the time it takes to say: 'Allahumma anta al-salam, wa minka al-salam...' (O Allah, You are Peace, and from You is Peace...). This is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as narrated by Aisha. The author, al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam), cites this hadith and also the incident where Umar ibn al-Khattab stopped a man who stood immediately after the fard to pray an additional prayer, warning that the People of the Book were destroyed because they lacked separation between prayers. The Prophet approved of Umar's action.

The passage then addresses the common practice of reciting longer adhkar, such as Ayat al-Kursi and tasbihat (33x each), immediately after the fard. The correct understanding, as argued by al-Kamal, is that these should be recited after the sunnah prayer, not between fard and sunnah. The hadiths that mention 'after every prayer' (dubur kulli salat) refer to after the entire prayer sequence, which includes the sunnah. The sunnah prayer is considered a follow-up (tabi') to the fard, and adhkar are also subordinate. The practice of the Prophet was to only pause briefly for the short supplication before standing for the sunnah; longer adhkar were not part of his regular practice between fard and sunnah.

The author notes that saying 'la ba's' (no harm) by al-Halwani implies that it is better not to recite them, but if one does, it is permissible and the sunnah prayer is still valid, though its perfection is diminished. The note at the end from al-Bahr adds that talking, eating, or drinking excessively between fard and sunnah reduces the reward of the sunnah but does not invalidate it.

In summary, the passage teaches that the sunnah is to separate fard and sunnah with a short pause, and to delay lengthy adhkar until after the sunnah. This maintains the proper sequence and avoids detracting from the sunnah prayer.

Key Terms
مَسْئُون (mas'ūn): In this text, likely a corruption of 'makruh' (disliked). It refers to the dislike of standing immediately for the sunnah after the fard.
الأوراد (al-awrād): Plural of wird; litanies or supplications recited at specific times, such as after prayers.
السنة (al-sunnah): The sunnah prayer that is prayed after the fard prayer (e.g., sunnah of Fajr, Zuhr, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Aisha, how long did the Prophet ﷺ sit after the fard prayer before standing for the sunnah?
A) He sat for a long time reciting tasbihat.
B) He sat only for the time to say 'Allahumma anta al-salam...'.
C) He did not sit at all but immediately stood for the sunnah.
D) He sat for two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid.

Key Takeaway
Delay lengthy adhkar until after the sunnah; only a short pause is sunnah between fard and sunnah.

The Sunnah of Separation Between Fard and Sunnah
Clarifying the sunnah separator between fard and sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah dhikr between fard and sunnah prayers and distinguish it from recommended longer adhkar.

Core Idea
The sunnah is a short dhikr; longer adhkar are mandub and should be after the sunnah.

This passage clarifies a common confusion: what exactly is the sunnah to do between the fard and sunnah prayers? While many recite lengthy adhkar immediately after fard, the established sunnah from the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) is a brief remembrance. We will examine the hadith evidence and understand the proper sequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the separation between fard and sunnah with a dhikr. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah — a confirmed sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Aisha reported by Muslim and al-Tirmidhi: the Prophet would not sit after salam except to say 'Allahumma anta as-salam…'.
This hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لم يقعد إلا مقدار ما يقول' indicates that the only action between salam and standing for sunnah is this dhikr, making it the established separator.
The 'illa' (except) limits the sitting to this dhikr alone.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some hold that longer adhkar (like Ayat al-Kursi, 33 tasbihat) immediately after fard are also sunnah. The Hanafi position distinguishes: such longer recitations are mandub, not sunnah for that specific time.
The source says 'لم يثبت عنه' — it is not established that he did these regularly.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The explicit hadith text is preferred ('نص صريح'). The longer adhkar are recommended but should be delayed until after the sunnah prayer.
Al-Marghinani and the author of Imdad al-Fattah adopt this view.

(2) The end of every prayer, thirty-three and thirty-three, etc. Because it does not require connecting these remembrances to the obligatory prayer, but rather they are after the sunnah, without engaging in what is not part of the appendages of prayer, so it is correct that they are at its end. And his recommendation of something does not necessitate his constancy upon it; otherwise there would be no distinction between sunnah and mandub. In my view, the statement of al-Hilwani is another ruling that does not contradict the two statements: it indicates that the sunnah is not lost by reciting litanies between the obligatory and the sunnah only. Hence, if he delays the sunnah after the obligatory and then performs it at the end of the time, it is not
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the proper placement of adhkar (remembrances) after the fard (obligatory) prayer and before the sunnah prayer. It is an expansion on the matn of Nur al-Idah which states that it is sunnah to say tasbihat thirty-three times after every prayer. The commentator clarifies that the established sunnah from the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) is to separate the fard from the sunnah by a brief remembrance, specifically the words reported in the hadith of Aisha: 'Allahumma anta as-salam wa minka as-salam tabarakta ya dhal-jalali wal-ikram.' This hadith is explicit. The commentator addresses a common practice in his time of reciting longer passages like Ayat al-Kursi and tasbihat with a specific count of thirty-three between the fard and sunnah. He explains that while these are recommended (mandub), they are not the established sunnah for that specific slot. The sunnah is to recite a short dhikr as a separator, and then the sunnah prayer. The longer recitations should be delayed until after the sunnah. The passage also includes a note from al-Bahr about talking, eating, or drinking between the fard and sunnah: this diminishes the reward of the sunnah but does not invalidate it. The overall ruling is that the sunnah of separation is established by a specific hadith, and one should not confuse it with general recommendations.

Key Terms
دبر الصلاة (dubur al-salah): The time immediately after completing the fard prayer, before beginning the sunnah.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed; its omission is not sinful but is a loss of reward.
مندوب (mandub): A recommended act that is not consistently performed by the Prophet; its performance is rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sunnah between fard and sunnah is to recite a short dhikr; longer recitations are mandub and should be placed after the sunnah prayer.

The Imam's Sunnahs After Salam: Turning and Facing the People
Stating the sunnah actions for the imam after completing the fard salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts for the imam after the fard prayer and apply them to a scenario, distinguishing between sunnah and wajib.

Core Idea
After fard prayer, imam turns left, prays elsewhere, then faces the people – all sunnah.

When the imam completes the obligatory prayer, there are several recommended actions that carry spiritual reward and practical wisdom. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains what the imam should do after the salam, including turning to the left for the sunnah prayer and then facing the congregation. Understanding these sunnahs helps preserve the proper etiquettes of prayer and avoids confusion for later worshippers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Read the passage and list the actions recommended for the imam after the fard prayer. Determine the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah) for each.
The two main acts are: turning to the left to pray the sunnah elsewhere, and facing the people after the sunnah (or directly).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited as evidence for facing the people. Note that it is from Bukhari and Muslim.
The hadith states: 'When the Prophet prayed, he would turn to us with his face.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves recommendation, not obligation. The Prophet's action is followed as a sunnah.
There is no command (amr) indicating wujub; it is merely a habitual practice.
4
Note the ikhtilaf about direction
The passage mentions different opinions on which direction the imam should turn when facing the people. Identify the preferred view and its basis.
Turning to the right (facing the left of the congregation) is preferred due to a hadith in Muslim.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the author prefers one side over the other. The tarjih is based on a specific hadith about companions loving to be on the Prophet's right.
This shows that usul principles like tarjih using stronger evidence apply to sunnah acts as well.

And it is recommended for the imam after his salam to turn to his left, for the supererogatory prayer after the obligatory, and that he faces the people afterwards. And it is said: virtue is not specific to one direction over another, and that is the soundest view, but whatever is further from ostentation and more conducive to humility and sincerity is better. Thus in al-Nihaya. And it is recommended for the imam after his salam to turn to the right of the qibla, which is the opposite side from his left, meaning the left of the one facing the qibla, because the right of the opposite person is the left of the one facing the qibla. He turns to it for supererogatory prayer after the obligatory because the right has virtue. He should not pray in the place of the obligatory prayer, lest it be confusing for one who comes after the salam. It is also better for one other than the imam to move from his place, as it is narrated from Muhammad that he said: It is recommended also for the congregation to break the rows and disperse so that confusion is removed from the incoming person who sees the whole and the distant one from the imam, and to increase his witnesses, because it is narrated: 'The place of the salah will testify for him on the Day of Judgment.' Thus in al-Badai. And it is recommended that he faces the people afterwards, i.e., after the supererogatory if there is one, and likewise if there is no supererogatory after the obligatory, he faces the people with his face if he wishes, provided that there is no one praying in front of him, because of what is in the Sahihayn and others: 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed, he would turn to us with his face.' And if the imam wishes, he may turn to his left and make the qibla to his right, as when his facing would be towards a worshipper even in a distant row, and if he wishes, he may turn to his right and make the qibla to his left, and this is preferable because of what is in Muslim: 'When we prayed behind the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), we loved to be on his right so that he would turn to us with his face.' And if he wishes, he may go for his needs because he has completed his prayer. Allah says: 'Then when the prayer is concluded, disperse in the land' (Quran 62:10). The command is for permissibility. And its being in Jumu'ah does not negate it being in others, rather its clarification there is by way of indication. And in a prayer that has no supererogatory
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the recommended acts (mustahabat) for the imam after completing the fard prayer, based on the text of Nur al-Idah. The commentator expands on several points: First, it is recommended for the imam to turn to his left after the salam in order to perform the sunnah prayer. The reason given is that the right side is more virtuous, and by turning left he faces the right side of the qibla. He should not pray the sunnah in the exact spot where he prayed the fard, so as not to confuse someone who comes later. This also applies to the congregation: it is recommended that people move from their places and disperse, so that incoming worshippers do not mistake the spot for still being part of the fard. The hadith about the place of prayer testifying is mentioned as a reason for multiplying witnesses. Second, after the supererogatory prayer (or if there is none, immediately after the fard), it is recommended for the imam to face the people, turning his face towards them. He has the option to turn left or right, but turning to his right (meaning facing the left side of the people) is preferable based on a hadith in Muslim where the companions loved to be on the right side of the Prophet so that he would turn to them with his face. The imam may also leave for his own needs, as the Quranic verse indicates permissibility after prayer. The passage ends with a note about prayers that have no supererogatory, continuing from the previous topic.

Key Terms
يتحول إلى يساره (yatahawwalu ila yasarihi): The imam turns to his left after the salam, meaning he moves slightly to face the right side of the qibla.
يستقبل الناس (yastaqbil al-nas): The imam faces the congregation after completing the sunnah or fard, turning his face towards them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Remain in the same spot until everyone leaves
B) Turn to his left and not pray the sunnah in the same place
C) Immediately leave the mosque
D) Face the qibla and recite adhkar

Key Takeaway
The imam should turn to his left after salam and not pray the sunnah in the same spot, then face the congregation, with turning right (facing their left) being preferred.

Turning Left and Facing the Congregation: Post-Salaam Sunnah
Rulings on imam's post-salaam sunnah actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions of the imam after the obligatory prayer and identify when it is disliked to remain facing the qibla.

Core Idea
After prayer, turn left for sunnah, then face the people; remaining facing qibla in Fajr/Asr is disliked.

The imam's conduct immediately after the obligatory prayer follows specific sunnah practices. These actions ensure clarity for latecomers and reflect the Prophet's (ﷺ) example. This lesson covers the core rulings on turning left, performing nafl, and facing the congregation, including an important exception for Fajr and Asr prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
The text states two sunnah acts for the imam: first, turning to the left (relative to the qibla) to perform voluntary prayer, and second, after that (or if no nafl), facing the people with his face.
Turning left is defined as shifting to the side of the qibla that is on his left, which is the right side of the qibla.
2
Recognize the exception for Fajr and Asr
For prayers that have no supererogatory after them (Fajr and Asr), it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) for the imam to remain sitting in his place facing the qibla. This is due to the Prophet's consistent practice of not doing so.
The text cites the practice “kaan” (he used to) from Sahihain as evidence.
3
Understand the virtue and wisdom
The imam and congregation are encouraged to shift positions after prayer to avoid confusion for incoming worshippers and to gain the testimony of the prayer place on the Day of Judgment.
The text mentions that moving from the prayer spot is recommended for all, not just the imam.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
In practice, after the Fajr prayer, the imam should not sit facing the qibla; instead, he should turn left (or shift) and then face the congregation if he stays. This aligns with the sunnah and avoids the disliked action.

It is recommended for the imam after his salutation to turn to his left, to offer voluntary prayer after the obligatory, and thereafter to face the people. ... For the prayer that has no supererogatory after it, like Fajr and Asr, it is disliked for the imam to remain sitting in his place facing the qibla.

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah actions of the imam immediately after completing the obligatory prayer. The key ruling: the imam should turn left (from the perspective of the qibla) to perform nafl, then face the congregation. It also covers the virtue of performing sunnah at home except tarawih, and the recommendation for both imam and congregation to shift positions to avoid confusion for those entering later. الاستقبال (al-istiqbal): Facing the congregation after prayer.
